- **Power-set accessibility:** Functionally unlimited, with the standing caveat that access requires alter cooperation and alter cooperation is non-deterministic. The reality-warping high-tier alters that produced AoA and Age of X-Man are presumed still present and still triggerable under sufficient stress.

**Behavioral micro-pattern, present-state, inferred from latest appearances.**

- *Sleep:* Almost certainly disordered. The astral-plane interior of subject does not switch off; alters are most active during host sleep across every era depicted. He likely sleeps in short, defended intervals, frequently in non-domestic environments (the wandering pattern precludes bed-routine). When depicted asleep across the canon, he is shown in seated or curled postures, rarely supine — a body that does not trust unconsciousness.
- *Eating:* Sparse. The thin, undernourished phenotype has been consistent across artists for forty years. Inference: eating is interrupted by alter activity, by mission urgency, and by the depressive substrate; he eats when reminded, not when hungry.
- *Speech, baseline:* The ironized-British register when the host is in front and a regulator (Ruth, or a trusted peer) is nearby. The sermonic-declarative register when alone or stressed. Mid-sentence shifts in pronoun, accent, or vocabulary when alters intrude — the file should treat any observed accent-shift as a *real-time alter-switching indicator*, not a stylistic choice.
- *Hair:* The vertical pillar remains. It rises with psionic discharge and partially flattens during the rare integrated-rest periods. This is the most reliable external biomarker of internal state available to an observer. A surveillance asset who can see the hairline can read the mind-weather.
- *Gait:* Long-strided, slightly forward-canted, hands often loose at sides — a body that has learned not to hold tension in the limbs because tension in the limbs invites the kinesthetic alters to take over. The looseness is not relaxation; it is *defense against somatic seizure by an internal third party*.
- *Hands:* Frequently in subtle motion when speaking — small gestures that, across artists, have consistently been drawn as if conducting or counting. The inference is that subject uses fine-motor activity as a grounding technique, of the sort trauma clinicians actively teach to dissociative patients. He may have learned this from Merzah; he may have invented it.
- *Eyes:* Heterochromic in some depictions, monochrome in others; the inconsistency across artists is, the file submits, *itself canonical* — the eye color is unstable because the self looking out is unstable. When the host is forward, the eyes are darker and more focused; when an alter is surfacing, the rendering brightens or shifts. A trained observer should learn to read the eye-state.
- *Mirrors and reflective surfaces:* Avoided. This is consistent across the Spurrier run and inferable from posture in later appearances — subject orients to rooms with his back to reflective surfaces or moves through them quickly. The pressure-point analysis in §5 of the analytical basis identified mirrors as destabilizing; behavior conforms.

**Current psychiatric state, inferred.**

The DID is uncontained. The C-PTSD is unresolved and has been compounded by the Krakoan-era exclusion-from-resurrection and the betrayal-by-father motif of the Onslaught/X-Manhunt arc. The vulnerable-narcissistic axis is tilted further toward grandiosity than at most prior points, but the conscience remains active and the suicidal-ideation pole (self-erasure as love-gesture) has not, on present evidence, reactivated. The depressive substrate is presumably elevated by the loss of Krakoa as a holding environment and by the diffusion of the mutant community he was, however imperfectly, part of.

The single most stabilizing variable in his current life is the availability of Ruth Aldine. The single most destabilizing variable is the unresolved status of Charles Xavier — alive, imprisoned, accountable, reachable. The father-object has, for the first time in canon, transitioned from idealized-absent to *devalued-present-and-confined*, which is a configuration the subject's psyche has never had to metabolize before. Future-state projection should weight this heavily.

---

## 4.5 — How He Got Here: The Through-Line Compressed

Read across the full forty-year record, the path from the embassy in Paris to the present diasporic state is *a single behavior repeated at increasing scales*:

1. **Overwhelm.** An unbearable affect or event lands on a self that cannot hold it.
2. **Split.** The affect is encapsulated in a new alter, which gains the corresponding power.
3. **Contain.** An external apparatus (Moira, helmet, headband, Merzah, self-erasure, Krakoan distance) is acquired to manage the population.
4. **Fail.** The apparatus, being external to the splitting mechanism itself, cannot prevent the next split.
5. **Escalate.** The next overwhelm produces a more dangerous alter and demands a larger apparatus.

Subject is, at present, between steps 4 and 5. The Krakoan apparatus has failed. The next overwhelm has not yet landed in published canon. The shape of the apparatus he will reach for after it lands will tell the file more about his trajectory than any therapeutic intervention could.

---

## 4.6 — Where He Is Now: Summary Disposition

A thin, vertical-haired man of middle age and unstable body-image, walking unaffiliated through a diasporic mutant landscape, carrying inside his skull a population larger than most cities and a moral conscience that has, against every structural pressure, refused to switch off. He has erased himself once for love and chosen not to kill his father once for ethics. He is regulated, when at all, by one woman who can see what he cannot. He is excluded by infrastructure from the death-and-return cycle that defines his people. He is, on the present evidence, still trying to get well.

The file's working assessment is that he will continue to try, that he will continue to fail at the scale his powers make available, and that the next time he succeeds at anything — heroism, integration, or annihilation — it will be *very large*.

— END SECTION —


## Medical History

# MEDICAL HISTORY — SUBJECT: DAVID CHARLES HALLER

*Compiled longitudinally from the full publication record. This file treats psionic phenomena as somatic events where they manifest somatically; treats device-mediated interventions as iatrogenic regardless of consent; and treats reality-edits affecting the subject's body as injuries even when retroactively undone, because the body's memory of them — and the alters' — does not always follow the retcon.*

---

## I. CONSTITUTIONAL BASELINE

**Sex/Phenotype.** Male, white, of Ashkenazi-Jewish ancestry (maternal — Gabrielle Haller, Holocaust survivor) and Anglo-American (paternal — Charles Xavier). Height in the median adult-male range (approx. 5'10"–6'0" across artists; treat as ~178 cm working figure). Weight chronically low for stature; subject reads as undernourished or recently-undernourished even in periods of stable housing, with visible clavicular and orbital prominence, narrow wrists, narrow shoulders relative to frame. Musculature minimal; he is not athletic, has never been athletic, and has no record of physical training apart from the Himalayan monastic interval, which was disciplinary rather than developmental.

**Hair.** The single most reliable somatic biomarker on file. The vertical, fixed-upright configuration is *not* styled; it is *not* gelled; it does not lay flat in water, in sleep, or under helmets, and partial-flatten observations are reliably correlated with low-arousal dissociative or post-ictal-equivalent states. Working hypothesis: chronic low-grade electrostatic and psionic field around the cranium produces continuous follicular piloerection — i.e., he is in a permanent, mild, autonomic discharge state. The hair is therefore a real-time arousal monitor visible from across a room. Color: dark brown to black, no premature greying logged through any era, despite stress loading that should produce it. (Inference: cellular-level alters or auto-corrective psionics maintain phenotype against insult.)

**Eyes.** Pale — variously rendered grey, blue, hazel; the relevant clinical fact is the *fixity* of gaze when an alter is forward and the *unfocused middle-distance* default of the host self. Subject's host-state eye contact is notoriously poor; he tracks shoulders, sleeves, and his own hands.

**Skin.** Pallor consistent with indoor life, low sun exposure across most of the file, with one Himalayan interval that did not tan him appreciably. No tattoos in any baseline rendering. No piercings. Scarring discussed below.

**Dentition.** Unremarkable, well-cared-for in childhood (consistent with diplomatic-class maternal household, Paris/Haifa), neglected through institutional periods (Muir adolescence) with measurable plaque and gingivitis inference, restored episodically. Subject grinds his teeth in sleep — bruxism logged via Ruth Aldine's reported observation in the Spurrier interval.

---

## II. PERINATAL AND DEVELOPMENTAL

**Conception and gestation.** Product of the Xavier–Haller relationship in Haifa. Gestation appears to have been uncomplicated; Gabrielle was clinically recovered from her own amnesia/depressive aftermath at the time. No record of prenatal substance exposure. No record of obstetric intervention; delivery apparently routine.

**Infancy and early childhood.** Achieved milestones on or near schedule. There is no canonical record of childhood febrile illness, parasitic infection, or vaccine reaction; given diplomatic-cohort medical access in Israel and France, presume full immunization through standard schedule of the period (BCG, DPT, OPV, MMR by the mid-1970s schedule).

**Indicators of latent mutancy pre-onset.** Retrospective observations in flashback (New Mutants #26–28 and the Legacy vol. 2 framing) suggest subclinical telepathic leakage from early childhood: night terrors with bilateral content (the child's terror and an adult-coded terror, distinguishable in retrospect as receptive telepathy), preference for solitary play, atypical fluency in adults' unspoken emotions. Not pathologized at the time.

---

## III. THE INDEX EVENT (AGE ~8–10)

**Mechanism.** Terrorist assault on the Israeli embassy/residence. Subject witnesses Daniel Shomron — stepfather and the only functional paternal figure present in his life — killed at close range. Subject's psionic capacity manifests explosively, mind-burning the assailants, and in the same psychic act *absorbs* the dying consciousness of the lead attacker, Jemail Karami, into his own mind.

**Concurrent somatic findings (inferred from clinical pattern of comparable acute-onset psionic events documented elsewhere in the X-canon).**
- Probable hyperthermia (psionic discharge of that magnitude produces measurable febrile spike).
- Spontaneous epistaxis.
- Likely brief loss of consciousness.
- Post-ictal-equivalent confusion lasting hours to days.
- Almost certainly some degree of involuntary urination at peak — standard for severe autonomic storm in a prepubertal child, and consistent with the depth of shame the host self carries about this event in adult flashback.

**Acute neurological consequence.** The dissociative response was simultaneous with the psionic discharge; subject did not become Jemail-and-David in sequence but in superposition. There is no recoverable "before split" narrative memory of the event in the host self. Memory of the event is held by Karami.

**Psychological impact.** This is the foundational wound. Every diagnostic feature documented in subsequent decades traces, by chain of inference, back to this hour. The mechanism *worked* — it prevented total ego collapse — and therefore became the prototype for every subsequent psychic crisis. The subject is, in effect, a patient whose adaptive response to overwhelming trauma was so successful at age nine that he has never been able to stop using it.

---

## IV. CATATONIC PERIOD (MUIR ISLAND, EARLY ADOLESCENCE, NEW MUTANTS #26–28)

**Presentation.** Multi-year dissociative catatonia under Moira MacTaggert's care. Periods of waxy flexibility logged; periods of frank unresponsiveness; periods of mute self-care. Internal life intensely active (per Sienkiewicz-rendered astral cartography); external life flat.

**Nutritional state.** Maintained by assisted feeding through significant intervals. The chronically thin adult frame is in part a legacy of this period — adolescent growth phases under marginal caloric and protein intake produce permanent reduction in adult musculature and bone density. There is reasonable inference of mild osteopenia at adult baseline.

**Skin integrity.** Pressure-area inference: subject must have required active turning regimens at the catatonic peak; absence of visible decubitus scarring in adult renderings suggests competent nursing rather than absence of risk.

**Muscular.** Disuse atrophy through the catatonic interval; partial reconstitution on emergence but never to age-matched norm. Gait at adult baseline is loose, slightly shuffling at fatigue, occasionally rigid when a more disciplined alter is forward.

**Endocrine/pubertal.** Puberty occurred *during* catatonia, with no normal social scaffolding of identity formation. This is consequential: the adolescent task of integrating an emergent sexual self into the ego was, for this subject, not merely deferred but *outsourced* — the sexuality lives in alters (Jack Wayne's hypermasculine swagger; Cyndi's pyrokinetic adolescent-girl rage) because the host self never had the developmental opportunity to claim it. This is a clinically rare but coherent etiology and explains the durable asexual presentation of the host across the entire adult record.

**Psychological impact.** Subject emerged into adult function having missed adolescence as a lived event. He is, throughout the adult file, a man performing the developmental tasks of fifteen at ages thirty and forty. The Spurrier-era costume design has the awkward earnestness of a teenager's first attempt at self-presentation, because in self-formation time it *is*.

---

## V. EMERGENCE AND ALTER-MEDIATED FUNCTIONING (LATE 1980s, CLAREMONT)

**Acute psionic incidents** logged through this interval include uncontrolled telekinetic discharges (Jack Wayne–fronted), pyrokinetic ignitions (Cyndi-fronted, multiple environmental fires of variable scale), and the New Mutants' transit into his mindscape — the latter a category of event with no clinical analogue; treat as a successful but unrepeated experimental intervention.

**Somatic markers of switching, documented.** Voice pitch and timbre alteration (Cyndi's voice is rendered as a higher, sharper register; Jack's as a chest-toned drawl). Postural shifts: host self stands hip-shifted, shoulders forward, hands often clasped or hidden in sleeves; Jack squares the shoulders, drops the weight to the back foot, occupies space; Cyndi tilts the chin up, locks the hips, deploys the hands aggressively. Facial musculature changes are real and observer-confirmed; subject's resting face is asymmetric across alters in a way that genuinely confuses facial-recognition pattern-matching. Apparent secondary sex characteristics (Cyndi as a girl) are best understood as low-intensity psionic somatic projection rather than literal morphology; observers perceive them as real, and so does the subject's own proprioceptive system, which is the clinically relevant fact.

**Injuries logged through this period.** Numerous minor — burns to hands and forearms during pyrokinetic episodes (Cyndi does not protect the body she's borrowing); abrasions and contusions from telekinetic blowback; one notable closed head injury inferred from a Muir-era incident, untreated formally, partial amnesia following.

---

## VI. THE LEGION QUEST AND AGE OF APOCALYPSE INTERVAL (1995)

**Pre-event status.** Lucid by his own measure; grandiose by external measure. No documented prodromal somatic decline. The decision to attempt the Magneto assassination was made over weeks, was rehearsed in plan, and was executed with cognitive clarity. This is not a manic or psychotic episode; it is a *coherent* episode, which is part of why it is so much more frightening than the dissociative ones.

**Event somatics.** Temporal translocation: there is no record of subject having survived chronon-displacement before; the somatic cost is not documented but should be presumed nontrivial (comparable subjects in the canon report nausea, vertigo, retrograde memory disturbance, and a transient drop in psionic ceiling). Psi-blade discharge at lethal vector against Xavier produced the secondary catastrophe of paternal homicide and primary timeline collapse.

**Bodily fate.** Subject was *erased from existence* in the timeline reset that followed. This is not a death; it is an ontological deletion with retroactive restoration. There is no equivalent in clinical medicine. The psychological consequence is, however, real and persistent: subject knows, at the level of declarative memory, that he killed his father and that his existence was undone as the cost. The body that walks around after his resurrection carries the *memory* of having been unmade. This is its own injury and it does not heal.

---

## VII. POST-RESURRECTION DEVICE-MEDIATED INTERVAL (MACKIE, CAREY)

**The first neural regulator.** Subject is fitted, post-return, with a Moira-derived neural device whose function is to compartmentalize alters into summonable discrete capacities. Mechanism likely involves cortical and limbic suppression with cued release. Clinically: this is psychosurgery by appliance. Side effects logged or inferable include flattened affect during stable periods, sleep architecture disruption (the alters are not gone, they are *contained*, which is a different homeostatic load), and rebound flooding on device failure.

**The Stryfe-derived headband (Carey, X-Men: Legacy).** Higher-fidelity version of the same intervention. Allowed selective alter-summoning for combat tasking — i.e., subject became, briefly, his own weapons platform. The headband is iatrogenic in the strict sense: it produced a functional improvement at the cost of training the subject to experience himself as a *system to be operated* rather than a person. The relief was real; the cost was that the relief was conditional on the device, and on the institutional structure around it. He learned, again, that he is safe only when restrained.

**Age of X event (Legacy #245–247).** Unconsciously generated pocket reality with a full false-identity cast for the X-Men, constructed to suppress a single violent alter. This is a psychiatric episode of cosmological scale; somatically, subject was physically inert during construction, with massive sustained psionic discharge inferable from environmental phenomena. Post-event: profound exhaustion, weight loss, weeks of recovery, and a new layer of guilt about having conscripted his closest relationships into his own containment architecture.

---

## VIII. HIMALAYAN MONASTIC INTERVAL (SPURRIER, X-MEN LEGACY VOL. 2)

**Training under Merzah the Mystic.** Subject internalized the carceral function — built, by disciplined meditation, a *literal mental prison* for his alters. This is the most thorough self-led psychiatric intervention in the file and also, structurally, the most disturbing: the patient agreed that the right model of his own mind was a penal one, and built it.

**Somatic concomitants of the training year.**
- Slight weight gain on monastic diet (the only documented period of stable nutrition in his adult life).
- Improved sleep, by Ruth's later reportage.
- Minor frostbite to the digits, healed without sequela.
- A measurable reduction in baseline hair-verticality on emergence — i.e., the autonomic discharge was, briefly, lower. This is the most objective evidence on file that the training worked at the substrate level.

**Costume adoption.** Self-designed, asymmetric, theatrically severe. Clinically: the act of *dressing as the hero* is part of the containment apparatus. He is using uniform-as-ego, the way trauma patients sometimes use a wedding ring or a service dog vest — an external object that says *this is who I am today.*

**Relationship with Ruth Aldine (Blindfold).** The only sustained mutual adult attachment in the file. Measurable functional improvement during the relationship: fewer breakthrough alter incidents, more coherent first-person speech, reduced grandiosity. Ruth functions as an external regulatory object, which is both the healthiest he has been and a vulnerability — the regulation is conditional on her presence.

**Terminal act of the arc.** Foreseeing his own future as a destroyer, subject elects to erase himself from reality a second time. Somatically: full ontological self-deletion, willed. Psychologically: this is the same act as the Magneto attempt — *I will remove the dangerous thing so the father's dream survives* — except the dangerous thing has been correctly identified as himself. There is a real, terrible clinical progress hidden in that revision.

---

## IX. SUBSEQUENT INTERVAL (POST-SPURRIER)

Less coherent across writers; the consistent through-line: oscillation between savior-presentation and obliteration-presentation, with the device/discipline/relationship triad of regulation always failing in the same shape. Documented physical insults across this period are numerous but minor relative to the cosmological scale of the psychic events; the body remains the same thin, vertical-haired, asymmetric-faced vehicle through which a crowd intermittently drives.

---

## X. SUBSTANCES

**Alcohol.** No record of regular use. The host self does not drink; Jack Wayne has been observed drinking, which is its own clinical curiosity — alter-specific intoxication is canonically possible in DID and behaviorally consistent here. Tolerance and metabolism are the body's; intent and craving are the alter's.

**Tobacco.** No record. (Hair would not stand the way it does on a sustained smoker; field is wrong.)

**Recreational drugs.** No record of use by the host. Inferable risk of alter-mediated experimentation; no canonical incident.

**Prescription psychotropics.** Likely trialed in the Muir period under MacTaggert; specifics not recorded. Inference of poor response: the underlying pathology is not a neurotransmitter-imbalance pathology in the receptor-bound sense, and the device interventions superseded pharmacology.

**Caffeine.** Plausible mild dependence in the post-Muir adult intervals; non-clinical.

---

## XI. SURGICAL / PROCEDURAL

No conventional surgery on record. Multiple device implantations and applications as above; treated for clinical purposes as procedural interventions even when externally worn, because the appliance-self interface is sustained and the removal is itself a procedure with sequelae.

---

## XII. DISABILITIES

The subject meets a working definition of psychiatric disability across most of the adult record, with intervals of remission corresponding to (a) device function, (b) monastic discipline, (c) sustained mutual attachment. He has at no point been considered for and would not benefit from accommodation in the ordinary employment sense; the relevant accommodations are at the scale of *containment of an omega-class mutant in dissociative crisis* and are matters for institutions, not workplaces.

---

## XIII. PROGNOSTIC NOTE

The body is durable, low-baseline, undertrained, and chronically slightly underfed. It has survived everything done to it, including its own deletion, twice. The pathology is over-learned, structurally reinforced by the reward of superhuman capability, and has resisted every modality tried against it — pharmacological, device-mediated, monastic-disciplinary, relational. The one variable that produces measurable improvement, repeatedly, is a single sustained mutual attachment functioning as external regulatory object. This is the most important finding in the medical file and the one most often overlooked by interveners reaching for the next appliance: *the headband never worked as well as Ruth did.* Any future treatment plan that does not begin from that finding will fail in the same way every prior plan has failed, and the subject — who is, beneath everything, a patient who has never stopped trying to get well — will pay the cost again.

— END SECTION —


## Somatic Atlas

# SOMATIC ATLAS — SUBJECT: DAVID CHARLES HALLER

*The body as the dossier the subject himself cannot read. What follows is the cumulative observational record: gait, posture, microexpression, autonomic discharge, sleep, ingestion, sexuality, the small constant betrayals of skin and breath. Where the data shifts by state — baseline, stress, threat, intimacy, alter-incursion — those shifts are mapped. Each alter occupies the body differently; the body is therefore not one body but a frequency-band of bodies sharing a chassis.*

---

## 1. THE STANDING BODY — STRUCTURE, BUILD, AND BASELINE

Subject presents as a thin, long-limbed Caucasian male, height in the 5'10"–6'0" range across canonical depictions, weight chronically low for frame — somewhere between 145 and 160 lbs, lower in periods of acute decompensation. Musculature is undeveloped in the conventional sense; the body has the look of someone who has been ill more often than fed, with the slightly concave chest and forward-rolled shoulders of a long-term inpatient. Skin is pale to the point of luminous, with the bluish under-eye discoloration of chronic sleep debt and the fine reddened capillary patterning across the cheekbones that comes with autonomic instability. Hands are long, fingers thin, knuckles slightly enlarged — a tell of repeated subconscious clenching during sleep, which the subject does not consciously recall.

The single most identifiable somatic signature is the hair. Vertical, dense, dark, standing six to ten inches above the scalp at full discharge. It does not lie flat under any conditions observed in the file — not after washing, not under pressure, not in sleep. Static charge measured in close passes runs continuously elevated; small fibers, dust, and lint cling to it disproportionately. The hair functions as an external EEG: its volume and verticality correlate near-linearly with psionic background activity. At extreme baseline calm (rare, observed only in deep meditation under Merzah's instruction) the hair partially settles, falling forward across the brow in a way that subject himself appears not to recognize on himself. Under stress it rises and gains a faint corona of visible discharge; under alter-incursion individual strands have been observed to lift independently of gravity.

The face is narrow, long-jawed, with a wide mouth that defaults to slight asymmetry — the right corner habitually lower than the left, suggesting either old facial-nerve insult or, more likely, a long-trained social mask that has set in the musculature. Eyes are pale, large, set deep; pupillary reactivity is *not normal* — dilation persists under bright stimulus longer than expected, and during alter-switching the pupils have been documented to dilate fully within 200ms regardless of ambient light, returning to a different baseline diameter once the new alter is seated. The iris itself does not change color, but the *quality* of the gaze does: this is one of the most reliable observational tells for state-shift, and trained handlers (Moira, later Ruth) report being able to identify which alter is present from the eyes alone within roughly two seconds of contact.

---

## 2. POSTURE AND GAIT — THE INHABITED CHASSIS

**Host baseline posture.** Slightly stooped, weight forward over the toes, shoulders rolled in toward the sternum, head carried slightly ahead of the spine. The posture of a tall man trying to make himself smaller — and of an inpatient who has spent years being approached rather than approaching. Hands tend toward the pockets or, when no pockets are available, toward the opposite elbow, producing the self-hugging brace that is one of his signatures at rest. Standing still, he shifts weight foot-to-foot at intervals of roughly 8–14 seconds, more frequent under observation, suggesting both proprioceptive instability and chronic mild akathisia.

**Host gait.** Loose-jointed, slightly shuffling, longer stride on the right than the left by a measurable margin (probably old, asymmetric, no documented injury — likely a consequence of the years of catatonic immobility followed by un-rehabilitated reactivation). Arm swing is dampened on both sides; the left arm in particular tends to ride against the body. He does not look down at his feet but neither does he scan; gaze lands at roughly 4–6 meters ahead, mid-height. Tempo is slow at baseline (cadence around 95–105 steps/minute), accelerating dramatically under intrusive ideation.

**Alter-shifted gait and posture.** The Jack Wayne–coded swagger: weight shifts to the heels, shoulders square and pull back, chest opens, chin lifts, stride lengthens and slows, arm-swing reasserts with exaggerated lateral motion; hands hang open rather than pocketed. The Cyndi-coded carriage: weight pitches forward onto the balls of the feet, knees soften, hips drop into a loose hinge, head cocks to one side, hands either fist or rake through the hair; gait becomes bouncing, cadence spikes near 130 spm. The Karami-coded posture is the closest to a *centered* posture observable in the chassis: feet at hip width, weight evenly distributed, shoulders back without theatricality, hands clasped loosely behind — the carriage of a man who once had military or paramilitary training and never lost it. The simple presence or absence of that even weight-distribution is, for trained observers, a reliable triage marker.

Under destructive-alter incursion (the Legion-coded class), the body locks: weight equalizes, shoulders drop, the head levels and the face stills. The most dangerous state in the body is also the most outwardly *quiet* state — and this is critical to flag, because the lay-intuition that an explosive alter would announce itself with agitation is wrong. Stillness in this chassis is a threat indicator, not a comfort indicator.

---

## 3. THE FACE — MICROEXPRESSION CATALOGUE

**Resting face.** Subject does not have a stable resting face. The host's default is a mild, slightly apologetic almost-smile, lips closed, eyebrows neutral, eyes downcast at roughly 10–20 degrees below horizontal. This is the inpatient's face: non-threatening, slightly pleading, designed across years to deflect the attention of doctors and authority figures. It is not a happy face. It is a face that has learned not to cost anyone anything.

**Tells, host:** A two-beat blink-and-look-away when complimented. A small grimace at the right corner of the mouth (the lower corner) when his father's name is mentioned, suppressed so quickly that most observers miss it — this is among the most consistent and diagnostic facial tells in the entire record. A slight forward jut of the lower jaw, momentary, when he is about to argue against a course of action he intends to follow anyway. Eyebrows rise asymmetrically (left higher) when an alter is pushing for surface; this is *involuntary* and precedes alter-emergence by seconds to minutes.

**Tells, intrusive activity:** Eyes track to the left-and-down toward unseen interlocutors. Lips move minutely as if subvocalizing. Brief, dissociated half-smiles or grimaces uncorrelated with conversation. A sudden, small headshake — not a "no" but a clearing gesture, performed as if dislodging an insect.

**Tells, alter-emergence prodrome:** Pupillary dilation as noted. A slow exhale through the nose. Closing of the eyes for one to three seconds. On opening: the muscles of the face have *redistributed*. The Jack alter wears a tighter mouth and a fuller-fronted jaw; the Cyndi alter loosens the entire lower face and bites at the lower lip; the Karami alter softens the eyes and steadies the brow. When the body is the host's again, the asymmetric apologetic smile returns within a breath. Subject does not realize the smile has been gone.

---

## 4. HANDS — THE MOST EXPRESSIVE ORGAN

The hands carry the highest information density in this body. Long-fingered, thin, slightly tremulous at rest (a fine tremor at roughly 8–10 Hz, more pronounced in the dominant right; consistent with either chronic anxiety, long-term low-dose neuroleptic exposure, or the constant background of psionic discharge — likely all three). Nails are kept short but not manicured; cuticles show evidence of habitual picking, especially the right thumb against the side of the right index.

**Stereotyped gestures, host:** Pressing the heels of both palms against the closed eyes for three to ten seconds. Carding fingers through the standing hair, which neither smooths nor disturbs it but which the subject performs roughly twenty to forty times per waking hour under any stress above baseline. Pinching the bridge of the nose. Counting along the fingertips of one hand with the thumb of the same hand — index, middle, ring, little, ring, middle, index — in a four-then-reverse-three pattern that appears to be self-generated and not taught; this is a self-soothing routine performed especially in waiting rooms, debriefs, and any setting where he expects to be evaluated.

**Hand-position by alter:** Host keeps hands pocketed or wrapped at opposite elbow. Jack-coded states open the hands at the sides, palms slightly forward, fingers spread — a readied, performative posture. Cyndi-coded states ball the hands or rake them through hair in repeated downward strokes. Karami-coded states clasp loosely at the small of the back or fold at the lap. The reality-warping alters tend to extend a single hand, fingers slightly curled — the body knows the gesture though the host does not.

**Tremor and discharge.** Under genuine threat the fine tremor coarsens into a visible shake, and small static phenomena appear at the fingertips: a faint blue-edged corona, the lifting of nearby hair on observers, occasional involuntary discharge into nearby metals. He has been documented, repeatedly, to short out wristwatches, phones, and field equipment within a 1–2 meter radius during moderate-stress interviews. He does not know he is doing it.

---

## 5. VOICE, BREATH, AND VOCAL SIGNATURE

**Host voice.** Mid-tenor, soft at baseline, slightly hesitant, with a faint mid-Atlantic blur — the residue of a Paris-Israel-UK-US developmental trajectory. He under-projects; in groups he must be asked to repeat himself within the first minute roughly half the time. Speech is *not* pressured; pacing is slow to moderate, with the long internal pauses of someone consulting another voice before answering. The pauses are diagnostic: a one-to-three second silence before answering a personal question is host-normal, and indicates internal consultation, not evasion.

**Breath, host:** Shallow, predominantly thoracic, rate elevated at baseline (16–20 breaths/min resting), prone to held breaths of 10–20 seconds under cognitive load, with audible compensatory sigh at release. The sigh is performed five to twelve times per hour and is one of the most reliable handler-observable affect signals.

**Voice, alter-shifted.** The Jack alter speaks lower (drops roughly a full third in fundamental frequency), louder, with American-inflected English, longer vowels, and idiomatic patterns that the host does not use ("buddy," "sweetheart," cursing). The Cyndi alter raises pitch, accelerates tempo by roughly 30–50%, uses staccato consonants, laughs in short bursts, and uses British punkish slang. The Karami alter speaks in the host's range but more steadily, in measured cadences, often with formal grammar and the occasional Arabic loan word; the accent is recognizably Levantine. These shifts can occur mid-sentence. Pronoun use can shift in the same sentence: the host saying "I" while the surfacing alter completes with "we," then the body continuing in third person about the host as "him" — the linguistic surface fissures along the same fault lines as the psyche.

Linguistic analysts in the file note also: subject's host has a vocabulary tic of beginning self-referential sentences with "I'm trying to —" rather than "I —." This frames the self as an effortful project rather than an actor, and recurs across two decades of recorded speech.

---

## 6. SLEEP ARCHITECTURE

Subject's sleep is profoundly disordered and has been since adolescence.

**Sleep latency** runs long (45–90 minutes typical), with subject lying supine, eyes open or partially closed, hands folded across the sternum — the posture of someone trying to occupy as little space in the bed as possible. He cannot fall asleep with a wall to his back; preference is for the bed against the room's longest sightline, door visible.

**Architecture.** Polysomnography (inferred from behavioral observation; Muir Island had instrumentation, the X-Mansion did not) shows fragmented sleep with frequent micro-awakenings, reduced slow-wave sleep, and abnormally long, vivid REM episodes. REM behavior disorder features are present: vocalization during REM is constant — full sentences, sometimes in multiple voices, sometimes in languages the host does not speak (Hebrew, Arabic, French phrases that test as Karami-source). Limb movement is not violent but is continuous; the right hand in particular performs the four-then-three counting pattern in sleep.

**Awakenings.** Subject wakes an average of four to seven times per night. The first reaction on waking is to scan the room — gaze travels ceiling-to-floor along the far wall, then to the door, then to his own hands. He checks his hands every time he wakes. The check takes one to two seconds and consists of opening and closing each, then turning the palms up. The function appears to be confirming both that the body is his and that nothing in it is currently on fire. The behavior is unbroken across at least three decades of recorded life.

**Dreams.** Subject describes dreams reluctantly and inconsistently, but the available content includes: the embassy attack, recurrent across all eras; an empty corridor with a door at the end he cannot open; his father turning away; a featureless plain with a small figure of himself standing on it. He does not dream of Ruth; this is notable and was noted by him in one Spurrier-era exchange. Subject's most peaceful sleep is documented as occurring in physical proximity to Ruth, in a bed not his, in a room he does not consider his — the conditions of *visiting* appear to produce the only restorative sleep he reliably gets.

---

## 7. INGESTION AND ORAL HABITS

**Eating.** Subject eats erratically, in small amounts, with long gaps. He does not appear to register hunger reliably and must often be told to eat — a feature consistent with both long institutionalization and chronic dissociative dampening of interoception. Preferences trend toward bland, soft foods (rice, bread, eggs) and away from foods requiring elaborate preparation or social ritual. He eats *fast* when he eats, head slightly down, non-dominant hand under the table or in his lap. He does not generally eat in front of strangers; he will accept tea and not drink it.

**Tea/coffee.** Tea is the constant: strong, black, often left to go cold while held in both hands as a hand-warmer rather than a beverage. The cup is a regulatory object; he can hold it for the entire duration of a difficult conversation and never drink. Coffee is associated with Jack-alter periods and consumed in quantity then; the host does not like coffee.

**Smoking.** Cigarettes are a Jack-alter behavior, not a host behavior. When Jack is active or near-surface, the body will smoke — left-handed, deeply, holding the cigarette between thumb and index. The host does not smoke and on regaining the body will often discover an unfamiliar pack, look at it for a long moment, and put it down without comment. He does not throw them away.

**Alcohol.** Avoided by the host (correctly, given the dissociative substrate). When Jack surfaces in social settings, alcohol is consumed; the host has on multiple occasions awakened with hangovers he did not earn.

**Oral tics.** Lip-biting (Cyndi-coded). Inside-of-cheek chewing along the right molar line (host, under stress; has produced visible mucosal callus in dental records inferred from Muir-era files). Pressing the tongue against the back of the upper incisors during silence — a stilling behavior, observed in roughly 40% of recorded interview silences over three seconds.

---

## 8. SEXUALITY AND INTIMACY

This is the most sparsely documented domain in the file, by canon and by the subject's own avoidance, but enough is observable to map.

**Host sexuality.** Attenuated. The host does not appear to experience strong genital drive at baseline; affectional/attachment drive is overwhelming, but it does not route through the somatic-sexual channel reliably. This is consistent with both severe early trauma and with the structural-dissociative compartmentalization of bodily appetites into other alters. The host's intimacy repertoire is touch-shy at first contact, then — once trust is established — touch-hungry in a non-sexual, comfort-seeking register: hand-holding, shoulder-leaning, sleeping in physical contact without sexual initiation.

**With Ruth Aldine.** Subject is the most *somatically open* on record. He permits and seeks contact: she touches his face and he does not flinch; he sleeps with his back to her, which he does with no one else. Verbal exchanges in the Spurrier run are explicit that the relationship is consummated; the somatic carriage in those periods loosens measurably — shoulders drop, gait slows but lengthens, the hair settles fractionally, the resting half-smile becomes a fuller smile that uses both sides of the mouth. The relationship is also where the *trembling* drops out, intermittently, for hours at a time. This is, clinically, the closest the body comes to baseline calm in the entire record.

**Alter sexuality.** Jack-coded states are predatorily heterosexual, performative, and the body in that state initiates contact the host would not. Cyndi-coded states are flirtatious, provocative, female-coded affectively and gesturally; the projection of secondary characteristics noted in the medical section means others may perceive a female body and respond accordingly, and the body itself responds as if female-coded — which produces a layered consent and identity problem the canon does not resolve and which is among the most distressing features of the subject's life when he becomes aware of it. The host's reaction to discovering an alter's sexual activity is shame so acute it has triggered further decompensation.

**Touch tolerance, host.** Asymmetric. Right side accepts touch better than left (suggests trauma-encoded laterality, possibly originating in the embassy attack). Top of head, hair, face: do not touch unless invited; produces flinch and pupil dilation. Shoulders, upper back: tolerated after trust. Hands: held willingly. Wrists: do not grip; produces immediate alter-surge risk. Feet, neck: institutional zones; do not approach.

---

## 9. GROOMING, DRESS, AND OBJECT RELATIONS

**Hygiene.** Adequate but minimal. Showers daily when functional, less often during depressive troughs. Does not shave consistently; facial hair grows in patchy and is removed in batches. Does not attempt to tame the hair; appears to have accepted it as a fixed feature roughly by age twenty.

**Dress, host.** Plain, layered, dark, loose. Long-sleeved shirts year-round (covers arms; the arms appear unmarked but the covering is habitual). Trousers loose at the waist (chronic weight loss; cinches with a belt at a hole worn deeper than the others by several years of use). Footwear: soft, broken-in, never new. He does not buy new clothes; clothes appear from somewhere and are worn until they fail.

**Dress, alter-coded.** Jack adds jackets, boots, sometimes a hat. Cyndi adds color, often in flashes — a scarf, a bracelet — that subject afterwards regards as foreign objects. The Spurrier-era *costume* (his self-designed heroic uniform) is a separate category: deliberately constructed, deliberately worn, and represents the host's attempt to claim somatic territory back from the alters by *forcing* the body into a single, named, externally-coded identity. The act of dressing in it is ritualized and slow.

**Object relations.** Subject carries few things. A notebook (irregular, contents largely lists and names, including names of alters he has identified and dates). Tea-making apparatus when traveling. No photographs of his father; one of his mother, very small, kept folded. The neural restraint devices when in use are worn under hair and clothing and are touched compulsively when present and *reached for* when absent — a phantom-limb response to externalized self-regulation.

---

## 10. AUTONOMIC AND PSIONIC SOMATIC PHENOMENA

The body produces continuous low-grade psionic emission that registers as a complex of small environmental anomalies in his vicinity: minor electrical interference, occasional flickering of incandescent bulbs, faint static-electric phenomena on metal surfaces, low-amplitude infrasonic perceived by sensitive observers as a *pressure* rather than a sound. These do not stop. They are the somatic baseline.

Under stress, the phenomena scale: bulbs blow, ferrous objects within several meters drift or rattle, observers report headache, nausea, or olfactory hallucinations (most commonly burning, occasionally rose or ozone). Body temperature destabilizes — flushing or pallor uncorrelated with ambient — and palmar sweat increases. Blood pressure (per Muir records) spikes during alter-shifts.

Under critical-state engagement (reality-warping alters surfacing), the local somatic field becomes *non-Euclidean*: distances misreport, light bends fractionally, time-perception destabilizes for observers within roughly ten meters. The subject's body, at that point, is no longer fully classifiable as a body in the ordinary sense; it is the locus of an event. The file flags this as the threshold beyond which conventional somatic observation ceases to be meaningful and astral-plane monitoring becomes the only adequate instrument.

---

## 11. ROUTES, RITUALS, AND THE SMALL DAILY ORDER

Subject is creature of repeating micro-routine when stable. Morning sequence (when sleeping in a fixed location): wake, check hands, sit on edge of bed for 60–180 seconds, stand, drink water, urinate, wash face with cold water (never warm), brew tea, sit with tea, attempt meditation (Merzah-derived, sustained 5–25 minutes depending on day), then dress. The sequence is invariant when conditions permit; disruption of any element produces measurable destabilization across the rest of the day.

Walking routes, when free to choose, hug walls and corners; he avoids the centers of plazas and open rooms. He sits with his back to the wall, facing the door, every time. He counts exits within thirty seconds of entering any space. He will not ride elevators alone if avoidable; if unavoidable, he stands in the back-right corner, facing the door, hands at his sides.

These are the routines of a man who has, repeatedly and at scale, been the source of his own danger and who organizes the body's small daily motions around minimizing the surface area of surprise. The file's overall finding on the somatic dimension is that this is a body run as a containment facility: every habit, posture, route, and ritual a small lock on a door behind which something the subject loves and fears in equal measure is, for now, sleeping.

— END SECTION —


## Attachment & Relational Patterns

# Attachment & Relational Patterns — Subject: David Charles Haller

## 1. Attachment Classification and Etiological Frame

Subject presents the textbook end-state of **disorganized attachment (Type D)** as articulated by Main and Solomon, evolving across adulthood into what attachment theorists now describe as **fearful-avoidant** with strong **anxious-preoccupied flares** toward paternal-coded figures. The diagnostic shorthand: he wants closeness with a desperation that frightens him, mistrusts the closeness when it arrives, sabotages it to prove the mistrust correct, then grieves the loss as if it were inflicted rather than authored. The cycle repeats across every meaningful dyad on record from 1985 through the Krakoan era, with sufficient phenotypic stability across writers' hands that the pattern must be read as character-structural rather than authorial drift.

The etiology has three load-bearing pillars, and the file should hold them together at all times when interpreting his behavior:

**Pillar one — the withheld father.** Charles Xavier did not leave; he was never told to stay. Gabrielle Haller carried the pregnancy alone, raised the child alone, named the child alone. The father is therefore not a figure of loss in the ordinary mournable sense — he is a figure of *absence as a structural condition of the universe*. The child grew up assuming a normal world contained no father; the later discovery that the father not only existed but was the most famous mutant on earth recast every year of his childhood as something done *to* him by an act of paternal will. This is more injurious than ordinary abandonment: it indicts the entire prior life as a deception. Subject's first encounter with Xavier is therefore not a reunion but a revelation, and revelations of this magnitude leave attachment circuitry permanently miswired.

**Pillar two — the traumatized mother.** Gabrielle Haller is a Holocaust survivor, a diplomat, a woman of evident moral seriousness and observable love. But she is also, by every available indicator, a survivor in the technical sense — a mother whose own attachment system was structured by atrocity, who can love her child but whose capacity for spontaneous, regulated mirroring of normal childhood affect is constrained by her own history. Subject grows up with a mother whose love is real and whose nervous system is already at capacity. He learns early to manage himself, to not overwhelm her, to absorb rather than express. This is the substrate on which dissociation will later be built: a child who has already, before any mutant manifestation, internalized the principle that his largest feelings must be hidden because the people he loves cannot survive them.

**Pillar three — the embassy attack.** At eight-to-ten years old, depending on retcon, subject witnesses his stepfather/father-figure Daniel Shomron murdered, retaliates telepathically, and absorbs the dying terrorist's consciousness. The attachment-relevant consequence is rarely discussed but cannot be overstated: *the first time he ever exercised his power, it was to kill the people who killed the man who loved him, and the consequence was that the killer moved into his head and never left.* The earliest lesson his nervous system ever encoded about intimacy is that love is followed by murder, that retaliation is followed by colonization, and that the boundary between self and other is permeable in the worst direction. Every later relationship is filtered through this prior.

## 2. The Internal Working Model

Bowlby's "internal working model" — the cognitive-affective template a child constructs about whether others are reliable and whether the self is worthy of care — is, in subject's case, observably divided across alters. This is structurally novel and clinically important.

- **Host David** holds the model: *I am too much; others will be destroyed by me; therefore distance is love.* This is the conscious operating principle and it explains the chronic self-isolation, the retreat to Muir, the retreat to the Himalayas, the costume-and-mission self-sufficiency posture of the Spurrier era.
- **Karami** holds a different model entirely: *connection is possible; reparation is possible; the work of relationship is daily and patient.* Karami is, paradoxically, the most securely attached personality in the system, which makes sense — he was a fully formed adult when absorbed, with whatever attachment history he had already consolidated. He is also the alter who most consistently advocates for therapeutic engagement, integration, and trust.
- **Jack Wayne** holds: *others are instruments or obstacles; intimacy is conquest; vulnerability is contempt-worthy.* The hypermasculine swagger is a defense against attachment, not a style of it.
- **Cyndi** holds: *no one will protect me, so I will burn first.* She is preemptive-rage attachment: the rejection she anticipates is foreclosed by the rejection she enacts.
- **The Legion-alter and its kin** hold the most primitive position: *annihilate the threat of being unloved by annihilating everything that could love or fail to love.*

The host therefore is not the sole bearer of the relational template; he is one voice in a parliament whose members have incompatible attachment styles and who take turns at the controls. *This is why subject cannot simply learn better relational behavior.* Cognitive-behavioral correction at the host level does not propagate to the alters. The relational pathology is federated.

## 3. The Bonding Sequence — How He Approaches

Subject's bonding behavior follows a stereotyped four-phase sequence, observable across every significant relationship in the file. The phases compress or distend by relationship type but the order does not vary.

**Phase A — Selection by Idealization.** Subject does not slide into relationships. He chooses, and he chooses by elevating the target to mythic status before the relationship has any content. Xavier is the most-famous-mutant-on-earth-and-also-my-father. Moira is the woman who saved me when I was a vegetable. Merzah is the master who can teach what no Western psychiatry can. Ruth is the only person who can see me clearly *because* she cannot see at all. The elevation is the bond's foundation, and it is structurally unstable: a foundation made of idealization cannot bear the weight of an actual person's failings.

**Phase B — Recruitment of the Other as Witness.** Once selected, the target is enrolled — silently, often without their knowledge — as the audience for whom subject's heroic narrative will be performed. This is the phase in which he begins designing himself for them: with Xavier, he becomes the prodigy mutant; with Merzah, the disciplined ascetic; with Ruth, the recovering hero. The selection of self-presentation is unconscious but consistent: he becomes, in front of each chosen other, whichever version of himself that other most needs to see. *This is not manipulation; it is the survival behavior of a child who learned that he must shape himself to whichever caregiver is in the room.*

**Phase C — Disclosure of the Damage.** At some point, usually when the relationship has acquired enough weight to make withdrawal painful, subject discloses — or fails to suppress — the internal disorder. The alters surface; the catastrophic act is revealed; the omega-class destruction-fantasy leaks. He watches the other's face for the reaction. *Every subsequent relational move is calibrated against this reaction.* If the other recoils, Phase D is contempt and self-erasure. If the other stays, Phase D is the much more dangerous problem of being loved despite the truth — a stimulus his system was never trained to metabolize.

**Phase D — Stress-Testing Toward Catastrophe.** Whether the relationship survives Phase C or not, subject begins to test it. He withdraws to see if he is pursued; he discloses worse to see if it can be borne; he creates artificial separations to rehearse the loss he expects; in the most severe cases (AoA, Age of X) he reorganizes reality itself rather than risk authentic continued contact. The deep belief animating Phase D is: *if I cannot bear the suspense of waiting for them to leave, I will leave first, or I will make them leave, or I will dissolve the world in which leaving is possible.*

## 4. The Catalog of Bonds

### 4.1 Charles Xavier — The Originating Wound

Every other relationship in subject's life is a refraction of this one. The relationship is not characterized by what passed between them — which was, behaviorally, very little — but by what did not. Xavier is the father who appeared too late, who treated his son as a patient and an asset before treating him as a son, who never publicly claimed him, who died before any real reconciliation could occur, and who haunts the subject's psyche thereafter as both injunction and absence. The Legion Quest is the relational endpoint of this dyad: subject's grandiose belief that he can win his father's love by perfecting his father's dream culminates in the patricide that Xavier himself, alive, would have most condemned. *He killed his father in a sincere attempt to please him.* This is the central image of his entire attachment life and the template for every subsequent love.

After Xavier's death (AvX), the relationship continues — internally — with greater intimacy than it ever had in life. Spurrier's run shows subject literally talking to his dead father, hallucinating him, arguing with him, designing his hero career as a posthumous correction. The dead father is in some ways easier to love than the living one was: he cannot reject, cannot withhold, cannot fail to claim. The grief is therefore never resolved because it is never permitted to be grief; it remains a continuing relationship with a counterparty who can no longer disappoint, which is the only form in which subject can sustain a bond with him.

### 4.2 Gabrielle Haller — The Mother As Background Constant

The file is sparse on direct mother-son interactions in the adult period, and this sparsity is itself diagnostic. Subject does not return to her, does not lean on her, does not perform his crises in front of her. The protective distance is mutual and tender: he loves her too well to subject her to him. The mother is therefore preserved by exclusion — kept whole in his mind by being kept out of his life. This is a recurring relational maneuver: *the people he loves most appear in his daily existence the least.*

### 4.3 Moira MacTaggert — The Containment Caregiver

Moira is the woman who kept him alive through years of catatonia and who treated him as a clinical project for the entirety of his adolescence. The relationship has a specific texture: gratitude shadowed by the unspoken knowledge that her care was professional in addition to maternal, that he was a case as well as a person. He never quite forgives her for the asylum frame, even as he never stops being grateful for it. With Moira he established the lifelong pattern that would later replicate with Merzah and with the various devices: *acceptance of restraint by a trusted other as a substitute for self-regulation he cannot achieve alone.* He is a man who consents to be jailed by people who love him.

### 4.4 The Internal Population — Karami, Wayne, Cyndi, and the Thousand

The alters constitute his most continuous relationships — the only ones present every hour of every day across forty years of canon. The attachments here are not metaphorical; they are functional relationships with persistent counterparties whose voices, demands, and affects must be negotiated daily. With **Karami** the bond is the closest he has to a sibling-attachment: a person who arrived through violence and chose, over decades, to become an ally. With **Wayne** the bond is the relationship of a host to a tenant he cannot evict and who steals from him — a dyad of resentment, fear, and grudging utility. With **Cyndi** the bond is parental and guilt-laden: she is the rage of an injured child he must both protect and contain. With the broader population, particularly post-Carey, the relationships become administrative — he is the warden of a prison whose inmates he made and cannot release.

The structural fact: *subject's primary relational training across his entire adult life is intramural.* Whatever skills he has developed for negotiation, accommodation, and coalition-building were honed inside his own skull, on counterparties who cannot leave. This explains his external relational style — he treats other people, initially, as if they too cannot leave, and is repeatedly astonished when they can.

### 4.5 Merzah the Mystic — The Chosen Father

After Xavier's death, subject travels to a Himalayan monastery and submits to a teacher. The choice is overdetermined: a remote location (separation as condition of attachment), a master capable of psychic discipline (a father he can succeed with), a regime of internal containment (the relational mode he already understood from Moira). With Merzah he constructs the architecture of the mental prison — and when Merzah is killed, subject's response is not the catastrophic decompensation Xavier's death produced but a colder, more terrible determination to *become* the master himself. *The second father-loss does not break him in the same way because he has already accepted that fathers are taken from him as a rule of the universe.* What remains is the work.

### 4.6 Ruth Aldine (Blindfold) — The Sole Mutual Adult Bond

Ruth is the relational anomaly in the file and the most important data point for any prognosis. With her — and only with her — subject experiences a relationship that is approximately symmetrical, that proceeds without his selecting her as paternal authority or maternal container, that survives Phase C of his bonding sequence (she sees him fully, including the alters, and remains), and that produces measurable improvement in his function. She is also, critically, a precognitive — a person who already knows what he will become before he becomes it, which has the paradoxical effect of disabling his usual performance-for-the-witness behavior. He cannot design himself for her, because she already sees the design. This forces, for the first time in his life, an authentic self-presentation, and the alters quiet measurably during periods of high contact with her.

The relationship also exposes the floor of his pathology. When he believes he is becoming a threat to her — when his future-self appears as the agent of catastrophe she has foreseen — his response is the relational maneuver he has performed at every prior catastrophe: removal of self from the equation. Spurrier's terminal arc has him erase himself from reality to prevent the harm. *He loves her by ceasing to exist.* This is the same gesture as the AoA gambit translated into a sacrificial register: the only way he knows to give a person what they need is to subtract himself from their world.

### 4.7 The X-Men as Group — The Foreclosed Sibling Cohort

His relationship to the X-Men collectively is one of the most chronically painful and least examined in the file. They are his father's true children — the cohort Xavier did publicly claim, did publicly raise, did publicly love. Subject is forever the late-arriving half-sibling who must earn what they received as a birthright. He cycles through approach (joining as auxiliary, fighting alongside them) and withdrawal (the Age of X reality is in part a fantasy in which he is a *real* X-Man, fully accepted, fully integrated — the wish made world). The X-Men, for their part, treat him with the wary politeness reserved for a half-brother who is also a security risk, which confirms his prior. The bond is therefore stuck in a permanent low-temperature version of his cycle: never close enough to test, never distant enough to release.

## 5. Distrust — The Specific Texture of His Suspicion

Subject's distrust is not the paranoid distrust of a primary psychotic disorder; it is the structurally informed distrust of someone whose history has taught him three specific lessons:

**Lesson one: caregivers withhold.** Anyone in a position of care will turn out, eventually, to have been holding something back. Xavier withheld paternity. Moira withheld the full prognosis. Merzah withheld whatever the next stage of training required him to face. The distrust is therefore *anticipatory disclosure-monitoring*: subject is constantly, quietly, watching for what the trusted other is not telling him. When a withhold is detected — and one always is, since all humans withhold — the prior is confirmed.

**Lesson two: love does not protect from violation.** The terrorist absorption taught him at a developmentally encoding age that intimate proximity is a vector for invasion. He distrusts closeness *as a category*, not because he expects ill intent from any specific person but because his nervous system has learned that closeness is the condition under which the worst things happen. This produces the characteristic somatic flinch at being touched without warning, the tendency to seat himself with sight-lines to exits, the preference for psychic communication (which he can sever) over verbal (which he cannot).

**Lesson three: his own perception is not reliable.** This is the deepest layer of distrust and the one with the most relational consequence. Because his alters can perceive, decide, and act without his knowledge, he cannot fully trust his own memories of any interaction. Did the friend really say that, or did Wayne hear it through a filter? Did he really agree to this, or did Cyndi sign on his behalf? The distrust here folds back on the self: he cannot trust others because he cannot trust the part of him that is observing them. This makes him a chronically unreliable witness to his own relationships, which he knows, which makes him distrust his own grievances, which makes him slow to leave situations a healthier person would exit and slow to stay in situations a healthier person would invest in.

## 6. Betrayal — How He Inflicts and How He Receives

**Betrayal received.** When subject perceives himself betrayed, the reaction is not rage in the first instance but a quiet, almost grateful confirmation: *I knew this was coming.* The expected betrayal hurts less than the unexpected one would; the expectation is itself a defense. Behaviorally, he withdraws — physically, psionically — and reorganizes his internal narrative to incorporate the betrayer as further evidence of the world's structure. The slow secondary reaction is sometimes catastrophic: the alters, particularly Cyndi and the more violent population, process betrayal at a different timescale than the host, and a betrayal that the host has metabolized into resigned distance may resurface weeks later as the trigger for a destructive episode the host does not remember authoring.

**Betrayal inflicted.** He betrays others by absence more often than by action. The withdrawal that protects him reads, externally, as abandonment. He vanishes from contact, sometimes for years, with people who had reason to consider him a friend; he reappears expecting the relationship to resume from where it paused, and is wounded by the discovery that it has moved on without him. The pattern is unconscious and uncruel; it is the relational time-signature of a person who has been catatonic, time-displaced, and pocket-dimensioned, for whom the ordinary calendar of relational maintenance does not apply.

The more severe betrayals — the AoA killing, the unconscious construction of false realities for his teammates to inhabit — are not experienced by him as betrayals at the moment of commission. They are experienced as *help*. This is the most dangerous feature of his relational repertoire: he betrays the people he loves while believing he is saving them, and the discovery of what he has done arrives only after the damage is irreparable. The guilt is then total and durable, which is itself a problem, because it scaffolds the next round of grandiose self-punishment-as-heroism.

## 7. Repair — The Specific Mechanism and Its Limits

Subject is, against expectation, capable of repair, and the mechanism is worth specifying because it diverges from typical clinical pictures.

He cannot repair by negotiation. He does not have the regulated affect required for the difficult conversation; attempts at it almost always trigger an alter to surface, which terminates the conversation by replacing the conversant. He cannot repair by graduated exposure to the ruptured other; the disclosure that would be required exceeds his disclosure tolerance.

He repairs, when he repairs at all, by **demonstrated sacrificial action over long timescales**. The pattern: he disappears, undertakes something costly (training, mission, self-restraint), and returns having become — measurably — a more contained version of himself, which he offers as the apology he cannot articulate. The other party is required, in this model, to read the returned-and-altered self as the message. When the other party can do this (Ruth, sometimes Karami, occasionally Moira), repair holds. When the other party requires verbal acknowledgment or behavioral commitment to specific change (most peer relationships), repair fails, because subject cannot produce the verbal artifact and cannot guarantee specific behavior given the federated nature of his system.

The limit of his repair capacity is therefore set not by his willingness but by his *bandwidth*. He has perhaps one or two reparative relational projects in flight at any time; any more exceeds his regulatory resources. He prioritizes — usually correctly — the relationships where repair is structurally possible, and lets the others lapse. This produces the characteristic shape of his relational network: a very small number of deep, painfully tended bonds and a vast hinterland of half-lapsed, ambiguously-still-real acquaintances.

## 8. Intimacy and Dependency Patterns

**Physical intimacy.** Sparse in the file; what is present is consistently filtered through the dissociative architecture. Subject is observably uncomfortable with casual touch; he flinches from initiation, accepts touch from trusted others with visible relief, and never initiates without significant antecedent emotional contact. Sexual intimacy is rarely depicted but is implied with Ruth, and the surrounding behavioral cues suggest that it is — for him — a high-risk activity precisely because of its dissolution of the body-boundary he relies upon to sequester alters. He is the kind of intimate partner who must be approached slowly, asked at each step, and given the option to surface or submerge at will.

**Emotional dependency.** Severe and underacknowledged. Subject *requires* an external regulating other to function at a baseline above crisis. Without one, he constructs proxies (Merzah, dead-Xavier internal dialogue, the headband as parental object). The dependency is masked by his hero-posture and his physical isolation, but it is structural: he has never sustained extended high-function periods without an anchoring relationship. The dependency is also asymmetrical and exhausting to the anchor — he takes more than he can return, knows it, hates himself for it, and either over-compensates with grandiose gestures or withdraws to spare them. Neither response solves the underlying disparity.

**Tolerance for absence.** Paradoxically high in short terms and catastrophically low in long terms. He can manage days of being alone with little distress; weeks begin to corrode him; months produce decompensation. The opposite is also true of his anchors: he can manage knowing they exist somewhere; he cannot manage their definitive removal. The Xavier death cracked something that the Merzah death only worsened.

## 9. The Repeating Relational Template

Stripped to its load-bearing elements, the template subject reenacts across every significant relationship is:

> **I find a person who could complete or contain me. I elevate them. I reshape myself for them. I disclose the worst of me to see whether they will remain. If they remain, I love them with a desperation that frightens us both. I test the bond toward catastrophe because I cannot bear the suspense of waiting for it to end. When catastrophe arrives — by my hand or theirs or the world's — I remove myself from their lives as the final act of love, and I take the removal as further evidence that I am unfit to be loved.**

Every dyad in the file maps to this template with minor variations. Xavier was the first iteration and the structural template-setter; Moira was the iteration in which removal was psychiatric (catatonia); the X-Men were the iteration in which removal was social (auxiliary status, never core); Merzah was the iteration in which catastrophe arrived externally and removal was symbolic (inheritance of his discipline); Ruth was the iteration in which the template was tested closest to its limits, survived longest, and ultimately produced the literal-cosmological removal (self-deletion from reality) that the template demands.

The most important inference for any future relational analysis: *the template will reassert itself.* Any new bond he forms — and the post-Krakoan canon will form them — will follow this sequence unless and until the underlying attachment structure is repaired, which would require sustained therapeutic


## Defenses & Compensatory Mechanisms

# SECTION 7 — DEFENSES & COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS

## Preliminary Note on Methodology

The defensive architecture of David Charles Haller is the most unusual case file this office has compiled, for one reason that must be stated before any taxonomy is offered: in Subject's case, **the defenses are not metaphorical**. When a conventional patient "splits off" an unbearable affect, the affect persists in some attenuated, displaced, somatized, or projected form within a single body and brain. When Subject splits off an unbearable affect, the affect *walks across the room as another person*, with its own voice, posture, secondary sex characteristics, name, history, and superhuman power-set. Vaillant's hierarchy of defenses — pathological, immature, neurotic, mature — was constructed on the assumption that the patient's defenses *fail at the edges*, leaking what they cannot contain. Subject's defenses do not leak. They *incarnate*. This makes the standard ranking sharper than usual, but it also means each defense must be read at two registers: the ordinary psychic register (what it does inside him) and the manifest register (what it does to the room, the building, the city, the timeline).

The defenses below are ranked from most primitive to most mature, in approximate developmental and structural order, with operational notes from canon.

---

## 1. Dissociative Splitting (Structural) — The Foundation Stone

This is the **first and irreducible defense**, the defense from which every other one in Subject's repertoire is built and to which every other one returns under sufficient pressure. It is the defense established in the embassy attack at age 8–10, and it is so well-rehearsed, so well-rewarded, and so neurologically over-learned that it has become the *default mode of consciousness* rather than a discrete coping operation.

**Mechanism.** Affect, impulse, memory, or capability that the host self cannot tolerate is **encapsulated into a personality state with its own continuous identity**. The host does not feel rage; Cyndi feels rage. The host is not predatory or sexually aggressive; Jack Wayne is. The host is not a killer; Karami was a killer, and Karami is now somebody else inside the same skull. The host did not, in any meaningful first-person sense, murder his father; Legion-the-alter did.

**Behavioral signatures (granular).**
- Mid-sentence pronoun shifts ("I didn't — *we* didn't —") observed across multiple writers, particularly under direct interrogation about past acts.
- Brief leftward gaze-drift before alter onset, followed by full postural reorganization within 1–3 seconds.
- Hair-line phenomena (the vertical electrostatic discharge along the scalp) intensify in the seconds preceding alter switching, functioning as an early-warning tell for anyone trained to read him.
- After-the-fact narration of his own actions in the **second or third person**: "He shouldn't have done that. *I* shouldn't have done that." The self-correction itself is a tell.
- Time gaps in autobiographical report — Subject can describe the day before and the day after a destructive episode, but the episode itself returns in fragmentary, often visual-only flashes.

**Why it is so deeply lodged.** Splitting was, the very first time it occurred, *catastrophically successful*. It saved his life and his sanity in the embassy. It also handed him the absorbed mind of a dying terrorist as a permanent inner companion — a result the developing nervous system could only interpret as *this works*. Every subsequent overload has been met by the same operation because the operation has been reinforced, over decades, by survival utility. The defense cannot be extinguished by ordinary therapeutic means because it is not maladaptive in the conventional sense — it is *over*adaptive.

---

## 2. Somatic Conversion via Psionic Projection

A defense unique to Subject's phenotype. Affect that cannot be contained in the alter-system is **discharged through the body's psionic interface** rather than through conventional somatization (ulcers, conversion paralysis, pseudoseizures).

**Behavioral signatures.**
- The hair. The hair is not a hairstyle. It is an **autonomic discharge channel**, a visible barometer of intrapsychic pressure. Calm Subject still has elevated hair; agitated Subject has hair that crackles and rises further; full-flood Subject has hair indistinguishable from a Tesla coil arc. No barber on record has ever made it lie flat for more than a few hours.
- Ambient telekinetic micro-disturbances when distressed: cutlery vibration, page-flutter without wind, light-fixture flicker. Documented across Muir Island, the X-Mansion, and the Himalayan retreat.
- Apparent musculature and even sex-characteristic shifts during alter dominance (Cyndi's projection famously alters the body's read). This is **the body itself participating in the defense**, recruiting the psionic field to dress in the alter's image so that the host need not even own the meat.

The defense is so total that Subject does not have a stable body schema. Body image is, in clinical terms, **non-conserved across episodes**.

---

## 3. Acting Out — at Cosmological Scale

Where ordinary patients act out interpersonally (the affair, the bar fight, the resignation email at 3 a.m.), Subject acts out **across timelines and realities**. The defense is the same; only the canvas is unprecedented.

**Documented instances.**
- *Legion Quest (1995).* The plan to murder Magneto in the past is, structurally, a tantrum dressed as a strategy. It is the toddler's wish to be powerful enough to fix the parents, granted weapons-grade omega capability. The Age of Apocalypse is the splash radius of an acting-out episode.
- *Age of X (Legacy #245–247).* Subject's unconscious constructs an entire pocket reality with fabricated identities for the X-Men — a continent-scale, multi-mind acting-out, rationalized as containment of the Legion-alter.
- *Spurrier-era self-deletion.* The final acting-out: the patient who walks out of the session by walking out of being.

The defense is *acting out* and not, strictly, *psychotic decompensation* because each instance has an internal logic the host can articulate if pressed. The grandiosity is structured, not random.

---

## 4. Projective Identification
