Subject does not merely project; he projects *into living systems that then perform the projected content back at him*. Karami, the absorbed terrorist, is the cleanest example: an external object (a hostile mind) is taken inside, treated as part of the self, and then — over years — comes to operate as the *moral conscience* Subject cannot generate from his own resources. Subject has externalized his superego into a stranger and then re-internalized the stranger. This is projective identification with a feedback loop sealed by mutant capability.

A second instance: the X-Men, in Carey's runs and again in Spurrier's, are repeatedly **made to enact roles Subject has unconsciously assigned them** — savior, judge, executioner, mirror. They do not always know they are being cast. He does not always know he is casting.

---

## 5. Idealization and Devaluation (with Asymmetry)

Standard primitive defense, observed in textbook form around every paternal figure: Xavier, Moira MacTaggert, Merzah, briefly Magneto-as-rival-father.

**The asymmetry is diagnostically important.** In standard borderline-spectrum presentations, idealization-devaluation cycles symmetrically — the lover is god, then trash, then god again. In Subject's case, **devaluation is almost always aborted mid-arc and converted into self-attack**. He cannot sustain a hostile read of the father. The moment Xavier disappoints him, the affect that would, in another patient, become contempt or grievance, in Subject becomes shame and a redoubled effort to earn the lost approval. The devaluation does occur — but it lands on himself.

This is why Xavier's death was so destabilizing: the death sealed the cycle before the devaluation could ever land where it belonged.

---

## 6. Omnipotent Fantasy / Grandiose Compensation

The compensatory mechanism most visible to outsiders and the one most often confused with the underlying pathology. Subject's grandiose plans — kill Magneto and complete the dream, train in the Himalayas and become a hero on his own terms, save the X-Men from the alter by building them a better world — are **cognitive expressions of an infant's wish to be powerful enough to make the parent love him**.

The compensation is *negative* (in the diagnostic sense — it produces harm) because of the catastrophic mismatch between the affective age of the wish (preschool) and the operational scale of its execution (omega-class mutant ability). A two-year-old's bid for parental attention, granted the means to rewrite time, becomes the Age of Apocalypse.

**Behavioral tells.**
- Costume design as ritual. Subject has, repeatedly across runs, *designed his own outfit* before attempting heroism — the act of self-naming and self-uniforming is the grandiose compensation made tangible.
- Speeches and manifestos, often delivered to an audience of one (himself, in a mirror, or to Ruth as proxy). The rhetoric is the load-bearing structure of the compensation.
- Adoption of mentor-language ("the dream," "the work") absorbed verbatim from Xavier and redeployed in his own voice.

---

## 7. Reaction Formation (Spurrier-Era Dominant)

A neurotic-tier defense observable mostly in the *Legacy vol. 2* maturation arc and after. The rule: **the louder Subject insists on a virtue, the more violently the opposite content is active beneath**.

- "I am in control of my mind" — said in the moments preceding alter breakthrough.
- "I am no longer my father's son in any way that limits me" — said while wearing a costume that visually echoes Xavier's color palette and while pursuing Xavier's mission.
- "I will not harm Ruth" — said in the build-up to a future in which his existence is what harms her.

Reaction formation in Subject is **the marker of his most evolved period**, because it requires a host self stable enough to construct a virtuous self-image to defend. Earlier in the record, the defense is unavailable; there is no integrated "I" to perform a virtue from.

---

## 8. Isolation of Affect

Subject can describe — in flat, articulate, often clinically precise language — events that should produce overwhelming grief or terror. The Karami absorption, the embassy attack, the patricide, the Age of Apocalypse, all narrated in interviews with Moira and later with Merzah at a register of affect that is wildly mismatched to the content. This is not absence of feeling. The feeling has been **routed away from the narrative apparatus**, often into an alter, so that the host can speak about his own catastrophes the way a historian discusses a 19th-century war.

The defense fails predictably when the listener is someone whose approval Subject seeks. Then the isolation collapses, the affect floods back, and the alter system mobilizes.

---

## 9. Intellectualization

Closely paired with isolation of affect. Subject's vocabulary for his own pathology is **frighteningly accurate** — across writers, he has used language about "splitting," "containment," "integration," "alters," "psychic architecture." He has read his own chart. This is not pseudo-insight; the cognitions are largely correct. It is, however, a *defense*, because the act of describing the architecture is repeatedly substituted for the act of dismantling it.

The Himalayan training under Merzah is the most spectacular example: an entire ascetic regimen designed to **build a more elegant prison** rather than to free the prisoner. The intellectualization is so refined it becomes its own monastery.

---

## 10. Repetition Compulsion

Functionally a defense in the Freudian sense — the unbearable is returned to in the hope that this time the outcome will differ. Subject's life is structured as repetition at the cosmological scale:

- Twice, he has **erased himself from existence to repair what he or his father broke**. The structural identity of the AoA reset and the Spurrier-era self-deletion is not coincidence; it is repetition.
- Multiple successive *containment apparatuses* (Moira's interventions, the Stryfe headband, Merzah's internal prison) are the same defense rebuilt in different materials.
- Successive bids for paternal approval (Xavier alive, Xavier dying, Xavier's ghost, Merzah as surrogate, Magneto as anti-father, his own internalized father-ego) iterate the same approach pattern across decades.

The defense's logic: *if I do it again, more correctly, the wound will close.* It does not.

---

## 11. Sublimation (Partial, Fragile)

The first of the **mature-tier** defenses available to Subject, and the one most worth protecting clinically. Heroism, when it is not contaminated by the grandiose-omnipotent fantasy, is genuine sublimation: aggressive and reparative drives channeled into socially valuable action. The Legacy vol. 2 hero-arc is the longest sustained sublimation in the record.

It is fragile because it sits directly atop the grandiose compensation (mechanism 6) and is constantly recruited into its service. The diagnostic question — *is this gesture sublimation or grandiosity?* — is answered by looking at who Subject expects to be watching. Sublimation requires no audience. Grandiosity requires the father.

---

## 12. Altruism (Costly, Specific, Verified)

A mature defense reliably present in one circuit: **Ruth Aldine.** Subject's care for Ruth is observable, persistent, and not performed for any audience. He has subordinated his own missions to her safety. He has withheld information from her to protect her, and has accepted information from her that destabilized him, because she needed to be heard. This is altruism in Vaillant's strict sense — the conversion of conflict into the satisfaction of giving to another — and it is the **single most reliable indicator that the patient has not been lost**.

When the altruism extends beyond Ruth (to the New Mutants, to Merzah, to the X-Men in his better hours), it tends to be diluted by mechanisms 3 and 6. With Ruth, it stays clean.

---

## 13. Anticipation (Catastrophic Variant)

A mature defense, deployed *malignantly* in the terminal Spurrier arc. Subject anticipates a future in which he becomes the destroyer he has always feared, and acts in the present to prevent it. In an ordinary patient, anticipation looks like prudent planning, advance grief work, the will written before the diagnosis worsens. In Subject, anticipation looks like **self-erasure as preemption**.

This is the defense that gets him to the self-deletion ending, and it must be ranked among the mature-tier mechanisms because *the cognition is correct*. He really would have done the harm. The defense fails not at the level of accuracy but at the level of proportionality: the only intervention he can imagine at omega-scale is annihilation of his own existence.

---

## 14. Humor (Sporadic, Spurrier-Coded)

Late-emerging, intermittently observed, mostly in the Spurrier voice. Self-deprecating, aware of the absurdity of his own existence, occasionally directed at the apparatus of superhero life. The humor is real and is a mature-tier defense when present, but it does not have the structural depth in his repertoire that the lower-numbered defenses do. It is best read as **evidence of what he could have been with a different developmental history** — and therefore as an argument against giving up on him.

---

## Cross-Cutting Compensatory Mechanisms

Beyond the discrete defenses above, three compensatory **patterns** operate across the system:

### Positive

- **Conscience as load-bearing structure.** Despite the body count, Subject's superego is intact and often punishing. The conscience is partially housed in the Karami alter, which is an architectural oddity but a functional one: he has externalized his moral capacity into a being who cannot abandon him because that being lives inside him.
- **Treatment-seeking as identity.** Across forty years of publication, no matter the writer, **Subject keeps showing up for the next intervention.** He accepts the headband. He travels to the monastery. He cooperates with Moira, with Xavier, with Magneto, with Merzah, with Ruth-as-witness. The willingness to try is itself a compensatory mechanism — possibly the most clinically significant one in the file.
- **Capacity for one mutual attachment.** Demonstrated with Ruth. The capacity is narrow but real, and is the substrate on which any therapeutic alliance must be built.

### Negative

- **Heroism-as-penance.** The hero project is contaminated by guilt-management; rescues are performed to balance a ledger that cannot be balanced.
- **Withdrawal disguised as protection.** "I am leaving so I don't hurt you" is, in Subject, sometimes true and sometimes a rationalization of preemptive rejection. The two are clinically indistinguishable from the inside, which is why they recur.
- **Conversion of psychic pain into world-events.** The defining negative compensation. Other patients give themselves headaches; Subject gives the timeline an apocalypse. The mechanism is the same; only the scale invalidates ordinary containment strategies.
- **Containment-as-cure conflation.** Subject repeatedly mistakes the *suppression* of an alter for the *resolution* of the underlying split. Each new prison is, to him, evidence of progress. Each prison's eventual failure is, to him, evidence that the next prison must be stronger. The compensation is the architect of its own collapse.

---

## Operational Summary

The defensive architecture is **bottom-heavy**: mechanisms 1–6 (the primitive tier) do almost all of the load-bearing work, and the mature-tier defenses (11–14) sit on top of them as a thin and intermittent layer. Under any significant stress, the mature layer collapses first and the system reverts to splitting, somatic projection, acting out, and omnipotent fantasy in rapid succession. The escalation is predictable enough to be tabled (see Section 5) and is the basis for any operational protocol involving Subject.

The single most important clinical fact in this section is this: **none of Subject's defenses are stupid.** Every one of them was, at its origin, the correct response to an impossible situation. The pathology is not that he chose badly. The pathology is that he learned, too early and too well, and was never given the conditions under which he could afford to unlearn.

— END SECTION 7 —


## Longitudinal Psychological Profile

# Longitudinal Psychological Profile — David Charles Haller

*Decade-by-decade clinical evolution of affect regulation, cognitive style, and self-concept, derived from the cited behavioral record. Frameworks invoked: structural dissociation theory (van der Hart/Nijenhuis/Steele), Bowlby/Main attachment taxonomy, Kohutian self-psychology, Linehan's biosocial model of affect dysregulation, Herman's complex-trauma staging, Putnam's discrete-behavioral-states model of DID, and Kernberg's structural-personality organization scale. None of these were available to him; all of them apply.*

---

## I. Childhood and Pre-Onset (c. age 0 – age 9/10)

### Affect regulation
The pre-onset child, as reconstructable from the Haller household flashbacks (New Mutants #26–28; X-Men Legacy #1, 2012), presents as **constitutionally sensitive and environmentally over-buffered**. Gabrielle Haller, a Holocaust survivor diplomat, is a high-functioning trauma adult: warm, articulate, organized, but with the characteristic affect-narrowing of a survivor parent — affection delivered competently, distress metabolized privately, the household kept emotionally *quiet* so as not to re-injure the mother. The child therefore receives, in Linehan's terms, a moderately **invalidating environment** of the genteel kind — not cruelty, but a household where large feelings are not modeled, named, or coregulated, because the mother has spent decades learning to not have them in front of others. Daniel Shomron, the stepfather, appears to provide warmer secondary scaffolding, but the regulatory load is too thin for what is coming.

Baseline affect in this period is probably **mildly anxious-compliant** with episodic dysregulatory bursts the household reads as "moodiness." There is no model in his early environment for what to do with an explosion.

### Cognitive style
Intelligent, verbal, bicultural (French/Hebrew/English exposure inferable from the household's diplomatic life), oriented toward pleasing adults. The cognitive style of an only-child of a senior parent who is herself organized around a missing reference point (the father he does not know exists). Magical-thinking traces are likely already present in age-typical form: the wish-as-cause logic of the latency-age child, slightly inflated by precocity and by the unstated father-mystery.

### Self-concept
**Provisional, mother-mirrored, father-shaped-by-absence.** The classic structure of the unacknowledged child: a self organized around a gap. He does not yet know the gap's name, but he is already living its geometry — what Kohut would call a self with an unfilled idealizing pole, looking for someone large enough to merge with and be steadied by.

### The rupture event
The embassy attack does not modify this developmental line; it **detonates it.** Witnessing Shomron's murder collapses the secondary attachment scaffold; the psionic discharge that mind-burns the attackers introduces the child to himself as a killer; the absorption of Jemail Karami's dying consciousness installs a second mind inside the first. From a structural-dissociation standpoint this is a textbook **primary structural dissociation** event happening at the precise developmental window (latency-to-prepubertal) where DSM-aligned researchers identify peak risk for what will become DID. The defense saves the child's functional sanity in the moment by **partitioning the unbearable** — and is, catastrophically, *rewarded by survival*. The first lesson of his life as a mutant is: *splitting works.*

---

## II. Catatonic Adolescence on Muir Island (c. age 10 – late teens)

### Affect regulation
**Affect is offline at the surface and chaotic beneath.** Multi-year dissociative catatonia (New Mutants #26) is not absence of affect; it is the **tertiary structural dissociation** endpoint — the apparently normal personality (ANP) has gone dormant because every emotional part (EP) is too loud for it to inhabit the body. The Sienkiewicz-rendered astral plane sequences are diagnostic: a roiling internal weather of terror, rage, grief, sexual confusion, and grandiosity, with no executive self to modulate any of it. Externally: flat. Internally: storm.

This is the period in which his lifelong **dysregulatory grammar** is encoded. The body learns that "feeling something large" equals "the world ends, people die, my mind kills." The somatic prohibition against affect that follows him into adulthood is laid down here.

### Cognitive style
Functionally arrested. Cognition continues inside — the alters develop sophisticated voices, narratives, agendas — but **integrated reflective function is unavailable**. There is no metacognitive observer, in Fonagy's sense, capable of saying *I am having a thought.* There are only thoughts, owned by personalities that take turns owning them.

### Self-concept
**The host self is essentially in abeyance.** Karami, Jack Wayne, and Cyndi develop as the operational selves; "David" is the absent center around which they orbit. When the New Mutants enter his mind and Karami brokers a partial integration, what surfaces is not a recovered self but a **newly assembled one**, stitched from fragments and missing pieces — closer to what Putnam describes as a "host" personality created *after the fact* to manage the system, rather than the original child resumed.

The clinical signature of this period that persists for the rest of his life: **he experiences his own emergence into consciousness as a kind of awakening from a sleep he was not the one having.** He does not feel like the protagonist of his own past. This is not metaphor; it is the phenomenology of severe dissociative recovery.

---

## III. Late Adolescence / Early Adulthood — Muir Island Plateau (late 1980s, Claremont)

### Affect regulation
**Brittle external composure scaffolded entirely by others.** Moira MacTaggert provides the structural holding environment a developmental parent would have provided fifteen years earlier; the Muir Island facility functions as exoskeletal regulation. Within that scaffold, baseline affect is **anxious-vigilant** — the constant low-grade fear of an alter surfacing. Subject begins to demonstrate the characteristic DID-adult posture: **affect-monitoring as a full-time cognitive task**, with attention chronically split between the external world and an internal one.

Switching in this era is **trigger-bound and recognizable**: threat → Jack Wayne; humiliation or sexual content → Cyndi; moral complexity → Karami. The differentiation is clean enough that observers can begin to predict it, which is actually a sign of *system organization*, not chaos. Many DID patients in their twenties present exactly this way: the system has stabilized into a workable polity, even if the polity is at war.

### Cognitive style
Reemerges as **articulate, polite, slightly formal — the speech of someone who has had to relearn social register from observation rather than continuous participation.** He listens carefully. He defers. The cognition is intact but operates with an **over-cautious metacognitive overlay** ("if I think this, will it wake someone up?"), which produces a characteristic hesitancy and a tendency toward intellectualization. Abstract reasoning is preserved; rapid intuitive social cognition is impaired, because intuition requires unselfconscious affect-access he does not have.

### Self-concept
**The first stable bad answer to the identity question.** He begins to define himself, in this period, as **"Charles Xavier's son" and as "Moira's patient"** — two relational identities, both subordinate, both organized around being-watched-by-a-better. Kohut would describe this as a **mirror-hungry/idealization-hungry self** finding two partial selfobjects and clinging to both. There is no autonomous "David" yet; there is the son and the patient.

Critical, often-overlooked development of this era: **he begins to *like* some of his alters.** Karami particularly. The system stops being purely persecutory and starts being, in a sad way, his social world. This will matter enormously in his thirties, when integration is proposed as treatment goal — he resists it partly because it would, from his subjective interior, be a series of killings.

---

## IV. Early Adulthood — The Legion Quest Era (c. age 20–22, 1995)

### Affect regulation
**A specific, catastrophic decompensation pattern emerges and is now diagnosable.** The pre-AoA David is, on the surface, the most "recovered" he has been: lucid, organized, articulate, even charismatic. The clinical mistake — made by every character around him and by readers — is to interpret this as health. It is the **manic-coherent presentation of a vulnerable narcissistic decompensation in progress.** When the wounded grandiose pole of the self finally finds a project large enough to fit it (*I will kill Magneto, perfect the dream, win the father*), affect organizes around the mission with frightening tidiness. The internal storm goes quiet because *all of him is finally pointing the same direction.*

This is the most important affect-regulatory datum in his entire history: **he is only ever fully integrated when oriented toward catastrophe.** The same wholeness he seeks through monks and headbands is available to him for free whenever he commits to an annihilatory plan. Health and apocalypse feel the same from inside.

### Cognitive style
**Grandiose-strategic.** The plan is well-formed: he understands time travel, identifies the leverage point, anticipates resistance. Cognition is **functionally hypomanic but not disorganized** — goal-directed, energetic, internally consistent, magical only at the load-bearing premise (*killing Magneto = father's love*). The premise is delusional in Jaspers's strict sense (incorrigible, idiosyncratic, derived from affective rather than evidentiary grounds), but it is dressed in instrumentally sound reasoning, which makes it almost impossible to argue him out of.

### Self-concept
**Briefly, terribly coherent.** He is, for the first time in his life, **a person with a mission rather than a patient with a condition.** This unitary self is built on a single fused identification: *I am my father's instrument; I am the one who will finish his work.* This is exactly the kind of foreclosed identity Marcia's adolescent-identity model describes — adopted whole from an authority figure without exploration — except the authority figure has never spoken to him about it, so he is foreclosing on a *fantasy* of the father.

When the plan kills Xavier instead of Magneto, the foreclosure shatters. The post-event self has nowhere to go and is, mercifully for him and disastrously for the timeline, **erased from existence before having to metabolize what it has done.**

---

## V. Late Twenties / Early Thirties — Post-Resurrection and Carey Era

### Affect regulation
**Re-traumatized baseline, technologically scaffolded.** Returning to existence carrying the AoA memory — even partially, even with the timeline reset — installs what looks like classic **post-atrocity moral injury** on top of the existing C-PTSD. He is quieter in this period; the affect is **depressively flat with episodic flares**, and the flares are now actively feared by the subject himself rather than merely by others.

The neural/Stryfe-derived containment apparatus represents a critical evolution in his regulatory model: **he has accepted that his mind requires hardware.** Where Muir-era David tolerated being a patient, post-resurrection David has internalized the identity of *a man who needs a device to be safe to be near.* This is a downgrade in self-concept dressed as an upgrade in function — and it is the seed of every subsequent attempt to find a more elegant prison.

### Cognitive style
**Reflective, guilt-saturated, prone to intellectualized rumination.** He thinks well and constantly about what he has done, which is in some senses healthier than not thinking about it and in other senses a fresh defense — **affective avoidance via cognitive over-processing.** He can give you a coherent account of his pathology; he cannot use the account to change. This is the cognitive style of many high-functioning trauma adults in extended treatment: insight outruns capacity.

The **Age of X arc (Legacy #245–247)** is the most diagnostically telling event of this decade. Without conscious awareness, he generates an entire pocket reality and a falsified set of identities for the X-Men, in order to suppress a single violent alter. This is **dissociation acting at the scale of his powers**: the defense is no longer encapsulating an affect inside the mind, it is **encapsulating a reality outside it.** The cognitive style is now *world-building as repression.* No human-scale framework adequately captures this; the closest is what Bromberg calls "standing in the spaces" between self-states, except the spaces have become inhabited geographies.

### Self-concept
**Patient-with-device.** A self defined by what restrains it. There is genuine character — kindness, hesitancy, dry self-awareness — but no autonomous project. He is waiting, in this period, for someone to tell him what he is for. When no one does, the unconscious supplies the Age of X as a kind of dream-solution: *be a hero in a world you secretly built so that the part of you that wants to destroy this world has somewhere harmless to live.*

---

## VI. Thirties — The Spurrier / Legacy vol. 2 Maturation Arc

This is the **richest single period of psychological development** in the entire record and warrants the longest treatment.

### Affect regulation
**Active, effortful, monk-trained, and — for the first time — partially internalized.** The Merzah training installs what is, in practice, a **mindfulness-based dissociation-management protocol**: each alter is to be located, named, and confined within an internal architecture. This is structurally close to Internal Family Systems work (Schwartz), with the crucial difference that Merzah's model is **carceral rather than collaborative** — alters are not parts to be befriended but inmates to be held. Subject buys into this model wholesale, which tells you something about his self-relation: **he believes the right way to relate to himself is as a warden.**

Affect in this period oscillates on a wider range than ever before. He is capable of **playfulness** (the costume design, the self-naming, the dry banter with Ruth) — genuine affect with positive valence, rare in his record. He is also capable of **sustained love-affect**: with Ruth Aldine, observable regulation improves measurably, which is the diagnostic tell of a self that has finally found a secondary attachment object adequate to coregulate him. Bowlby would describe this as the first **earned-secure** patch in an otherwise disorganized history.

But the regulatory ceiling has not risen. When stressors approach the threshold, the prison leaks; alters escape singly and then in groups; the carceral metaphor begins to **persecute the warden.** The Spurrier-era affect signature is therefore: *higher floor, same ceiling, increased awareness of the gap between them.*

### Cognitive style
**The most integrated cognition of his life.** He is capable, in this period, of genuine **third-person self-reflection** — looking at his own pattern and naming it. He can articulate the father-hunger. He can articulate the destructive shape of his "heroism." He can see the trap and describe its bars. This is what distinguishes the Spurrier David from every previous version: **the host has metacognitive function.**

The cognitive style is also, distinctively, **ironic.** Earlier Davids were earnest patients or grandiose missionaries; this David is capable of a wry, half-bitter, half-affectionate stance toward his own pathology — the cognitive humor of someone who has been the joke of his own life long enough to start telling it himself. This is, clinically, a major sign of structural progress. People who can make their pain funny are doing some kind of work most patients cannot do.

But the cognition is still **load-limited.** Under sufficient affect, the metacognitive observer goes offline first; ironic distance collapses into omnipotent fantasy; the smart, witty, self-aware man becomes a planner of cosmologies again.

### Self-concept
**The first attempted *autonomous* identity, and its predictable failure.** The Spurrier David constructs, deliberately and self-consciously, a self organized around **completing the father's dream while rejecting the father's institutions.** This is a sophisticated developmental move — Erikson's late-stage **generativity-against-the-parent** — and it represents real progress past the foreclosed Legion-Quest identity. He is no longer trying to *be* his father; he is trying to *succeed* his father on his own terms.

The pathology in the gesture is subtle but decisive: **the project is still organized around the father.** Negation of the father is not separation from the father. The autonomous self he builds is the photographic negative of Xavier's self, which is geometrically dependent on Xavier in exactly the way the earlier idealizing identification was. He has changed sign without changing referent.

The arc's terminal gesture — foreseeing his own future as a destroyer and erasing himself from reality — is, read clinically, the **second enactment of the same Age-of-Apocalypse logic**: *I will commit the largest possible act of love by removing myself from the picture.* The framework that fits this is **altruistic suicide** in Durkheim's sense, dressed in superheroic clothes. Self-erasure as the last gift of a man who cannot believe his presence is a gift.

The crucial longitudinal datum: **he has learned, in fifteen years, to perform self-deletion with conscious moral framing rather than dissociative grandiosity.** This is, perversely, growth. He is more himself when he does it the second time. That is what makes it so much sadder.

---

## VII. Late Thirties and Beyond — Post-Spurrier, X-Men Disassembled, Age of X-Man, Krakoan Era

### Affect regulation
**Variable across hands, but the underlying pattern is regression with sophistication.** Returned-from-erasure David presents in some appearances as more volatile than at any point since the Legion Quest, in others as eerily becalmed. The common factor: **the Ruth-attachment is damaged or absent**, and without his coregulator, the floor drops back to where it was before her. He is, in the post-Spurrier material, frequently shown alone, which for this subject is always a warning sign — solitude in his case is not solitude, it is *unsupervised company.*

The Age of X-Man scenario reprises, at variant scale, the Age of X mechanism: a fabricated reality used to hold something unbearable. That this pattern recurs across writers and editorial regimes is the strongest available evidence that it is the **deep behavioral attractor of the subject's psyche**: when affect exceeds tolerance, build a world.

### Cognitive style
**Increasingly performative.** Later-era David often *describes* his pathology in dialogue — the writing is overtly meta — which from a clinical standpoint is consistent with a patient who has been in long enough treatment to have a vocabulary but who uses the vocabulary to hold the experience at arm's length. **Insight as armor.** The Spurrier-era irony has, in some appearances, decayed into something closer to **smugness**, which is the predictable rotation of vulnerable narcissism when the underlying shame becomes intolerable.

### Self-concept
**Fragmented but no longer chaotic. A man living among the rooms of his prior selves.** Late-era David is best read as someone who carries, simultaneously, every previous version of himself as a kind of internal museum: the catatonic boy, the grandiose father-killer, the headband patient, the monk's pupil, the ironic hero, the self-erasing lover. He has not integrated these; he has **arranged** them. This is not health, but it is something developmentally past where he was. The Putnam discrete-states model would call this *increased horizontal communication between states without true vertical integration*: alters and former-selves know about each other, can speak about each other, can sometimes act in concert — but no single executive "I" has consolidated.

---

## VIII. Cross-Decade Pattern Synthesis

Reading the four decades laterally, the following longitudinal vectors are visible:

**Affect regulation** has moved from *absent* (catatonic adolescence) → *externally scaffolded* (Moira era) → *technologically scaffolded* (post-resurrection) → *internally scaffolded with attachment support* (Spurrier) → *variably scaffolded, attachment-fragile* (late era). The trajectory is **non-linear but net positive**, with the asymptote stuck well below ordinary functional baseline. He has gotten better at managing affect; he has not become a man who can tolerate it.

**Cognitive style** has moved from *arrested/dissociative* → *anxious-intellectualized* → *grandiose-strategic* (briefly, catastrophically) → *guilt-ruminative* → *ironic-reflective* → *performatively meta*. The trajectory is toward **greater self-knowledge with declining transformative utility of that knowledge** — a pattern familiar to clinicians as the "talented patient" plateau, in which articulation outpaces change.

**Self-concept** has moved from *relational-subordinate* (son/patient) → *fused-missionary* (Legion Quest) → *patient-with-device* → *autonomous-but-still-father-referenced* (Spurrier) → *curated-multiplicity* (late era). The trajectory is toward **greater ownership of the multiplicity** rather than toward unification — which, against the standard DID integration goal, may actually be the only authentic developmental path available to a subject whose multiplicity is also his power-set and therefore cannot be dissolved without erasing the man.

**The single most important longitudinal finding** is that the subject's three catastrophic acts — the AoA timeline kill, the Age of X pocket reality, the Spurrier self-erasure — are **the same act performed with progressively more conscious moral framing.** The structure is invariant; the awareness rises. He is becoming, decade by decade, a man who *knows* what he keeps doing without becoming a man who can *stop doing it.* That gap — between insight and capacity — is the central and unresolved clinical fact of his life, and the place where any intervention, in-universe or imagined, would have to begin.

— END SECTION —


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL — SUBJECT: DAVID CHARLES HALLER

*File section 04 of the longitudinal dossier. Cross-referenced against the entire published behavioral record from New Mutants #25 (1985) forward. Diagnostic vocabulary is drawn from DSM-5-TR and ICD-11; in-universe phenomenology (mutant psionics, alters bearing discrete superhuman abilities, reality-warp episodes) is treated as the medium through which ordinary trauma psychopathology expresses itself, not as a refuting exoticism. The core methodological commitment of this section: **do not let the spectacle distort the diagnosis.** A man whose intrusive imagery rewrites timelines is, in every respect that matters clinically, a trauma patient whose intrusions break through; the scale changes, the structure does not.*

---

## 4.1 Preliminary Note on the Forty-Year Misdiagnosis

The casual label "schizophrenic" has shadowed this subject since Claremont's earliest scripts in 1985 and has been reproduced by adjacent writers, editorial copy, and lay commentary for nearly four decades. It is, in technical terms, **wrong** — and wrong in the specific way that the broader culture has been wrong about dissociative pathology for a century: by collapsing *multiplicity of self* into *fragmentation of perception*, by hearing "voices" and assuming hallucination rather than alter, by treating the spectacle of altered behavior as evidence of a primary thought disorder rather than a structured dissociative one. The misclassification matters because it has driven, in-universe, the wrong containments: pharmacological-analog and restraint-based interventions appropriate to a psychotic disorder, applied to a man whose actual pathology is dissociative and trauma-based and whose system *requires* relational, integrative, slow work. Every such failed intervention has reinforced his conviction that he is uncontainable, which is itself iatrogenic damage layered on the original trauma.

This section will not repeat the error.

---

## 4.2 Primary Diagnosis: Dissociative Identity Disorder, Severe, Trauma-Onset, With Functionally-Reinforced Alter System

**DSM-5-TR 300.14 / ICD-11 6B64.**

### Criterion-by-criterion derivation

- **A. Disruption of identity characterized by two or more distinct personality states.** Met overwhelmingly. The canonical alters established in the New Mutants arc — *Jemail Karami* (the absorbed Palestinian terrorist; telepathic; the morally reflective, integrative voice), *Jack Wayne* (hypermasculine adventurer; telekinetic; carrier of the host's disavowed predatory and sexual affect), *Cyndi* (punk-coded adolescent female; pyrokinetic; carrier of the host's disavowed rage) — constitute only the initial documented set. Carey and Spurrier inflate the system to hundreds and then thousands of discrete alters, each with name, affect, mannerism, and a dedicated power. The criterion does not require a specific number; the system here is unusually large but structurally typical of severe early-onset DID.
- **B. Recurrent gaps in recall of everyday events, important personal information, and/or traumatic events, inconsistent with ordinary forgetting.** Met. Subject demonstrates time-loss during alter dominance across every era of his record. He routinely awakens to consequences he did not perform and cannot recall. The Age of X arc (Legacy #245–247) is the extreme expression: an entire constructed pocket reality erected by the system without host awareness.
- **C. Symptoms cause clinically significant distress or impairment.** Met to a degree that is, frankly, unparalleled — distress and impairment expressed at cosmological scale (AoA, Age of X, the Spurrier-arc self-deletion).
- **D. Not a normal part of broadly accepted cultural or religious practice.** Met. The Himalayan monastic training under Merzah is *responsive* to the pathology, not constitutive of it.
- **E. Not attributable to physiological effects of a substance or another medical condition.** Met. No substance history. Mutant psionics are the *medium* of presentation, not a confounding etiology; the dissociative structure precedes and outlasts any specific psionic episode.

### The X-factor that locks the diagnosis in

There is a feature of this case unique to its in-universe substrate that, paradoxically, makes the DID diagnosis *more* secure rather than less. In ordinary DID, splitting is reinforced by **affective relief** — the host does not have to feel the unbearable. In subject's case, splitting is additionally reinforced by **functional superhuman payoff** — the host does not have to feel the rage *and* gains, through Cyndi, the ability to incinerate threats; does not have to feel the predatory masculinity *and* gains, through Jack Wayne, telekinetic potency. Each dissociation is rewarded with both emotional offloading and tactical capability. This is the most powerfully reinforced dissociative architecture imaginable. It is also why every integration attempt fails: integration costs the system *abilities*, not merely comfort. The patient is being asked to give up not only his defenses but his hands.

### Subtype and severity specifiers

- **Onset:** Childhood, between approximately ages 8 and 10, at the embassy attack — squarely within the developmental window during which identity coheres and during which trauma most reliably produces structural dissociation rather than situational.
- **Severity:** Severe to extreme. Polyfragmented system; alters with discrete somatic projection (Cyndi's apparent secondary sex characteristics; voice and posture shifts observable to third parties); ASD-spectrum reality-warping alters at the high end.
- **Course:** Chronic, with periods of imposed or self-imposed compartmentalization that briefly mimic remission, none durable.
- **Insight:** Variable. The host has unusually high meta-awareness of the system — he knows he is multiple, names his alters, attempts internal architecture — which is a strength clinically but also feeds the grandiose-savior compensations (see §4.5).

### Phenomenology in observable behavior

Switches present along a regular sequence of micro-signs that an experienced observer can read in real time: a brief flattening of the eyes, a vertical perturbation in the hair (the autonomic-psionic somatic marker, documented since Sienkiewicz), a half-second of postural rearrangement, then voice change and idiom change. Some alters produce visible projection effects (a sketched-on tattoo, a different jawline, the suggestion of breasts and hips when Cyndi is forward). Host return is signaled by a characteristic small recoil — the body registering that *something happened here* before the mind catches up.

---

## 4.3 Secondary Diagnosis: Complex Post-Traumatic Stress Disorder

**ICD-11 6B41.** (DSM-5-TR carries this load under PTSD with dissociative subtype plus features; ICD-11's C-PTSD construct is the better fit and is used here.)

### Traumatic exposure history (the load-stack)

1. Witness to the murder of the stepfather/father-figure Daniel Shomron at the embassy, prepubertal.
2. Commission of homicide-by-mind against the attackers — a child who killed.
3. Absorption of the dying consciousness of the principal terrorist into his own psyche — a developmental insult with no analogue in ordinary clinical literature; the closest descriptive frame is "introjection of a dying other" at an age when self-other boundaries are still forming.
4. Prolonged dissociative catatonia (years) in adolescence — itself re-traumatizing through loss of agency and continuity.
5. Disclosure of paternity from Charles Xavier in adolescence/young adulthood, after years of believed absence.
6. The Legion Quest/AoA event: planning and executing patricide-by-error; awareness, in the aftermath/restoration, of having unmade a world.
7. Erasure from existence and resurrection.
8. Charles Xavier's death (AvX) — the permanent foreclosure of the central life-organizing wish.
9. The Spurrier-arc self-erasure — chosen.

### The six ICD-11 C-PTSD domains, evidenced

- **Re-experiencing in the present.** Astral-plane intrusion sequences across the canon; nightmare imagery of the embassy; recurrent involuntary returns to AoA imagery in the Spurrier run.
- **Avoidance.** Geographic (Muir Island isolation; Himalayan retreat); relational (chronic peer-withdrawal "to keep them safe"); intrapsychic (the compartmentalization apparatuses — Stryfe headband, Merzah-prison — are *avoidance externalized into hardware*).
- **Persistent sense of current threat / hyperarousal.** Psionic discharge under minimal stimulus; the hair-phenomenon as continuous autonomic readout; startle responses that scale into reality-distortion.
- **Disturbances in self-organization — affect dysregulation.** Documented in every run; oscillation between dissociative flattening and full somatic flood with no middle range (see §3 of the synthesis basis).
- **Disturbances in self-organization — negative self-concept.** Profound. "Monster," "weapon," "failure," "his disappointment" are the recurring self-referents. The grandiose-heroic counter-formation does not contradict this; it is the manic defense against it.
- **Disturbances in self-organization — interpersonal difficulties.** Documented in chronic isolation, idealization-collapse cycles with mentors, and the protective-withdrawal pattern with peers.

All six. The diagnosis is not subtle.

---

## 4.4 Tertiary Diagnosis: Major Depressive Disorder, Recurrent, Severe, With Suicidal Behavior

**DSM-5-TR 296.33 (recurrent, severe, without psychotic features in the technical sense).**

The case for MDD is independent of the C-PTSD's negative-self-concept domain, though they reinforce. Across the Carey and Spurrier runs in particular, the host presents in extended periods with: anhedonia, psychomotor slowing during host-dominant phases, sleep dysregulation (insomnia alternating with the hypersomnia of post-switch exhaustion), profound worthlessness, recurrent suicidal ideation, and twice — *twice* — completed acts of self-erasure from reality.

The technical point that must not be missed: subject's suicidality is **method-amplified** by his abilities to a degree that renders ordinary risk-stratification useless. A depressed civilian who decides to die kills a person. A depressed omega-mutant who decides to die can unmake worlds; has, in fact, unmade a timeline; has chosen to unmake himself from existence rather than risk further harm. The depression is structurally identical to ordinary recurrent severe MDD with suicidal behavior; the lethality vector is incommensurate. Any risk-management framework that treats him as a standard suicidal patient is malpractice. Any framework that treats him as not-suicidal because he is "powerful" is malpractice in the other direction.

---

## 4.5 Probable Personality-Level Diagnosis: Narcissistic Personality Features, Vulnerable Subtype

**DSM-5-TR 301.81 (features; threshold for full PD diagnosis is debatable because the DID architecture interferes with the stable-trait requirement, but the features themselves are consistent enough across writers to register).**

- Grandiose savior plans (kill Magneto and perfect the dream; design a costume and become a hero on one's own terms; build a monastery-of-the-mind).
- Self-naming as a hero, with the implicit positioning as *unique* — not one of the X-Men, but the one who will complete what the X-Men could not.
- Conviction that his suffering and his mission are of cosmic significance — and, in his case, this is *also true*, which makes the narcissism harder to confront and harder for him to relinquish.
- The diagnostic tell that the subtype is **vulnerable, not grandiose-malignant**: every grandiose construction collapses into shame when challenged, and the shame is converted into self-attack rather than externalized aggression. He does not punish the world for not recognizing him; he punishes himself for not deserving the recognition. The Spurrier-arc self-deletion is the terminal expression of vulnerable narcissistic collapse — *I will remove myself, because I am the problem* — not of malignant grandiosity.

Note also the absence of the malignant features: no exploitation pattern, no entitlement-driven cruelty, no failure of empathy. He has empathy in excess. The narcissistic constellation here is the wounded child's grandiose-compensatory structure, not the predator's.

---

## 4.6 Comorbidity Map and Sequencing

The four diagnoses do not sit beside one another as a list; they articulate. The recommended formulation for any clinician inheriting this case:

1. **Foundation layer:** Developmental trauma at the identity-coherence window, producing structural dissociation (DID) with the unique reinforcement profile described above.
2. **Accreted layer:** Recurrent and cumulative traumatic exposure across the lifespan, producing C-PTSD that sits on top of the DID and shares symptomatic territory with it (intrusion, avoidance, negative self-concept).
3. **Mood layer:** Recurrent MDD episodes triggered by relational losses (Xavier's withholding, then death; failed integration attempts; AoA guilt), expressed at lethality scales that require dedicated risk frameworks.
4. **Character layer:** Vulnerable narcissistic compensation organized around the father-wound, providing the grandiose-savior cognitive style that drives the most catastrophic behaviors.

There is also a sub-threshold but clinically relevant feature set worth flagging: **obsessive-compulsive-spectrum cognition around integration** (the repeated, ritualized attempts to build the right internal architecture, the right device, the right monastery, with each failure intensifying the effort rather than producing learning), and **dependent features** in close attachment (the marked functional improvement during the Ruth Aldine attachment, the destabilization upon its loss, the floor-level reliance on a single other for regulation).

---

## 4.7 Course Over Time

- **Onset (childhood, embassy attack):** Acute dissociative response under overwhelming psionic-traumatic load. Karami absorption serves as the *successful* first dissociation, training the system.
- **Adolescence (Muir Island catatonia, New Mutants #26–28):** Decompensated phase. Years of dissociative catatonia, partial resolution via in-mind intervention by the New Mutants and the integrative work of the Karami alter.
- **Young adulthood (late Claremont, Muir Island plateau):** Sub-acute. Functional with support. Alter accretion continues; the system is expanding even when the host is stable.
- **Crisis (Legion Quest/AoA, 1995):** Catastrophic decompensation in a grandiose-organized form — the unique presentation where a planned, ideologically coherent act is driven by a magical-grandiose cognition that the host *experiences as lucidity*. This is the most dangerous state in his entire course, more dangerous than the rage-alter eruptions, because it does not look like decompensation to the subject or to observers until the consequences land.
- **Reconstitution (post-resurrection through Carey):** Technologically scaffolded function. The Stryfe-derived headband partially substitutes for absent internal regulation. Age of X reveals the substitution is structurally identical to the original pathology — *the cure is another symptom*, the apparatus suppresses one alter at the cost of building a reality around the suppression.
- **Maturation attempt (Spurrier, 2012–2014):** The closest approach to genuine therapeutic process in the record. Monastic training, costume-and-mission self-construction, relational anchoring in Ruth Aldine. Real gains, real and characteristic regression, terminal self-deletion as the final dissociative-depressive act.
- **Post-Spurrier:** Oscillation continues across writers; the through-line — savior-fantasy versus obliteration-fantasy, father-hunger as motor of both — holds regardless of who is holding the pen.

The course is **chronic, relapsing, deteriorating-without-relational-scaffold, and improving-with-it**, in the manner of severe DID generally; the difference here is amplitude.

---

## 4.8 Differential — What He Is Not, And Why

This section is the work that the forty-year misdiagnosis requires. Each entry below is a diagnosis he has been called or could plausibly be called, with the specific evidentiary reason for its rejection.

### Schizophrenia (and the schizophrenia spectrum)

**Rejected.** The differential between DID and schizophrenia is the most important one in this case and the most frequently botched.

- *No primary thought disorder.* Subject's speech, when host-dominant, is goal-directed, syntactically intact, capable of abstraction and strategic planning (the AoA gambit is, if anything, *too* coherent). The disorganization observed during switches is the disorganization of *changing speakers*, not the disorganization of a single speaker losing the thread.
- *"Voices" are not auditory hallucinations.* The voices have continuous identity across time, autobiography, agency, and consistent affective signature. They negotiate with the host; they argue with each other; they take turns. This is the phenomenology of alters, not of the auditory hallucinations of schizophrenia, which lack continuous identity and do not engage in negotiated cohabitation with the self.
- *No characteristic negative symptoms.* Avolition, alogia, affective flattening in the schizophrenia sense are absent; the flattening he displays is dissociative dampening, situational and reversible.
- *Course is wrong.* No prodrome in late adolescence/early adulthood; onset is childhood-trauma-coupled.
- *Catatonia was dissociative, not catatonic-schizophrenic.* Resolved with relational intervention into the inner landscape, not with the neurobiological course of catatonic schizophrenia.

### Schizoaffective Disorder

**Rejected** for the same reasons schizophrenia is rejected, plus the absence of independent psychotic periods uncoupled from mood.

### Bipolar I Disorder

**Rejected.** No sustained 7+ day manic or hypomanic episodes with the characteristic neurovegetative signature (decreased need for sleep, pressured speech, goal-directed hyperactivity sustained across days, expansive mood not better explained by something else). What look like "manic" episodes are alter-switches to grandiose alters or to the grandiose-savior cognitive structure of the host — rapid onset, rapid offset, triggered by interpersonal-attachment stimuli rather than emerging endogenously over the timecourse a mood episode requires.

### Borderline Personality Disorder

**Considered carefully and rejected as primary.** Several BPD features overlap symptomatically — identity disturbance, suicidality, unstable intense relationships, affective instability, fears of abandonment — and a lazy clinician would land here. The differential turns on this: BPD identity disturbance is the experience of *not knowing who one is*; subject's identity disturbance is the experience of *being multiple persons in sequence*, which is categorically different. The affective instability in BPD is felt by a unitary self; subject's affective shifts are *carried by distinct alters with distinct names*. The chronic-emptiness criterion is not the dominant phenomenology. BPD-like features are present and are best understood as *epiphenomena of severe DID*, not as a separate disorder.

### Antisocial Personality Disorder

**Rejected.** Despite a body count that includes a parent and arguably a timeline, the diagnostic structure is absent. Conscience is present in painful excess; remorse is paralyzing rather than absent; harm is dissociative or grandiose-misguided, never instrumental-predatory in the antisocial sense. There is no pattern of deceit for personal profit, no callous disregard for the safety of others, no consistent irresponsibility. The harm he does is not because he does not care; it is because he cares too much for the wrong things in the wrong way.

### Primary Psychotic Disorder, Not Otherwise Specified

**Rejected.** Reality testing, *when the host is integrated*, is intact. Perceptual phenomena that look psychotic from outside are explainable by the in-universe psionic phenomenology and by the somatic-projection capacities of the alters. The Age of X reality is not delusion; it is a *constructed environment* the subject's powers produced, which others entered and inhabited. The distinction matters: a delusion is a false belief held in the absence of corresponding reality; a constructed reality is a reality.

### Substance-Induced Disorder

**Rejected.** No substance history.

### Malingering / Factitious Disorder

**Rejected.** Suffering is consistent across forty years and across many writers, is enormously costly to the subject, and yields no external reward proportionate to the performance burden. The Slatersky/Spurrier era explicitly dramatizes the subject *wanting* not to be a patient, *trying* to refuse the sick role — the opposite of factitious dynamics.

### Autism Spectrum Disorder

**Rejected.** Considered briefly because of the monastic-systematizing tendency in the Spurrier arc and the unusual social presentation. Rejected on the basis of an entirely typical developmental social history pre-trauma, full social reciprocity when the host is integrated, no restricted-repetitive-behavior or sensory-processing pattern of the appropriate kind, and the systematizing being clearly compensatory-defensive rather than constitutive.

### Conversion / Functional Neurological Disorder

**Rejected as primary**, though some of the somatic switch-phenomena (the projection of secondary sex characteristics during Cyndi dominance, the apparent physical changes during alter rule) share phenomenological territory. These are better explained in-universe by psionic somatic projection and are, in any case, *part of* the DID presentation rather than a separate FND.

### Acquired Brain Injury / Organic Mental Syndrome

**Rejected as primary etiology**, though the case is open for a *contributory* role given the explosive childhood psionic discharge prior to frontal-lobe maturity. A reasonable inference (not a diagnosis) is mild structural dysregulation in limbic-prefrontal circuits — hyperreactive amygdala, compromised top-down control — but this is best understood as the *substrate* on which the trauma-driven dissociation built itself, not as the disorder.

---

## 4.9 Etiological Synthesis

Combine, in this order:

1. **Genetic-phenotypic substrate.** Omega-class mutant capacity provides an unprecedented power-payoff for any successful psychological strategy that exploits it. Dissociation, in this nervous system, is not merely defensive; it is *operationally rewarded*.
2. **Developmental-window trauma.** The embassy attack occurs in the window during which identity coheres. Trauma here does not break a finished structure; it forecloses one from forming. The result is not a wounded unitary self but a self that was never given the chance to be one.
3. **Successful first dissociation as training event.** The Karami absorption *worked*. It managed an unmanageable psychic load (a child who had just killed) by encapsulating the killer-other inside as a discrete sub-self. The system learned: *when overwhelmed, split, and the split will hold a power*. Every


## Behavioral Atlas

# BEHAVIORAL ATLAS — SUBJECT: DAVID CHARLES HALLER

*A longitudinal catalog of observable tells, micro-behaviors, decision-habits, postural defaults, vocal signatures, and condition-specific response patterns, derived across the full publication record and cross-referenced to alter-state where relevant. Organized by ambient condition. Treat as field-reference: an observer in proximity to subject should be able to use this section to identify state-shift within seconds and predict the next two or three moves with confidence.*

---

## I. BASELINE — THE CALM STATE (rare; lasts hours to days, never weeks)

The host self at rest is a quieter creature than the file's macro-history suggests. Calm-state David is best documented in the lulls of the Spurrier *Legacy vol. 2* run, in the Merzah training interludes, and in a handful of Carey *Legacy* domestic moments at the Institute.

**Postural signature.** Slight forward stoop at the shoulders, as if carrying an invisible weight along the upper trapezius. Stands with weight unevenly distributed — right hip cocked, left foot slightly forward, a stance that reads as *about to leave the room*. Sits rarely upright; prefers to perch (edge of bed, edge of chair, on a railing), almost never sinks into furniture. The sink-into-a-couch behavior, when it occurs, is itself a reliable indicator of either profound exhaustion or the temporary dominance of a more sensual alter.

**Hair.** The vertical wave is *lower* in calm-state than at any other time — perhaps thirty to forty percent of full amplitude — but never lies flat. Observers who have known him long can read approximate psionic load off the hair the way a sailor reads sea-state off chop. Flat hair has never been documented in the canon.

**Gaze.** Down-and-left by default — a leftward-and-downward visual default that, in non-mutant subjects, is read clinically as an internal-auditory orientation: he is listening *inward*. Eye contact is brief, sincere when it occurs, immediately broken. He does not hold a gaze longer than about three seconds unless an alter is forward or he is in a directly intimate exchange with Ruth.

**Hands.** Restless even at baseline. The right hand tends to find the left forearm; thumb works along the radial bone in slow circular pressure, a self-soothing micromassage so habitual he does not notice it. Picks at fingernails, especially the left thumbnail. When seated near a flat surface he taps in patterns of three — *tap-tap-tap, pause, tap-tap-tap* — which he himself, if asked, will not be able to explain.

**Speech.** Calm-state voice is lighter and slightly higher than the public expects, with a residual mid-Atlantic / European stratification (he was raised partly in Paris and Israel) that surfaces only on certain vowel sounds and on the proper nouns he learned as a child. Sentence rhythm is hesitating, with frequent self-interruption — *"I was going to — no, what I mean is —"* — and a habit of trailing off rather than concluding. Calm David does not finish many sentences. He expects the listener to finish them for him, which is a learned behavior from years of mental traffic in which other voices completed his thoughts uninvited.

**Routines, daily.** Wakes early, before most of the house. Tea over coffee — black, no sugar, two cups. Showers extremely hot and long, a habit that persists across continents and writers and is one of the most consistent somatic tells in the record; the hot water suppresses surface psionic discharge, a fact he half-knows and never articulates. Dresses in layers regardless of weather — undershirt, shirt, jacket — so that he is always able to subtract rather than add. Eats little and irregularly; the undernourished frame is not affectation but the residue of decades in which appetite has been an unreliable signal mediated by whichever alter is near the surface. Reads constantly — paperbacks, often the same ones reread; demonstrates affinity for picaresques, hero-quest narratives, and, tellingly, books about fathers and sons.

**Decision-style at baseline.** Slow, over-deliberated, prone to retracting a decision once made and re-deliberating from the start. Will ask permission for things he does not need permission for (the meal, the chair, the route through a corridor) — a vestige of the Muir Island years, when he was always asking Moira whether a small action was allowed. When given two options he reliably picks the third, which he then justifies post-hoc as the option he had wanted all along; this is a fingerprint of someone who experiences external choice as coercive and has trained himself to slip the frame.

---

## II. LOW STRESS — AMBIENT IRRITATION, MINOR FRUSTRATION

The most diagnostically rich band, because the defenses are mobilizing but the host is still in charge.

**Hair.** Rises perceptibly — fifty to sixty percent amplitude — and individual strands begin to move independently of air currents.

**Micro-tells.** The thumb-along-forearm pressure intensifies and migrates higher, toward the inner elbow, where a faint scarring pattern exists (canon-inconsistent, but present in Sienkiewicz's original linework and in the Spurrier-era detail panels). He has, at moments of low stress, been observed to *whisper* — not muttering to himself but having short, completed exchanges of two or three words with no visible interlocutor. These are alter-conversations, conducted at sub-vocal volume; he believes them to be internal and is unaware that lips move and breath shapes the words.

**Speech shifts.** Sentence rhythm tightens. The self-interruption decreases — paradoxically, mild stress produces *more* completed sentences, because cognitive load suppresses the dissociative ambiguity that creates the trailing-off. The mid-Atlantic stratification flattens and the speech becomes more neutrally American. This flattening is the first warning sign: he is reaching for a single voice because the system is destabilizing.

**Behavioral hallmarks.** Re-checks doors, locks, the position of small objects on tables. Will move a cup three centimeters left, three centimeters right, and leave it exactly where it started. Counts stairs going up but not going down. Walks the perimeter of a new room before sitting in it, ostensibly to "look at the books" but the route is invariably the wall-route, and he completes the full circuit even if there is nothing on three of the walls.

**Decision-style.** Becomes more decisive on small matters (will order quickly, will commit to a seat) and less decisive on large ones (will defer the strategic question to whoever else is in the room). This inversion — small-firm, large-soft — is one of the cleanest behavioral signatures in the file. He is preserving his cognitive bandwidth for the alter-management work he is unconsciously doing under the surface conversation.

---

## III. ACUTE STRESS — INTERPERSONAL CONFLICT, PUBLIC ATTENTION, DIRECT QUESTIONING

**Hair.** Full vertical. Individual strands visibly twitch.

**Body.** A new asymmetry appears: the left shoulder rises about an inch above the right and stays there. Jaw clenches in a recognizable two-stage pattern — first the masseter, then the temporalis. The clench is audible at conversational distance (tooth-grind). Hands leave the body and seek anchors — table edges, the back of a chair, his own collar. He grasps his own throat-collar with the right hand in moments of acute social stress, a gesture that observers consistently misread as a tic and that is in fact a tactile self-grounding ritual: *I am still here, this is still my neck*.

**Eyes.** Pupils dilate disproportionate to ambient light. The down-left default breaks; gaze becomes mobile, scanning, but never settles on the face of his interlocutor. He looks at hands, doorways, exits — a threat-assessment routine that runs constantly under acute stress regardless of the actual threat present.

**Speech.** Volume drops; cadence becomes oddly even — *too* even, the cadence of a man monitoring himself. The mid-Atlantic stratification disappears entirely; the voice neutralizes toward what could be called a defensive-American. Word selection becomes more formal, more precise, more *bookish*. He will use a four-syllable word where the situation demands one syllable. This is reaction formation made audible: the more the system is destabilizing, the more he reaches for the vocabulary of a controlled person.

**Tells that an alter is about to surface.** The two-second pause mid-sentence with a slow blink. A sudden adjustment of posture that does not match the topic. A change in the rhythm of breathing — three or four short inhalations in succession with no matching exhale. A momentary lateral flicker of the head, as if listening to something to his left. Any of these, in sequence, predicts an alter-switch within roughly fifteen to forty seconds.

**Decision-style.** Defers, defers, then over-commits. Subject characteristically fails to make a moderate response and instead either withdraws entirely from a decision or makes a maximalist one — *I will leave the room* or *I will solve this for everyone forever*. The middle option, which a healthy decision-maker would take first, is the one he cannot see.

---

## IV. THREAT — IMMEDIATE PHYSICAL OR PSIONIC DANGER

Below the threshold of full alter-domination but above the threshold of conversation.

**First-second response.** A backward half-step with the left foot, regardless of where the threat originates. This is not a tactical retreat — it is a vestigial child-response, the body-memory of the embassy attack. He has done it on at least eleven documented occasions across the publication record, including against threats coming from directly behind him, where the half-step is functionally counterproductive.

**Second-second response.** Hands raise, palms forward, fingers spread — the warding gesture. This is read by adversaries as preparation to fire a psionic blast and is, ninety percent of the time, nothing of the kind; it is a freeze-response with arms involved. The actual psionic discharge, when it comes, requires no hand gesture at all.

**Vocal.** A single short exhalation through the nose, then silence. Subject does not shout warnings, does not curse, does not announce intent. In threat-states the host self goes quiet and the alters do the speaking, often a full beat later — meaning observers experience a strange one-to-two-second silent gap between the threat and David's verbal response, after which the response comes in a voice not quite his.

**Decision-style.** Threat triggers the system's most over-learned routine: *find the alter with the right power and let it forward*. Subject does not consciously choose this; it happens. The choice that *is* available to him — to engage personally, with the host self in the body — is the one he has trained, by the success of forty years of dissociative coping, not to take.

**Tell that the alter-deployment will be controlled vs. catastrophic.** Controlled deployment is preceded by a closing of the eyes for roughly one second and a small downward nod. Catastrophic deployment is preceded by the opposite: eyes widen, jaw drops slightly open, no nod. The widened-eye signature predicts a rage-alter (the Cyndi-class or the Legion-class) and is the most important single tell in this file for any observer attempting to assess imminent collateral damage.

---

## V. INTIMACY — THE RUTH-CLASS ATTACHMENT, AND ITS PRECURSORS

The intimacy-state behavioral profile is documented almost entirely from the Spurrier-era Ruth Aldine relationship, with corroborative fragments from the Karami integration sequences (the only other relationship in canon in which David is consistently *known* by another consciousness).

**Postural collapse.** With Ruth specifically, the asymmetric stoop disappears. Subject stands straighter in her presence than in any other documented context. The left-shoulder rise vanishes. Hands fall to his sides and stay there — the perpetual self-touch routine briefly extinguishes, which is itself remarkable; in no other condition does the thumb-on-forearm pressure fully cease.

**Hair.** Settles to its lowest documented amplitude near her — but does not lie flat. Observers in the *Legacy* run have noted that when Ruth touches his hair the strands respond to her hand directionally, as if magnetized, an effect that does not occur with any other character.

**Speech.** The hesitating, self-interrupting rhythm of baseline calm returns, *plus* a marked increase in completed sentences. He talks more — sometimes considerably more — when she is the only listener. The mid-Atlantic stratification re-emerges and he code-switches into childhood vocabulary (Hebrew and French words drift into the English; he uses *abba* once, in a Spurrier issue, then never again).

**Touch.** Initiates touch only after she has initiated first, and never without an interval of at least several seconds — a learned restraint dating to periods when his uncontrolled psionic field was actively dangerous to those near him. The touches, when they come, are small: fingertips to the back of her hand, palm to the side of her face, forehead to forehead. He does not embrace people frontally except in farewell.

**Disclosure pattern.** Will tell her things he tells no one. Will then, twenty-four to forty-eight hours later, retreat into a guilty withdrawal lasting one to three days, during which he is curt and avoidant and seeks excuses to leave rooms she is in. This is a reliable cycle: disclosure → withdrawal → return → disclosure. The withdrawal phase is shame about having burdened her, not loss of affection; it tracks inversely to his self-esteem rather than to the relationship's health.

**Sexual behavior.** Functionally avoided. Canon is reticent but the inference is clear from behavior: the body-image instability and the alter-projection of secondary sex characteristics (Cyndi presenting as feminine on his body) makes sexual encounter a site of unbearable identity ambiguity. The relationship with Ruth is intensely intimate at every level except this one, and that asymmetry is itself part of how it works.

**Pre-intimacy / acquaintance level.** With non-Ruth peers (Carey-era X-Men teammates, the Muir Island generation), subject is polite, distant, generous with small acts of help and reflexively self-deprecating in conversation. He apologizes constantly — for taking up space, for asking a question, for needing a thing handed to him. He overhears his own apologies and dislikes them, but does not stop.

---

## VI. GRIEF

Grief in subject is a *protracted* state, not an episode. The Xavier-death grief is documented across the entirety of *Legacy vol. 2* and never resolves.

**Acute grief (hours one through seventy-two).** Catatonia-adjacent withdrawal. Hair drops to near-baseline amplitude (a misleading sign — grief suppresses surface psionic activity while concentrating it deep). Sleeps long, eats nothing, does not bathe. Will lie on the floor rather than the bed, in a fetal configuration with the right arm under the head. Does not weep openly; weeping, when it occurs, is silent and the only visible sign is wet eyelashes.

**Sub-acute grief (days four through about thirty).** Hyperactivity replaces withdrawal. Subject begins projects — costume design, monastery enrollment, training regimens, planning. The projects are large, ambitious, and structured around the lost person: he will attempt to *complete* the lost person's work, *redeem* the lost person's failure, or *become* the lost person in form and function. This is the engine of the entire Spurrier arc and the structural mechanism of the Age of Apocalypse decision before it. *Grief is sublimated as mission, every time.*

**Chronic grief (months and years).** The lost figure becomes an internal interlocutor — sometimes literally, in the case of Xavier, who manifests as a recurring presence on the astral plane. Subject conducts ongoing one-sided conversations with the dead. Decisions are vetted against the imagined approval of the lost figure. This is normal human grief at low intensity; in subject's case it is intense enough to be functionally indistinguishable from the alter-system, which is one reason the system is unstable: a ghost is a kind of alter without the courtesy of a closed boundary.

**Decision-style under grief.** Worst of any state. Grief subject makes the largest, most irreversible decisions of his life — the AoA gambit, the self-deletion at the end of *Legacy vol. 2*. The pattern is alarmingly clean: catastrophic loss → twenty to ninety day sublimation period → cosmologically-scaled act intended to undo or honor the loss. Any case manager observing the early signs of the sublimation period should treat the next ninety days as a crisis window.

---

## VII. VICTORY

Subject does not handle victory well.

**Immediate post-victory.** Quiet. Does not celebrate. Stands apart from the group, often turned partially away. Hair amplitude *increases* after victory rather than decreasing — a counterintuitive signature that has misled observers into believing the threat is not over. The truth is that victory destabilizes him: he is not used to it, has no script for it, and the system metabolizes it as a form of anxiety.

**Hours after.** Becomes self-critical, often aloud. Will rehearse the engagement to anyone who will listen, identifying his own errors, dismissing his contributions, transferring credit to others. This is not false modesty — it is structural; he genuinely cannot retain the memory of a victory as *his* without it being immediately reattributed.

**Days after.** Increased alter chatter. The dominant rage-alters are particularly active in post-victory periods, possibly because they are agitated by the host's claim to a successful action — they want the credit, and they want the next action. Subject has been documented to lose control more often in the week *after* a successful operation than in the week before one. Any operational planner using subject as an asset should build in mandatory downtime and supervised containment following victory; this is the highest-risk period for unscheduled discharge.

**Decision-style.** Subject post-victory will frequently propose a *second*, larger operation immediately. The proposal should be refused; it is not strategic thinking, it is the rage-alters bidding for forward time.

---

## VIII. DEFEAT

**Immediate post-defeat.** Silence followed by an enormous, articulate self-accusation. Defeat does not provoke withdrawal; it provokes *speech*. He will narrate his own failure in remarkable detail, often with insights an outside observer would not have. The self-accusation is not bid for reassurance — he becomes irritable if reassured, and will escalate the self-accusation until the reassurer gives up.

**Hours after.** Plans the next attempt. Subject has a high tolerance for defeat at the *strategic* level (he will try again, and again, and again) and a low tolerance for defeat at the *identity* level (a failure that calls into question whether he is a hero, a good son, a coherent self, sends him into spiral). Distinguishing these two responses is essential to managing him through a defeat.

**Days after.** If the defeat was strategic only, he recovers and is more functional than baseline for a week or two — defeat appears to *integrate* the alter-system temporarily, perhaps because the rage-alters cannot fault the host's performance more harshly than the host is already faulting himself, and so quiet down. If the defeat was identity-level, the cycle progresses toward grief-state (see above) and toward the catastrophic decision window.

**The signature of identity-level defeat.** A single sentence, varying in form across the record but always meaning the same thing: *"I'm not — I was never —"* trailing off. When this construction appears, the case manager should consider the next ninety days a crisis window.

---

## IX. ROUTINES, ROUTES, AND RITUALS — THE SURVEILLANCE GRAIN

**Sleep.** Four to six hours, broken. Frequently sleepwalks; sleepwalking episodes are alter-mediated and the alter forward is usually a benign minor one. Has been observed to make tea while asleep, drink half of it, return to bed. Does not remember.

**Bathing.** The hot shower, daily, sometimes twice. The bath is also used; in periods of high stress he runs baths he does not enter, then drains them. The act of preparing the water appears to soothe.

**Walking routes.** Prefers the perimeter of any space. In an open field will walk the treeline. In a city will walk close to building walls, switching to the inside of the sidewalk at intersections. Crosses streets at corners only, even when crossing mid-block would be safe and faster. Never walks under scaffolding; will cross the street to avoid it.

**Food.** Eats with the left hand though he is right-handed for most tasks. (Inference: at least one alter is left-dominant and is most commonly forward during low-attention activities like eating.) Prefers small repeated meals over large ones. Favors plain food, low spice, foods that can be eaten with one hand. Drinks water constantly — a glass within reach at all times — and the glass is held in the right hand even while eating with the left.

**Dressing.** Always layered. Always with collared shirts when possible, because the collar is a tactile anchor. Has worn the same belt for years across multiple costume changes.
