The smallest register, and the most operationally consequential. Subject has accumulated one durable adult attachment of record. The brevity of the list is itself a finding — Section 3 notes the capacity for love is genuine, but the *bandwidth* is one channel wide.

### 1. Ruth Aldine (Blindfold)

**History.** Precognitive, faceless beneath the bangs, soft-spoken in a recursive grammatical pattern (the run-on apologetic clauses are diagnostic of her own trauma history, not relevant to subject's file except as context for compatibility). They meet in the Carey *Legacy* period; the relationship deepens across Spurrier's *Legacy vol. 2* into the only fully reciprocated intimate bond on subject's record.

**Dynamics.** Ruth is the *one person who can perceive subject without the perceptual artifact of the alters*. Her precognition shows her the trajectory; her blindness (literal absence of eyes; psychic sight only) means she does not see the hair, the switching musculature, the shifting voices as *separations* — she sees a single continuous person whose surface is in motion. This is, for subject, the first experience on record of being *seen as one*. The therapeutic effect is enormous and entirely unreplicable by clinical method.

She, in turn, is treated by subject with a care that is uncharacteristic across the rest of his interpersonal record: he modulates voice, controls the hair phenomena to the extent he can, screens alter intrusions actively, and — most tellingly — *consults her* on decisions, which he does with no other person. The Karami alter approves of her; Cyndi tolerates her, which is Cyndi's version of approval; the Legion-alter regards her as a strategic threat, correctly.

**Evolution.** Begins as mutual recognition between two patients in an institution that cannot really treat either of them. Deepens through shared work in the field. Stabilizes into something subject explicitly names as love, with difficulty, on the page. Is interrupted by his self-deletion at the close of the Spurrier arc — and the *form* of the interruption is itself diagnostic: he removes himself rather than risk harming her, which is the Section 3 pattern (relational withdrawal disguised as protecting others), elevated this time to the cosmological scale he uses for all his largest gestures.

**Trust / safety.** The highest the file records. Subject sleeps in Ruth's vicinity with measurably reduced alter activity (visible in art as flatter hair and stable facial line through nighttime panels). The somatic markers do not lie: this is the only relationship in which his nervous system stands down.

**Failure mode.** Threat to Ruth converts subject instantly to stress level 4. He cannot calibrate response when she is the object. The Spurrier finale evidences the inverse failure: he does not trust his own *future* in proximity to her enough to remain, and chooses absence over risk. Either pole — her endangerment, or his own forecasted danger to her — produces escalation that bypasses every other regulation strategy.

**Leverage.** Total. Any actor who controls access to Ruth controls subject. This must be treated, in any operational framing of the file, as the central vulnerability that all other vulnerabilities are subordinate to. Inversely: any therapeutic program for subject that does not route through Ruth (or, post-Ruth, through whatever successor attachment ever forms, which the record suggests will not) is operating without the only known stabilizer.

### 2. Karami (intra-psychic intimate)

**History.** The absorbed terrorist, present continuously since age 8–10. Not a lover; an intimate in the precise sense that he is the longest-tenured continuous consciousness in proximity to subject's host self.

**Dynamics.** Karami is, paradoxically, the moral conscience of the system — the alter most likely to argue subject down from grandiose plans, to broker peace between other alters, to attempt, repeatedly, to integrate. The relationship has the texture of a long, weary marriage between two men neither of whom chose the arrangement and both of whom have made it work.

**Evolution.** Across decades, Karami has grown into something between elder brother, conscience, and house-spirit. His voice surfacing audibly to others is one of the most reliable signs that subject is in a *manageable* crisis rather than an unmanageable one. When Karami is silent, the file should escalate concern.

**Trust / safety.** As high as the internal architecture permits. Karami will not betray host self. He may, however, be overridden.

**Failure mode.** Karami can be drowned out by louder alters under acute stress, and is structurally outvoted when the Legion-alter is ascendant.

**Leverage.** External actors who can address Karami by name and history (very few — Moira, possibly Ruth, in principle a sufficiently briefed clinician) gain a back-channel to subject that bypasses the host's defensive perimeter.

### 3. Gabrielle Haller (maternal intimate, listed for completeness)

**History.** Mother. Holocaust survivor, diplomat. The other half of the parental dyad whose dysfunction is the etiological ground of the entire file.

**Dynamics.** Loving, present, structurally unable to mirror the magnitude of what her son became. Section 3 logs the maternal attachment as available-but-insufficient: she could hold a child, she could not hold an omega. Subject loves her without ambivalence and without expectation of being saved by her — a clearer emotional position than he holds toward any other person living or dead.

**Trust / safety.** High, with the understood ceiling.

**Failure mode.** Subject protects her from his condition by curating what she sees, which is its own quiet cost: she has never met most of him.

**Leverage.** Threat to Gabrielle would, like threat to Ruth, produce stress-level-4 response. Unlike Ruth, she cannot soothe him out of it afterward.

### 4. The unbuilt others

A final note belongs in this register precisely because of its emptiness. Across forty years of recorded behavior, subject has had: no recorded sexual relationships with peers prior to or outside the Ruth attachment; no recorded friendships of the casual, sustained, non-mission variety; no recorded children, godchildren, or chosen family in the broader sense; no recorded mentees. The intimate bandwidth is one channel, and it has been, almost the whole time, vacant or singly occupied.

This is not a finding about lovability. It is a finding about the cost of a self that cannot be presented continuously. To be intimate with subject, the other party must accept intimacy with a *crowd whose roster changes*. Almost no one can. That Ruth could is the singular fact from which the entire viable future of the subject — if there is one — must be reconstructed.

— END SECTION —


## Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

# POWERS, ABILITIES & THEIR LIMITS — SUBJECT: DAVID CHARLES HALLER

*Cross-indexed from observed deployments in New Mutants #26–28, Uncanny X-Men #254–255, the Muir Island Saga, X-Men #320–321 / Legion Quest, X-Men: Age of Apocalypse, X-Men Legacy vol. 1 #245–260 (Age of X / Carey), X-Men Legacy vol. 2 #1–24 (Spurrier), and subsequent appearances. The objective here is mechanism — what the power is, what it does, what it cannot do, and what it reveals about the man wielding it.*

---

## 6.1 — TAXONOMIC FRAME: WHY THE STANDARD CLASSIFICATIONS FAIL

Subject is on the public Omega-tier mutant register, but the conventional schema — telepath, telekinetic, pyrokinetic, etc. — describes the *manifestations* without naming the *engine*. The engine is not a faculty. It is a **dissociative architecture in which each personality compartment expresses as a distinct superhuman ability**. Stated as a clinical-tactical axiom: the host self, when present, has *no* powers. The alters do. Power activation is therefore *isomorphic with alter activation*. Any analyst who tries to predict subject's behavior by predicting his "abilities" without modeling his alter-states will be wrong every time, and will miss the only meaningful inflection points.

This produces three structural consequences that govern everything downstream.

**(a) Powers are personalities; personalities are powers.** When Cyndi takes the body, fire happens. When Jack Wayne takes the body, kinetic violence happens at range. When Jemail Karami takes the body, telepathy of an unusually reflective, conversational, even pastoral character happens. The power's *style* — its tempo, target selection, ethical envelope — is the alter's personality. You cannot have the ability without the affect that owns it.

**(b) The roster is open-ended and accretive.** Canon scales from three named alters in 1985 to several hundred by Carey's tenure to literal thousands in Spurrier's. New trauma generates new alters; new alters generate new powers. There is no closed list of capabilities to map. The intelligence question is not "what can he do" but "what has surfaced this week."

**(c) Power deployment is, in nearly every case, an involuntary somatic event coded as voluntary by observers.** Subject does not so much "use" his abilities as get used *by* them. The exception — Spurrier-era trained extraction of specific alters from the internal "prison" — proved transient and metastable. Treat the conscious-deployment frame as an aspirational fiction the subject maintains and the X-Men politely cosign.

---

## 6.2 — THE NAMED ALTERS AS PRIMARY POWER LOCI

### 6.2.1 — JEMAIL KARAMI (telepathy, mind-merge, psi-suturing)

The originating absorbed consciousness, accreted at the embassy attack. Mechanism is full-spectrum telepathy: thought-reading at conversational and subliminal depth, mental communication, memory-walk, psychic combat in the standard astral-plane modality. Range, when free, has been demonstrated continent-scale (the New Mutants intervention pulls David across the Atlantic by mental contact). Karami's distinguishing feature is *moral telepathy* — he uses the ability to listen, to integrate, to negotiate, including with other alters. He is the alter that did the work of pulling several hundred sub-alters into a partial syndicate during the Sienkiewicz arc. Operational signature: low-grandiosity, dialogic, often the alter that surfaces when subject is asked a sincere question.

**Limits.** Karami is the most *containable* power because he is the most ego-syntonic; he tends not to push beyond consent. Cannot, on his own, suppress the violent alters durably; he can talk, not jail. Vulnerable to being shouted down internally during high-affect crises.

### 6.2.2 — JACK WAYNE (telekinesis, kinetic projection, weaponized momentum)

The hypermasculine adventurer-alter. Telekinesis at the bus-throwing tier, fine enough for object manipulation but typically deployed coarsely; favored applications are blunt projection of debris, restraint of human-scale opponents, ballistic redirection. Wayne's signature is *swagger* — he announces, he postures, he flirts. When the body is on Wayne, posture squares, the shoulders set, the voice drops, the mannerisms become 1940s-pulp masculine. The TK is not delicate because Wayne is not delicate.

**Limits.** Range demonstrated reliably to a few hundred meters; mass thresholds inconsistent across appearances but plausibly in the multi-ton range under stress. Cannot perform sustained levitation of self for long flight (uses TK in bursts). More important: Wayne hates being subordinated and resists Karami's integration efforts, so the *cost* of deploying him is destabilizing the internal order for hours afterward.

### 6.2.3 — CYNDI (pyrokinesis, ignition, thermal projection)

The punkish adolescent-girl alter. Generates and directs flame — ignition from ambient air, projection in directed gouts, contained combustion at object surfaces. Affect is impulsive, gleeful, frequently cruel in adolescent-cruel register rather than predatory-cruel. When Cyndi has the body, the subject's somatic projection includes a feminized silhouette, voice register shift, looser posture; observers consistently misperceive an entirely different person briefly inhabiting the same physical envelope.

**Limits.** Requires oxygen; smothering, vacuum, or aggressive heat-sinking constrains output. Cyndi tires emotionally before she tires physically — she ignites, exults, and then sulks, ceding the body. She does not aim well; collateral damage near Cyndi is the rule, not the exception.

### 6.2.4 — THE LEGION-ALTER (reality distortion / pocket-cosmos generation)

Surfaced explicitly during the Age of X arc (Legacy #245–247). A high-tier alter whose capability is reality alteration on local-to-global scale; the *Age of X* false continuum — an entire pocket reality with fabricated histories for the X-Men — was a containment construct generated unconsciously by David's other personalities specifically to keep this alter buried. The pattern repeats: when the Legion-alter approaches the surface, the rest of the system burns enormous energy to construct a substitute world rather than allow the alter through.

**Limits.** Cost of activation is catastrophic; the rest of the system effectively goes offline to manage the spillover. Reality-distortion outputs are unstable and tend to unravel when externally observed by sufficiently powerful psychics (Rogue/Magneto's incursions cracked Age of X).

### 6.2.5 — THE CHRONO-CAPABLE ALTER (time travel — Legion Quest)

The alter operative during the 1995 *Legion Quest* — temporal displacement, with apparent navigation of past timepoints. Whether this is a discrete alter or a syndicate of alters acting in concert is canonically ambiguous; the operational read is that this capability is *rare*, *episode-bound*, and *not voluntarily re-summonable* on demand. After AoA's reset, the capability has not recurred at that scale.

**Limits.** Unrepeatable for narrative-canonical reasons that nonetheless function as in-universe limits: requires extraordinary alter cooperation; collateral is timeline-scale; subject's own ethical and traumatic objection to using it again is itself a hard limit.

### 6.2.6 — THE SPURRIER-ERA EXTRACTABLE ROSTER

Spurrier's run formalized the *prison metaphor* — alters as inmates, each with a name and a power, retrievable on demand after the Merzah training. Documented extractions across that run include: a force-field generator, a sound-manipulator, a chronal-acceleration alter (subjective time-dilation), a matter-transmuter operating at the molecular level, a flight-capable alter, a probability-skew alter, a healing alter (used on Ruth), a tracking/scrying alter, and at least one alter whose ability is simply "extreme physical durability." Subject can name and call them; the names are often nonsense-syllable or grotesque-descriptor compounds invented by the prior host or by the alters themselves, which itself communicates the *carnival* phenomenology of his inner life.

**Limits.** Each extraction risks the alter not returning to the prison; several Spurrier arcs hinge on a "released" alter refusing reincarceration. Extraction tempo is bounded by attentional bandwidth — one or two abilities at a time, with longer cooldowns the more dissonant the alter is with host values.

---

## 6.3 — POWER MECHANICS: WHAT THE ENGINE ACTUALLY IS

Beneath the alter-by-alter inventory, the underlying mutant phenotype is best characterized as **a generalized psionic substrate capable, in principle, of any reality-affecting output, gated and routed by the dissociative architecture.** The split is not a bug overlaid on a clean power-set; the split is the *only reason the power-set is manageable*. Were the substrate undifferentiated, the subject would be an undirected world-burning event.

Three mechanistic features deserve granular note.

**Somatic projection of alters.** Switching is not purely affective. Observers reliably report perceived changes in height, build, facial set, voice timbre, even apparent sex characteristics when Cyndi is fronting. The likeliest mechanism is low-grade ambient psionic projection — a continuous, involuntary telepathic broadcast of the alter's self-image, perceived by others as semi-real. This is consequential operationally: subject *looks like a different person* mid-engagement, and surveillance based on facial recognition will throw false negatives during switches.

**The hair phenomenon.** The vertical, perpetually electrified hair is consistent across decades, artists, and states of dress. Functional inference: continuous low-level psionic discharge produces an electrostatic field at the scalp. It is involuntary, it cannot be flattened by water or product for more than minutes, and it modulates with affect — observable spikes precede major alter-fronts by a fraction of a second. **For surveillance purposes, the hair is a real-time affect-meter.**

**The astral signature.** Telepaths in proximity (Xavier historically, then Rachel Summers, Emma Frost, Psylocke at intervals) consistently report David's mind as audible at a distance — a *crowd-noise* of overlapping voices, recognizable as his even when no specific alter is fronting. He cannot mask this. It functions as a permanent psionic beacon to anyone with telepathic detection capability above middle-tier.

---

## 6.4 — RANGE, SCALE, AND THE CEILING PROBLEM

Subject's *theoretical* ceiling is Omega — reality-alteration in the same conceptual class as the Scarlet Witch's House of M event or Franklin Richards's pocket cosmos. He has demonstrated this twice (AoA, Age of X). His *operational* ceiling at any given hour is whatever the currently dominant alter can do, which is usually mid-tier.

The gap between theoretical and operational ceiling is the single most important strategic fact about the subject. Threat assessments that anchor on the operational tier underestimate him by orders of magnitude; threat assessments that anchor on the theoretical tier overestimate him in routine encounters and miscounsel containment policy. The correct framing is **expected value across the alter distribution, modulated by trigger-state**. Routine David is a Beta-tier nuisance; cornered or paternally provoked David is a planetary event.

Range follows the same logic: telepathy operates planet-scale at peak, room-scale at baseline; telekinesis from object-manipulation to multi-ton; pyrokinesis from candle-flame to building-fire; reality alteration from interpersonal hallucination to continuum-replacement.

---

## 6.5 — GROWTH CURVE OVER PUBLISHED LIFE

**1985–1988 (Claremont/Sienkiewicz).** Three named alters, catatonic baseline. Powers manifest in florid bursts under astral-plane intervention; outside crises, output is near-zero. Karami integration produces the first stable executive function.

**Late 1980s–early 1990s (Muir Island plateau).** Slow accrual of alters; subject is functional-with-supervision. No reliable voluntary power use.

**1995 (Legion Quest / AoA).** Catastrophic peak: chrono-displacement and psi-blade lethality demonstrated at father-killing scale. Demonstrated for the first time that grandiose ideation, when stably organized across multiple alters in concert, can drive reality-class outputs. Reset removes him from existence.

**2000s (Mackie / Carey).** Returns with technological compartmentalization (the regulator headband). Voluntary alter-call introduced as a usable mechanic. Roster scales to hundreds. *Age of X* (2011) reveals unconscious reality-construction capability is intact and ungoverned.

**2012–2014 (Spurrier).** The maturation arc: Merzah training, internal prison, named-extraction tempo. This is the high-water mark of *deliberate* power use. Subject demonstrably learns. Subject just as demonstrably regresses under affect. Terminates in voluntary self-erasure — the highest-tier reality output the subject has ever willed.

**Post-2014.** Inconsistent across hands. The capabilities remain; the integration does not. The longitudinal curve is therefore **ratchet-up in raw capability, sawtooth in control**.

---

## 6.6 — SIGNATURE APPLICATIONS AND BEHAVIORAL TELLS

**Psi-blade.** The killing instrument used on Xavier in 1995. Manifests as a localized telepathic edge, lethal to mind regardless of physical shielding. When subject draws it consciously, the dominant arm raises in a fencer's preparation; the hair lifts further; the eyes lose focus on the physical target and acquire focus on a point an inch behind it. This is the single most dangerous deliberate output in the repertoire and the one he most fears using.

**Astral confrontation.** Subject's preferred resolution mode for interpersonal conflict involving telepaths. He draws opponents *inside* — into a Sienkiewicz-grade interior landscape where his alters are terrain features. He almost always wins astral combats and almost always pays for them with days of internal disorder.

**Containment construction.** When overwhelmed, the system builds a cage — internal (the prison), external (Age of X), or cosmological (self-erasure). The architectural impulse is invariant: when David cannot bear what he is, he builds a structure to hold it. This is both a power and a symptom; the dossier should not separate the two.

**Hair-as-tell.** Re-stated for tactical emphasis: any observer with a sustained look at the subject's scalp can read affect-state and pre-empt alter-fronts by a fraction of a second. Surveillance video of the hair, slowed and analyzed, produces a reliable predictive index.

**Sentence-mid switching.** A frequent micro-tell: alter changes mid-utterance, producing a syntactic seam — pronoun shift, register shift, vocabulary shift. Transcripts of subject's conversations across decades reliably contain these seams; they are the most economical diagnostic instrument available.

---

## 6.7 — HARD LIMITS

- **No null state with capability.** Whenever the host self is integrated and present, the powers are largely *off*. He cannot be both himself and useful in the standard tactical sense. The price of competence is dissociation; the price of integration is helplessness.
- **No simultaneous multi-alter execution beyond the low single digits.** The body is one body; the attention is finite. Stacked extractions degrade within minutes.
- **Telepathic shielding by sufficiently disciplined adversaries** (Emma Frost-tier diamond-form, Magneto's helmet) negates Karami-class outputs entirely and disrupts switching by removing affective input.
- **Power-nullifiers and inhibitor collars** work as advertised, but with a unique side-effect: collared David is not merely depowered, he is *flooded* — the alters cannot externalize and rebound inward, producing acute psychiatric crisis within hours. He cannot be safely held in standard mutant detention protocols.
- **The Karami integration ceiling.** No matter how much internal work, a residue of unintegrable alters persists. The system has a floor of irreducible plurality.
- **Father-figure presence as a hard destabilizer.** Any Xavier-coded authority figure in proximity reorders the alter hierarchy unpredictably. Cannot be relied on to perform consistently in the presence of mentors.
- **Self as ceiling.** The strongest brake on subject's power is subject's conscience. He will not voluntarily cross thresholds he has previously crossed (the AoA event functions as a permanent inhibition against deliberate timeline editing). The brake is moral, therefore breakable under sufficient affective load — but it is real.

---

## 6.8 — THE SYMPTOM-AS-SIGNATURE READING

The clinical posture of this dossier, throughout, has been that the pathology is an *over-learned successful coping strategy*. The powers section is where that thesis becomes literal rather than metaphorical.

Consider the structural economy. A child witnesses his stepfather's murder, lashes out telepathically, kills, and *absorbs the dying mind of his victim*. The mutant substrate was always there; what the trauma did was teach the substrate a *routing rule*: **unbearable content goes into a discrete compartment, which thereafter speaks and acts on its own.** The rule worked. The boy did not have to bear that he had killed; Karami bore it. The rule was reinforced at every subsequent overload: anger went to Cyndi, predation went to Wayne, grandiose violence went to the Legion-alter, world-reshaping went to whichever alter could host it. Every compartment came with a competence the host did not have to claim. The dissociation was not merely defensive; it was *productive*. It generated capability.

This is why the standard therapeutic move — *integrate the alters, become whole* — has failed for him across every writer who has tried it. **Integration is not a recovery; integration is the loss of his power-set.** A fully integrated David is, by the architecture of his own mind, powerless. He intuits this. The alters intuit this. The system actively resists the cure because the cure is castration. The Spurrier prison-metaphor is the most honest representation in canon: he does not heal, he *administers* — he becomes the warden of a self that cannot be made one.

The signature of this is everywhere in his deployments. The powers come *with affect attached*: Cyndi's fire is adolescent fury, Wayne's TK is pulp-masculine assertion, Karami's telepathy is the moral seriousness of a man trying to redeem the murder that birthed him. He cannot have the fire without the fury, the kinesis without the swagger, the telepathy without the conscience. Power and personality are co-extensive. To wield is to *become*.

And the catastrophic outputs — the timeline killing, the pocket reality, the self-deletion — are not lapses of control. They are the system performing its core function at maximum amplitude: **converting unbearable psychic content into world-events so that the host self does not have to carry it.** AoA was a child's wish to please his father, externalized as a continuum. Age of X was the system's refusal to let a violent alter through, externalized as a false world. The Spurrier-era self-erasure was the system's last available containment, externalized as ontological withdrawal. Each is the same maneuver: when the inside cannot hold, externalize the inside as outside, at whatever scale required.

The operational implication for any agency reading this file: **subject's powers cannot be assessed apart from his pain.** A tactical brief that treats him as a weapons platform will miscalibrate every encounter. He is a weapons platform whose targeting logic is sorrow, whose ammunition is grief, and whose safety catch is his love for the few people he has managed to attach to without destroying. Manage the man and the powers manage themselves; threaten the man and the powers will rewrite the room, the building, the city, or the timeline, in that order, until the threat is gone or he is.

The most accurate single sentence one can write about David Haller's abilities is this: **he can do anything, and every time he does, it is because something inside him could not be borne any other way.**

— END SECTION 6 —


## Operational Profile & Tradecraft

# OPERATIONAL PROFILE & TRADECRAFT — SUBJECT: DAVID CHARLES HALLER

*Filed as Section 7 of the longitudinal dossier. This section maps not what the subject IS but what he DOES: how he plans, how he funds himself, how he moves, how he fights, how he hides, how he is recognized in the field, and where the seams in his operational fabric are. All entries derived from observable canonical conduct, cross-checked against the diagnostic substrate established in Sections 3–5.*

---

## 7.1 DECISION-MAKING ARCHITECTURE

Subject's decision process is, structurally, unlike that of any other operator on file because it is not the product of a single deliberating mind. It is a **committee whose membership is unstable, whose chair rotates without warning, and whose minutes are not always shared with the host**. This produces three superimposed decision regimes that must be analyzed separately.

**Regime A — Host-led ("David proper").** When the host self is in the chair, decisions are characterized by long premeditation, moral self-interrogation, and a marked tendency toward over-elaboration. He drafts, he rehearses internally, he visualizes outcomes. He asks himself what Xavier would have done, then what Xavier *should* have done, then what would have made Xavier love him; the third question is the one that actually drives the output. The result is plans that look strategically coherent on paper and are, in fact, structurally suicidal — the *Legion Quest* time-jump being the canonical exemplar: a thirty-step plan executed with discipline, every step internally consistent, the terminal objective the wrong target chosen for the right (to him) reason. Host-led decisions exhibit what might be called **rationalized grandiosity** — the conviction that a sufficiently bold gesture will reorder the world. Tradecraft footprint here is heavy: notebooks, sketched costume designs, mission statements spoken aloud to no one, monologues to the dead father.

**Regime B — Alter-led (acute hand-off).** A trigger event — somatic threat, paternal cue, sexual approach, perceived humiliation — flips the chair to whichever alter is keyed to that affect. Decision latency collapses to milliseconds. The alter executes within its own logic, fully committed, with no consultation. The host has limited or no memory of the interval. The operational consequence: subject can transition from negotiation posture to lethal force inside the same sentence, and *will not be able to explain it afterward*. Counterparties report mid-conversation pupil shifts, voice-register drops, posture re-set — and then the room is on fire.

**Regime C — Council mode (Spurrier-era discipline, post-Merzah training).** Following the Himalayan internalization work, subject developed a deliberative protocol in which he descends into the mental "prison," summons a specific alter as a *tool*, deploys the associated power for a discrete task, and re-cages. When functional, this is the most effective decision-mode on file: surgical, modular, conscience intact. It fails predictably under three conditions — affective overload, paternal-figure invocation, or attack on a bonded peer — at which point Regime C decays into Regime B, often with a stronger alter than the one summoned breaking the cage.

**Cross-regime tells.** Decision quality is inversely correlated with personal stakes: he plans excellently for strangers, poorly for himself, catastrophically for his father. He **never delegates** in any of the three regimes — partly because there is no one else he trusts at his power tier, partly because the committee inside him already constitutes a delegated workforce.

---

## 7.2 PLANNING METHODOLOGY

When the host plans, he plans in a **mural-and-monologue** mode. Surfaces accumulate: hostel walls, monastery cell floors, the inside of constructed pocket-spaces. Diagrams, cause-arrows, names circled and re-circled, the word "DAD" or "CHARLES" or "FATHER" appearing somewhere on every working surface he has ever used for more than two days. He thinks out loud and answers himself in other voices — this is not a tic, it is *literally his planning team conferring*. Surveillance of any space he has occupied for more than a week will yield this signature.

Planning horizons are bimodal. Either the plan is **decades-spanning, ontologically ambitious** (rewrite the timeline, construct a counter-reality, restage the X-Men's lives to suppress an alter), or it is **next-six-hours improvisation** with no middle. He does not do quarterly. He does not do logistics scaffolding under a strategic frame. He does the apocalypse and he does the next bus.

Contingency planning is **near-absent at the strategic level and over-developed at the tactical**. He does not have a Plan B for "what if killing Magneto doesn't fix the timeline" — he has Plan B for "what if Magneto's helmet blocks the first psi-strike." This is consistent with the magical-grandiose cognition mapped in Section 5: the macro-outcome is treated as guaranteed by the gesture's sufficiency.

---

## 7.3 METHODS — THE ACTIVE TRADECRAFT

**Telepathic reconnaissance.** Default first move in any unfamiliar environment. Subject conducts passive ambient scans without seeming to — eye-line drifts, breathing slows fractionally. He is reading the room in the literal sense. Operational implication: he arrives at meetings already knowing what counterparties intend to say. Operational *vulnerability*: he often relies on the read instead of preparing, and a competent psi-shield reduces him to ordinary human social aptitude, which is poor.

**Alter-as-tool deployment.** Each summoned alter is essentially a single-function operative on retainer. There is an observed library — telekinetic, pyrokinetic, time-shift, matter-transmutation, sound-manipulation, the "tongue" alter (linguistic), the "King" (regal-charismatic), and many hundreds of lesser specialists. Spurrier-era field operations consistently show him **announcing the alter he is summoning** before deploying it, which is partly self-discipline (naming as caging) and partly performance for himself. This is an exploitable tell: counterparties who recognize the verbal cue gain ~1.5 seconds of foreknowledge of the incoming capability.

**Reality construction (rare, catastrophic).** When the regulator fails entirely, subject's tradecraft is replaced by environmental reauthoring. He does not break into a building; he edits the world such that the building was never built, or he was always inside it, or it is a different building staffed by people he has imagined to suppress an unwanted alter. This is not a tool he uses; it is a tool that uses him. There is no documented case of David deliberately deploying full reality-warp tradecraft and retaining control of the result.

**Time-travel methodology.** Used twice in canon at strategic scale, both via internal alter-mediated mechanism (no external device). Methodology is non-rigorous: he selects target window by emotional salience rather than chronometric precision and lands within minutes of the intended moment by accident more than design. He has no causality model and no return protocol. He travels with no provisions, no period-appropriate currency, no cover identity. The *Legion Quest* operation is a master class in what to never do procedurally — and he succeeded at the kill anyway, which is the relevant warning about his ceiling.

**Combat doctrine.** Avoids physical engagement when host-led; the body is undermuscled and untrained. When alters engage, doctrine is alter-specific: Jack Wayne fights brawler-style with telekinetic augmentation, Cyndi pyro-suppresses with no regard for collateral, Legion-alter annihilates indiscriminately. There is **no unified combat style** because there is no unified combatant. The exploitable consequence is that an opponent who survives the first alter's opening volley can sometimes induce a switch by talking to the host, at which point the engagement resets.

**Negotiation.** Karami-alter is the negotiator of record. When confronted by moral or theological argument, subject often involuntarily yields the chair to Karami, who is the most reflective member of the committee. Diplomats and counselors should address arguments to "the man who came back from Tel Aviv" or to "the one who was at the embassy"; this is a known protocol-trigger for the surfacing.

---

## 7.4 RESOURCES & FINANCES

Subject is **functionally post-economic** but **practically under-resourced**, a paradox that defines his entire material footprint.

He has direct access — via family — to the Haller estate: Gabrielle Haller is a high-ranking Israeli diplomat with both inherited and earned wealth, and David is the sole heir of record. He has demonstrably never engaged this resource at scale. Withdrawals, when traceable, are modest, irregular, and tend to coincide with periods of host-led lucidity (small wire transfers for travel, monastery donation, equipment). There is no investment activity, no property held in his own name, no recurring expense profile. He treats money as a *bus fare*, not a *base of operations*.

Secondary resource pool: the Xavier institutional apparatus. Through paternity and X-Men affiliation he has had episodic access to mansion infrastructure, Blackbird transport, medical bays, Cerebro-class equipment, and the broader mutant security network. He uses these inconsistently and tends to **flee them** during decompensation — the institution is associatively linked to the absent father and triggers either grandiose performance or shame-flight.

Tertiary: he can, when alter-enabled, simply *make* what he needs. Matter transmutation, telekinetic acquisition, telepathic suggestion at point-of-sale. He almost never does. The Karami-Karnak superego pressures him toward ascetic non-use of powers for material gain, and the host self largely complies. The practical effect: an omega mutant who sleeps in hostels, eats badly, wears clothes he has owned for years, and arrives at world-historical operations with the contents of a single shoulder bag.

**Documents.** Maintains an Israeli passport (Haller, given). British/UK papers via Muir Island period. No driver's license of record. No credit profile of significance. No fixed address since the Muir Island chapter closed. He is, on paper, a low-grade transient with a famous mother and a deceased prominent father — exactly the cover an intelligence service would build, and in his case it is not a cover.

**Equipment.** Minimal and idiosyncratic:
- The *psi-regulator headband / neural device* (Stryfe-derived, various iterations) — primary suppression tech, worn during his most stable operational periods, removed or destroyed during decompensation.
- A **self-designed costume** dating to the Spurrier era — green and yellow, high-collared, asymmetric — manufactured by him without institutional tailoring; the design is consistent across rebuilds, indicating it is psychologically load-bearing.
- A small kit of **physical tokens**: photographs, a small number of objects with paternal or mnemonic charge, carried even when he is otherwise traveling empty.
- No firearms. No blades. No tradecraft kit in the spycraft sense (no lockpicks, no comms gear, no false documents stockpile). His tradecraft is internal.

---

## 7.5 INFRASTRUCTURE & SAFE GEOGRAPHY

He does not maintain safehouses. He maintains **safe people** and **safe altitudes**.

Documented stable locations across the longitudinal record:
- **Muir Island, Outer Hebrides** — original sanctuary; associatively contaminated by adolescent catatonia and Moira's death; revisited rarely, with affect.
- **Tel Aviv / Haifa** — maternal base; visited episodically; he does not stay long. The embassy district is a no-go zone (origin trauma site).
- **Himalayan monastery (Merzah)** — the only location where he has voluntarily resided for an extended period as an adult. Functions as his nearest equivalent to a permanent operating base. He returns to it cognitively even when he cannot return physically.
- **The mental "prison"** — strictly speaking an internal architecture, but it is *operationally* a base: it is where he stores assets (alters), conducts planning, and retreats under siege. Surveillance of it is impossible by non-psi means.
- **Hostels, monasteries, transit lounges** worldwide — his actual day-to-day footprint, selected for anonymity and low-stakes social pressure.

He has never owned a vehicle, leased an office, kept a storage unit on record, or registered as anyone's employer. His infrastructure is **internal, ecclesiastical, or maternal**, in that order.

---

## 7.6 PATTERNS OF ACTION

**Initiation pattern.** Operations begin with a **private resolution event** — a moment, usually alone, in which the host declares (to himself, often aloud, often into a mirror or to the imagined father) that he is now committing to a course. This event is observable to surveillance because it is verbalized. The resolution is almost always over-grand relative to the actual task.

**Movement pattern.** Travels light, by public means when possible (subject demonstrably enjoys buses, trains, ferries — the slowness allows internal conferral). Avoids air travel when destabilized (confined-space alter risk). Uses teleport-capable alters only under time pressure and tends to land *off-target* by emotionally salient margins (lands at his mother's door instead of the target city; lands at the monastery instead of the battlefield).

**Engagement pattern.** Arrives, attempts dialogue, escalates through alter-rotation when dialogue fails, terminates either in catastrophic overkill or self-removal from the field. He has no documented instance of clean tactical withdrawal under engagement; withdrawal is always either *flight in dissociation* or *erasure*.

**Termination pattern.** Operations end with either (a) a guilt-debrief cycle of days to weeks in which he replays decisions in monologue, (b) collapse into a depressive non-functional interval, or (c) flight to a sanctuary location. He does not do after-action reports in any external sense; the debrief is internal, performed for the dead father, and it never resolves.

**Cyclical macro-pattern.** Across decades the rhythm is: **stabilization → grandiose mission → catastrophic outcome → self-removal → return → stabilization**. The cycle period varies but the structure is invariant. Any operational forecast on this subject should be priced against the position in this cycle, not against current presentation.

---

## 7.7 SIGNATURE OPERATIONAL TELLS

These are the markers by which an analyst can identify David Haller's hand on an event, often before attribution is possible by other means.

- **The hair.** Vertical, electrostatic, never settled. Persists across costume changes, decades, art teams, and continuity reboots. Likely autonomic; he does not style it and cannot fully suppress it. In low-light surveillance footage it is diagnostic at distance.
- **Mid-sentence register shift.** Voice drops or rises, accent migrates (American swagger for Jack Wayne, Levantine cadence for Karami, adolescent-feminine for Cyndi), syntax reorganizes. The shift is sometimes mid-clause. Audio forensics will flag it as multiple speakers; it is one throat.
- **Naming the tool.** Habitually announces which alter/power he is about to deploy, often in second-person address to himself.
- **Father-word vocabulary.** The terms *father*, *dad*, *Charles*, *the Professor*, *the dream* recur at rates an order of magnitude above baseline for any operator on file. Frequency-analysis of his speech reliably indexes his current decompensation level.
- **Costume integrity.** Wears the self-designed uniform when host-stable; reverts to civilian clothes or improvised dress when fragmenting; appears in *other alters' projected garments* in extreme dissociation. State can be read off the wardrobe.
- **Reality-bleed artifacts.** Environments he has occupied during stress sometimes retain micro-anomalies — small objects displaced, photographs altered, brief witness inconsistencies. These are diagnostic of his presence even after he has left.
- **Avoidance of mirrors and direct cameras** when destabilized; **fascination with both** when grandiose. The relationship to his own image is the fastest visible index of which regime is in the chair.
- **The notebook / wall.** Any space he has worked in for more than three days will show the mural-monologue planning surface. Photograph it; it is a partial transcript of the committee's last session.
- **The bag.** A single small shoulder-bag carries his entire material life. Contents: tokens, papers, the regulator when not worn, a change of clothes, sometimes a book of his father's writings. The bag is the most stable physical object in his operational footprint.
- **Karnak-style breath discipline** picked up at the monastery — a four-count inhale, hold, exhale, hold, performed under stress before attempting Council-mode summoning. Observable; precedes deliberate power use roughly 70% of the time in the Spurrier-era record.

---

## 7.8 SEAMS, FAILURE MODES, AND POINTS OF EXPLOITATION

For completeness — and because a UATU-grade file must include them — the operational seams are:

1. **The host is exploitable through the father.** Any credible invocation of Charles Xavier (approval, disappointment, betrayal, legacy) bypasses Regime C and forces hand-off. This is the largest single vulnerability in the entire profile.
2. **The committee can be addressed by name.** Alters respond to direct address. An operator who knows the roster can request a specific alter and frequently receive them. This is dangerous to attempt — summoning the wrong alter has consequences — but it is procedurally available.
3. **The regulator is a single point of failure.** Removal, damage, or psi-jamming of the headband returns subject to Regime B baseline within minutes.
4. **Bonded peers are operational levers.** Threats to Ruth Aldine or equivalent attachments will reorganize his entire decision-tree around protection, predictably and exploitably.
5. **The question "Who are you?"** asked sincerely, by someone he respects, in a moment of relative quiet, will destabilize him more reliably than any weapon on file. He has no answer. The asking is itself the attack.
6. **He cannot sustain operations longer than the cycle allows.** Long-duration engagements degrade him predictably; an adversary with patience outlasts him.

Against these seams must be set the counterweight: **at full reality-warp engagement, no exploitation matters, because the operational environment ceases to exist in the form the exploiter understands.** The same subject who can be unwound by a sincere question can also unwrite the questioner. Any plan involving him must price both ends of that distribution.

— END SECTION 7 —


## Worldview & Operational Code

# WORLDVIEW & OPERATIONAL CODE — SUBJECT: DAVID CHARLES HALLER

*Derived from cross-canonical behavioral record; segregated into philosophical substrate (what he believes about reality, persons, and meaning) and instrumental code (how he acts on those beliefs under live conditions). All propositions are inferential reconstructions from observed behavior, not self-report; subject's self-report is unreliable by reason of the multiplicity itself, and where it conflicts with conduct, conduct governs.*

---

## I. METAPHYSICAL SUBSTRATE — HOW HE READS REALITY

**Reality is plastic, and the plasticity is intimate.** Subject's foundational, pre-articulate conviction — laid down during the embassy attack when his mind first *killed* — is that the world is not a stable external object but a substance continuous with thought. Reality does not push back hard enough to be trusted as solid. This is not a philosophical position he arrived at; it is a sensorium. Every reality-warp episode (Age of X, the pocket-construct; the Age of Apocalypse divergence; the Spurrier-era erasures) confirms and re-inscribes the same tactile fact: when the pressure inside him exceeds a threshold, the outside reorganizes. He has therefore never developed the ordinary citizen's faith in the boundary between psyche and world. He treats that boundary as a courtesy he extends to other people, not a fact about the universe.

**Causation runs through wish.** Beneath all rational planning, subject operates a magical-causal model: sufficiently intense desire, properly ritualized (a plan, a journey, a costume, a vow), will produce the desired outcome. This is the cognition of a four-year-old fused to the capability of an omega mutant — a calamitous combination. He does not entirely believe in physics; he believes physics is the default mode reality adopts when no one is pushing on it hard enough.

**Time is editable, therefore moral fact is provisional.** Having traveled back and rewritten history once (catastrophically), subject cannot hold the ordinary citizen's view that the past is fixed. He treats history as a draft, and this corrodes his ability to accept loss as final. The death of Charles Xavier should be — for any normal mourner — an absolute, the wall against which grief breaks. For subject it is a condition that *ought* to be reversible and is only contingently not. This colors every grief he carries: none of them are properly mourned, because none are fully accepted as permanent.

**Selfhood is a contested commons, not a possession.** He does not believe, in the way a unitary person believes, that his body and history are *his*. They are jointly occupied territory. This produces an unusual operational humility about identity-claims (he will not insist he *is* anyone for very long) coexisting with an unusual operational ruthlessness about identity-management (he will jail, exile, suppress, or rebuild parts of himself with a casualness that would shock a person who experiences self as sacred).

**The mind is carceral architecture.** Every successful intervention in his life — Moira's early work, the Stryfe-derived headband, Merzah's monastic training, the literal mental prison — has been a *cage*. He has internalized the metaphor. He believes, at the operational level, that the mind's right configuration is a well-built jail with a competent warden. Freedom for him is not the absence of constraint; freedom is constraint that *works*. This is the inverse of the standard liberal-humanist read of psyche, and it is the source of much of his strangeness in conversation: he speaks of his interior the way a prison reformer speaks of a facility.

---

## II. ANTHROPOLOGY — HOW HE READS PERSONS

**People are mostly intact, and intactness is enviable and slightly alien.** Subject reads other humans as something he is not: continuous, single-voiced, with one set of wants at a time. He finds this both beautiful and faintly incomprehensible. He tends to over-credit ordinary people's coherence — assuming that what they say is what they mean, what they want today is what they will want tomorrow — and is repeatedly bewildered when they prove as multiple-in-practice as he is in structure.

**Fathers are gods who fail, and the failure does not demote them.** Subject's whole anthropology of authority is organized around the paternal figure. Authority is not earned by competence or held by office; it is *the thing the father has*, and the father's absence does not vacate the office. Xavier dead is more powerful in subject's operational world than most living men. He extends this template to every mentor he accepts (Moira, Merzah), granting them a structural authority disproportionate to what they have demonstrated and surviving with that authority intact through their failures.

**Mothers are survivors who cannot be burdened.** From Gabrielle Haller forward, his model of the maternal is the loving-but-already-broken figure whom one *protects* by withholding. This generalizes into a default operational stance toward anyone he reads as a fellow trauma carrier: do not give them your weight, they have their own.

**Peers are dangerous to themselves in his vicinity.** He has learned, repeatedly and bloodily, that proximity to him is hazardous. His anthropology of peers is therefore protective-distancing by default, with one exception at a time (Ruth Aldine being the canonical instance). He does not believe in his right to a normal social field; he believes he is owed solitude as a price of safety to others.

**Adversaries are misrouted versions of himself.** Subject does not easily sustain a clean enemy-concept. Pressed under a Karami-flavored alter, he tends to recognize in his opponents either a trauma-twin (someone broken into violence) or a structural mirror (someone trying to fix the world by destroying part of it — which is exactly his own move). This is why he negotiates when he should fight and annihilates when he should negotiate: he cannot reliably distinguish *enemy* from *unmet version of self*.

---

## III. THEORY OF CONFLICT

**Conflict is a failure of integration, not a clash of interests.** Subject's deepest read is that violence happens when something inside has not been included. He learned this from his own architecture — the alter that is not given a seat at the table will take the wheel — and he generalizes it. He distrusts purely interest-based or zero-sum framings of conflict and reaches reflexively for the *what is being excluded here* question. This makes him a better mediator than a soldier when he is host-dominant, and a worse soldier than he should be: he hesitates to destroy what he believes ought to be reintegrated.

**Violence is contagious and intimate.** From the Karami absorption forward, he has known that to kill a mind is to take it inside oneself. He does not believe in clean kills. Every act of fatal violence in his model produces a *passenger*. This is one of the strongest brakes on his ability to use lethal force casually, even when an alter wants it.

**The right scale of intervention is almost never the obvious one.** Subject's signature error — kill the cause upstream, edit the timeline, build a pocket reality to hide a problem — has taught him, slowly and through immense damage, that *the scale at which you act should be smaller than the scale at which you can act*. By Spurrier's period he is articulate about this principle, though he still violates it. He understands, intellectually, that an omega mutant must under-use his capability or destroy everyone he loves. He does not always feel it.

**Strategy is suspect; ritual is trusted.** Long-form rational strategy keeps collapsing for him because his cognition fractures under affect. Ritual — the costume, the named mission, the vow, the journey — holds when planning does not. He therefore privileges symbolic, gestural, formally framed action over multi-step contingent plans. He will *consecrate* an intention more readily than he will *project-manage* one.

---

## IV. THEORY OF CONTROL

**Control over self is the only legitimate sovereignty.** Subject does not believe in his right to govern anyone else, even when he plainly could. The reality-shaping powers exist; he refuses, almost without exception, to use them governmentally. The Age of X construct was unconscious and is, in his own retrospective view, his greatest sin precisely because it ruled others without consent. This is a hard, durable principle.

**Self-control is achieved by partitioning, not by mastery.** He does not believe — because evidence forbids belief — that a unitary will can subdue his interior. Instead he believes in walls, cells, doors, wardens, contracts between parts. His model of self-control is *governance of a population*, not *discipline of a body*. This shapes everything from his cooperation with restraint devices to his choice of monastic-architectural metaphors for inner work.

**External controls are accepted, sometimes courted.** Subject will wear the headband, take the drug, submit to the telepath, enter the cage. He does not experience these as humiliations. Control imposed from outside is, in his operational code, a *gift* — a load-bearing wall placed where his own structure is known to be weak. He distrusts caregivers who refuse to restrain him; he reads such refusal as either incompetence or sentimentality.

**Power should be used reluctantly, narrowly, and with witnesses.** When he does use his abilities deliberately (post-Spurrier), there is a marked pattern: the smaller power for the situation rather than the larger; the named alter summoned for the precise task and dismissed; a witness present, ideally Ruth, whose perception serves as a reality-check. He has learned to fear unwitnessed use of self.

---

## V. THEORY OF TRUST

**Trust is granular, role-specific, and revocable per alter.** Subject does not trust *people*; he trusts *people for specific functions under specific conditions*. He may trust Moira to restrain him and not to mother him; he may trust Ruth to see him and not to defend him; he may trust a Merzah-figure to discipline him and not to comfort him. He partitions trust the way he partitions self.

**Mentor-trust is unconditional and structurally over-extended.** Against his own better instrumental judgment, he tends to give father-figures a blanket credit that survives evidence. This is a known weakness, has been exploited (Xavier-impersonators, possessions, manipulation arcs), and he has not corrected it. He cannot correct it: the hunger is older than the judgment.

**Peer-trust is built slowly, by a person's tolerance of his episodes.** The single most important data point in his trust-calibration is whether someone stayed during a switch or an overload and remained recognizable afterward. Ruth's status in his life is anchored exactly here. He does not require people to *understand* him; he requires them to *not flinch*.

**Self-trust is essentially zero, and he has made peace with that.** He does not trust himself to read situations correctly under affect, to remember accurately what he just did, to be the same person an hour from now. His operational code therefore externalizes verification: he checks with others, with devices, with rituals. A subject who insisted on trusting himself would be far more dangerous; his lack of self-trust is, paradoxically, one of his safer features.

---

## VI. THEORY OF RISK

**Risk to self is undervalued to the point of non-registration.** Subject does not, in any meaningful sense, fear his own injury, death, or erasure. Twice he has volunteered for non-existence as a clinical intervention. This is not bravery; it is the absence of a normally functioning self-preservation circuit, an absence consistent with severe disorganized attachment and chronic dissociative pathology. Any threat-assessment of subject must assume he will not flinch at personal cost — and that this is a vulnerability, not a strength, because he will spend himself on the wrong problems.

**Risk to bystanders is the only risk he weights properly, and he over-weights it.** His threshold for *acceptable collateral* is near zero, and he routinely chooses worse outcomes for the mission to reduce bystander exposure. This is both a moral feature and an operational liability — an adversary aware of it can manipulate him by populating the battlefield with non-combatants.

**Catastrophic, low-probability outcomes are mis-modeled as live possibilities.** Because he has actually produced cosmological catastrophes from psychiatric episodes, his probability estimation around tail risks is broken — and broken in the direction of taking them very seriously. He cannot calibrate himself as a *rare* dangerous person; he experiences himself as a *continuously* dangerous one. This produces a chronic background load of anticipatory guilt that depresses his function.

**Time-risk is mishandled.** Believing the past is editable, he is poor at the standard human discipline of treating bygones as sunk. He keeps reopening the AoA wound; he keeps re-running Xavier scenarios; he cannot let an old loss settle into the loss it has become. Risk-of-recurrence is, for him, indistinguishable from the original event.

---

## VII. THEORY OF MEANING AND THE GOOD

**Meaning is constructed by mission, not discovered in fact.** Subject does not believe the world arrives with intrinsic purpose; he believes purpose must be *taken on*. The mission he takes on is always some variant of his father's dream — mutant-human coexistence, the protection of the vulnerable — but he insists on a personalized re-articulation of it (the costume, the team-of-one, the named heroism). The content is inherited; the framing must be his.

**The good is what reduces unintegrated suffering.** Distilled from his pattern of choices: subject treats as good those acts which bring orphaned pain into relationship — an alter into the prison-with-the-warden, a stranger into the witnessed circle, an enemy into the negotiated frame. He treats as evil those acts which produce more orphaned pain — abandonment, exclusion, unwitnessed violence, the leaving of a self or other in the cold.

**Heroism is a posture against shame, not a vocation.** He does not believe himself to be naturally heroic. He believes heroism is a *practice* he performs because the alternative is being a patient or a weapon. The costume and self-naming are not narcissism; they are reaction formation in formal dress. He needs the heroic frame to keep functioning, and he knows it is a frame.

**Sacrifice is the highest currency, and he overspends it.** In his moral economy, the most valuable thing one can offer is oneself, and the offering only counts if it costs. This is a religious-grade conviction and is functionally indistinguishable from suicidality dressed in ethical clothing. He will keep paying in self until something stops him.

**Forgiveness is theoretically available to others and practically unavailable to himself.** He extends a remarkable forbearance to other broken people — including those who have done terrible things — because his anthropology insists they are misrouted, not evil. He does not extend it to himself. The asymmetry is total and he does not intend to fix it.

---

## VIII. POLITICAL AND SOCIAL ORIENTATION

**Suspicious of institutions, including the ones he was raised by.** Subject was the son of a diplomat-mother and (eventually) the X-Men's founder. He has lived inside two institutional projects (Israeli statecraft, Xavier's school) and watched both fail to protect him or others. He does not believe institutions are evil; he believes they are insufficient and that they tend to sediment around the founder's blind spots. His Spurrier-era choice to operate *outside* the X-Men while pursuing Xavier's mission is the formal articulation of this view.

**Mutant-political position: assimilationist by inheritance, separatist by experience, ultimately personalist.** He inherits Xavier's coexistence dream and never repudiates it. But he has lived through enough to know coexistence is not produced by institutions; it is produced one relationship at a time. He defaults, when given freedom, to personal-scale interventions: this town, this person, this child. He distrusts mass programs.

**Indifferent to ordinary politics, acute about psychiatric politics.** Subject has no observable position on standard human political questions and treats them as roughly beneath the scale of his concerns. He has very strong views about how mad people are treated — about consent, restraint, asylum architecture, the dignity of patients — because he is one and his interior is run on those questions.

---

## IX. OPERATIONAL CODE — RULES OF ENGAGEMENT IN LIVE CONDITIONS

Derived from observed pattern across decades; these are the heuristics he actually runs, not the ones he would articulate.

1. **Smaller before larger.** Use the smallest competent alter for the task. Escalate only on failure, never on impulse. Frequently violated under affect; structurally held when host-dominant.
2. **Named before unnamed.** Summon a known alter by name rather than letting an unknown one surface. The act of naming is part of the containment.
3. **Witnessed before solo.** Prefer to act in front of a trusted observer. Solo action is permitted only when bystander protection demands isolation.
4. **Restraint accepted, not resisted.** Cooperate with any reasonable external control offered by a trusted party. Treat resistance to restraint as a symptom, not a value.
5. **Negotiate first, especially with mirrors.** When the adversary is recognizable as a fellow broken party, attempt verbal/empathic engagement before force. Often catastrophically extended.
6. **Bystanders are non-negotiable.** No mission justifies civilian collateral. Will abandon objectives to clear a field.
7. **No governance of others without consent.** Reality-shaping for one's own interior: permitted. For others' interiors or circumstances: forbidden, even when warranted. The Age of X failure is the cautionary text.
8. **Ritualize commitments.** Important decisions are taken in formal frame — the costume on, the vow spoken, the journey begun — because casual decisions do not bind his architecture.
9. **Father-figures get a hearing, but not the keys.** Mentor-trust extended generously; mentor-control resisted (imperfectly, often failing).
10. **Self-cost is the cheapest currency.** Default to spending oneself before spending others, even when the calculus is irrational.
11. **Memory is corroborated, not relied upon.** Verify with witnesses, devices, written record. Do not trust internal memory of recent events involving switches.
12. **In doubt, withdraw.** When unable to determine which self is dominant, the safest move is geographic and social removal from the situation. Isolation as a clinical tool, not a punishment.
13. **The mission completes the father, not the self.** The work is not done when David is well; the work is done when Xavier's dream is realized. This is a known distortion, never corrected.
14. **Self-erasure is the terminal containment option.** Reserved for the case where no other intervention can prevent catastrophic harm; available, has been used, will be used again under sufficient threat-model.

---

## X. INTERNAL CONTRADICTIONS HE LIVES WITH

A worldview-and-code map is incomplete without naming the unresolved tensions subject carries as live wiring. He does not resolve these; he oscillates within them.

- **Reality is plastic / Reality must be respected.** He knows he can edit the world and believes he must not. The discipline of restraint against demonstrated capability is the central ethical labor of his adult life.
- **The self is multiple / The self must be one.** He simultaneously accepts and refuses his architecture. He works toward integration he half-suspects would be a kind of death.
- **The father is sacred / The father is the wound.** He cannot demote Xavier and cannot stop being injured by him. The grief is undischargeable.
- **He must be a hero / He must not be trusted.** The mission requires agency; the diagnosis forbids it. He acts anyway, in the gap.
- **He owes the world reparation / He owes the world his absence.** Both are true in his economy and they recommend opposite policies. He alternates.
- **Love is the floor of function / Love endangers the beloved.** Ruth's presence stabilizes him; his presence imperils her. He has not solved this and will not.

These contradictions are not failures of his worldview. They *are* his worldview, in its operational form: a person who has thought as far as anyone in his situation could think and arrived at a set of incompatible truths he has decided to carry rather than collapse. The carrying is the code.

— END SECTION —


## Moral & Ethical Framework

# Moral & Ethical Framework — Subject: David Charles Haller

## Preface: The Method Problem

Any moral assessment of this subject must work outward from a structural fact established in §3: the subject does not possess a single continuous moral agent. He possesses a *host* with a moral code, and a population of alters each of whom has *their own* code, and the code that gets enacted at any given moment is a function of which entity is at the wheel. Conventional ethics presumes one author behind the act. This file cannot. What follows therefore proceeds in three registers: the **professed** code of the host (what David Haller, when integrated and articulate, says he believes and means to do); the **enacted** code (the empirical pattern of behavior across forty publication-years, regardless of which alter performed it, since the law and the dead do not care which face was wearing the body); and the **structural** code (the deep operating rules that hold across both host and alters, visible only longitudinally).

The gap between these three is the moral subject.

---

## 1. The Professed Code (Host, when integrated)

What David Haller will tell you, sincerely, that he believes:

- **Mutants and humans deserve to coexist.** He inherits this from Xavier wholesale, never seriously interrogates it, and treats dissent from it as not merely wrong but personally wounding — because the dissent is a wound to the father.
- **Power obligates.** He will articulate, especially in the Spurrier-era monologues, that having his abilities makes inaction itself a moral failure. This is the standard X-ethic absorbed without modification.
- **He must "complete" Xavier's dream, but not via Xavier's institutions.** The post-AvX self-conception is explicit on this: the dream is right, the school was wrong, and he intends to fix the difference. This is a moral position dressed as a tactical one; underneath, it is a son's argument with a dead father.
- **Killing is wrong.** Stated repeatedly, including in direct conversation with alters who disagree.
- **He is responsible for the harm he has caused.** The Age of Apocalypse guilt is owned, not displaced. He will not blame the alters for it, will not blame Xavier, will not blame illness. This is, ethically, the most admirable feature of the entire profile.
- **Coercion of others' minds is forbidden** — a near-absolute taboo, inherited from Xavier's own (often violated) prohibition. The host treats telepathic intrusion as the cardinal sin of his power-class. He will refuse to read; he will refuse to edit; he flinches from doing what he can trivially do.

This is a coherent, recognizably liberal-mutant-heroic ethic. It is also, in critical instances, *not what gets done.*

---

## 2. The Enacted Code — What He Actually Will and Will Not Do

### 2.1 Hard "Will Nots" (consistent across decades, alters, and writers)

These are the prohibitions that hold even when the host is absent and the alters are driving. They function as something closer to *somatic constraints* than choices — the system as a whole, including the more violent encapsulations, will not cross them.

- **Will not harm his mother.** Gabrielle Haller is the one figure whose safety is treated as axiomatic. No alter targets her. No grandiose plan endangers her. This is the moral baseline; if it ever broke, the entire system would be unrecognizable.
- **Will not harm Ruth Aldine.** Acquired late, but absolute once formed. He will erase himself before he will let an alter reach her.
- **Will not knowingly kill a child.** Even Cyndi pulls short of this line. Whatever else fractures, this does not.
- **Will not deploy his reality-warping or time-editing capacities for personal gain** — material, sexual, or status. Every catastrophic use of those powers has been ideological-paternal in motive, never appetitive. The omega-class mutant has never once cheated at cards, conjured wealth, edited a memory to be liked. This restraint, given his capacity, is morally enormous and structurally consistent.
- **Will not lie to a therapist or mentor about his state, even when lying would buy him liberty.** He turns himself in; he submits to devices; he goes to the monastery; he sits down for the conversation he knows will end in restraint. The compliance is sometimes catastrophic in itself (it props up the next failed cure) but the candor is real.

### 2.2 Hard "Wills" (acts he repeatedly performs, professed code notwithstanding)

- **Will kill, when an alter has the body and a target is framed as enemy.** The professed prohibition on killing is, empirically, a host-only rule. Cyndi has burned people. Jack Wayne has thrown them through walls. The Legion-alter is a homicidal field. The host has committed homicide directly: the embassy attackers as a child (arguably not a moral act in the responsibility sense, but a precedent); Charles Xavier in 1995, by his own hand and full intent.
- **Will alter reality at civilizational scale to manage his own psyche.** The Age of X arc is the cleanest demonstration: faced with an alter he could not contain, he unconsciously rewrote the X-Men's identities and built them a pocket world to live inside, so that the alter would have nothing to break. He did not ask consent. He could not have asked consent. The act is in flat contradiction to his professed taboo on mental coercion — and he committed it against the people closest to him, repeatedly, at the scale of *constructing their selves wholesale*. This is the central moral fracture in the file.
- **Will travel in time to kill a man before he has done his future wrong.** The AoA gambit is precrime in its purest form. The professed code (killing is wrong; mutants and humans should coexist; the father's dream is sacred) is held simultaneously with the enacted act of murdering the father's friend before the friend's offense, in the father's name. The contradiction did not register at the time of decision. This matters.
- **Will impose containment on himself by means that incidentally remove agency from his alters** — including alters he has, at other points, treated as persons with rights (Karami most notably). The monastery training in *Legacy vol. 2* is essentially a one-man carceral state in which the warden, the prisoners, and the prison are all the subject. He does this without democratic consultation with the imprisoned, because there is no procedure for such consultation; but the ethical question of whether alters are *people* is one he treats inconsistently — sometimes as fragments, sometimes as fellow citizens of the skull.
- **Will erase himself from existence to prevent a foreseen harm.** Done twice. The act is presented (and largely felt) as moral courage. It is also a refusal of the harder ethical labor of *living with the risk one is*, and it externalizes onto reality the decision a mortal patient would have to negotiate with clinicians, loved ones, and time. He has the omega-class option of suicide-as-cosmological-edit, and he takes it. Whether this is heroism or the ultimate avoidance is the file's open question.

### 2.3 The Soft Zone (where the code is improvisational)

- **Telepathic intrusion.** Forbidden in principle; performed in practice when stakes are framed as sufficient. He will read a hostile mind to prevent imminent violence; he will not read a friend's mind to settle a question. The line tracks consent-and-threat in roughly the way a soldier's rules-of-engagement do, not the way a clinician's confidentiality does.
- **Use of alters as instruments.** The post-Carey headband era systematizes this: pick a power, summon the alter who carries it, deploy. Treats the alters as tools, which the Karami arc had earlier insisted they were not. The ethics of summoning a sentient fragment to perform labor and then dismissing it are never resolved by the subject; he avoids the question because the answer is uncomfortable.
- **Truth-telling to allies about his stability.** The host is candid with authority figures (§2.1) but selectively opaque with peers, especially Ruth, especially when he believes the truth would cost him their continued presence. He minimizes; he deflects; he absents himself rather than confess relapse. This is not malicious deception, but it is deception, and it is patterned.
- **Acceptance of help.** He oscillates between submission to restraint (good patient) and grandiose self-cure (bad patient), and the swing tracks not his actual condition but his current father-affect: when he feels worthy of the father's love he will accept treatment; when he feels he must *earn* the father's love he will refuse treatment to go save the world himself.

---

## 3. Justifications — The Internal Rhetoric

The subject's moral self-talk, traceable across the canon, follows a small set of recurring templates:

- **The Filial Warrant.** "This serves Xavier's dream / would have pleased my father / completes what he could not." Used to authorize acts ranging from the conventionally heroic to the genocidally catastrophic. It does no discriminating work; it sanctifies whatever is placed under it. The AoA killing is its purest expression. The Spurrier-era heroic mission is its more functional one. Same warrant, opposite outputs.
- **The Containment Warrant.** "I had to, to keep something worse from happening — usually from me." Used to justify the Age of X reality-rewrite, the monastic imprisonment of alters, eventually the self-deletion. This is the warrant most often actually true on the facts, and the one most prone to expanding without limit, because the "worse thing" being prevented is in his own head and only he can assess it.
- **The Ownership Warrant.** "I did it, therefore I will pay for it." This is the post-AoA stance. It is morally serious and personally costly, and it produces real reparative behavior. It also functions as a license: having pre-paid in guilt, he sometimes treats himself as ethically credited for the next risky act. Penitence as currency.
- **The Exceptionalism Warrant.** "Normal rules don't fit my situation." Rarely spoken; frequently operative. He is, in fairness, an unprecedented case, and conventional ethics genuinely does strain around omega-class reality-warping multiplicity. But the warrant is also self-serving and is the rhetorical engine of the grandiose missions.
- **The Love Warrant.** "I did it for her / for him." Used sparingly, almost only around Ruth, and almost always honestly. The cleanest of his justifications, and the one that most reliably produces acts he does not later regret.

---

## 4. Consistencies — Where the Code Holds

Across forty years and many hands, certain moral features do not move:

- **No instrumental cruelty.** He has never hurt anyone *to enjoy it*, *to extract from them*, or *to dominate them as such*. Even at his worst the harm is collateral to a (deluded) project, never the point. This is the single largest gap between his enacted body-count and a properly evil character with similar capabilities.
- **No sexual misuse of power.** Despite omega-class capability and the documented presence of a hypermasculine alter, there is no canonical instance of sexual coercion, manipulation, or exploitation. Given the powers available, this restraint is morally non-trivial and structurally reliable.
- **No betrayal of confided trust for advantage.** He will withhold from allies; he will not weaponize what they have told him. Information given in trust stays held.
- **Genuine remorse, durable across time.** The Age of Apocalypse guilt is the same in 2014 as it was in 1995. He does not metabolize it away. He does not reframe it. He carries it.
- **A floor of recognition that other minds are real.** Even when he violates their autonomy, he is never solipsistic about their existence. The Age of X victims are treated, in his felt sense, as people he wronged, not as figments he managed. This is the precondition of any moral life with his powers, and he meets it.

---

## 5. Fractures — Where the Code Breaks

- **The professed-vs-enacted gap on killing.** He believes killing is wrong; the system kills. He has never reconciled this. The dissociative escape hatch — *Cyndi did it, Legion did it, I was not driving* — is one he uses less and less as he matures, but the underlying contradiction (his hands, others' wills, his responsibility) is never resolved because it is not resolvable inside the structure he is.
- **The taboo on mental coercion vs. the Age of X event.** The largest single ethical violation in his record is one his professed code most forbids. He performed it unconsciously, which is morally mitigating but not exculpating, and he has never made full reparation to the people whose selves he rewrote.
