The file should note that he has also never had a structural opportunity to: the people involved either forgave him operationally or moved on, and the act has been narratively absorbed rather than ethically processed.
- **The Filial Warrant's lack of safety-rails.** As long as an act can be framed as service to the father, the subject's internal vetoes weaken. This is the single most dangerous feature of his moral architecture, because the framing is done by him, in private, often by the alter currently in charge, and there is no countersignature requirement. The AoA killing passed this gate. So did, in inverted form, both self-deletions.
- **Self-erasure as ethical exit.** Conventional ethics is hostile to suicide as solution; the subject's ethics permits it specifically when scaled to *prevent the harm he is*. The moral status of this is genuinely contested. The file's position: it is at minimum a refusal of the harder, more cooperative path of *being treated and contained by others over time*, and it has the effect of denying everyone who loved him the agency of choosing to live alongside his risk. Twice he has decided alone that the world is better without him; twice no one was asked.
- **Inconsistent personhood granted to alters.** Sometimes they are people he negotiates with (Karami). Sometimes they are powers he summons (the headband era). Sometimes they are prisoners he warehouses (monastery). The subject has not built a coherent theory of who lives in his head, and the resulting moral treatment is ad hoc — defensible case by case, indefensible as a system.

---

## 6. Drift Over Time

The longitudinal arc of the code is real and traceable:

- **1985–1991 (Claremont catatonia and Muir plateau).** No autonomous code. The host barely exists; ethics is whichever alter is up. Karami brings in a borrowed but serious ethical seriousness (the absorbed terrorist, paradoxically, is the most moral resident). The subject does not yet *have* a moral life; he has moral weather.
- **1995 (Legion Quest / AoA).** A coherent code is constructed for the first time, organized entirely around the Filial Warrant, and immediately produces catastrophe. Lesson the subject draws — eventually — is *not* that the warrant is bad but that he executed it poorly. The warrant survives. This is consequential.
- **2000s (Carey era and Age of X).** The code begins to incorporate the Ownership Warrant. He accepts that he caused harm, accepts restraint, accepts treatment. Functions improve. Then the Age of X event reveals the limits of the host's control over the system's ethical behavior, and the code is forced to absorb a new fact: *I can do grave wrong while sincerely meaning not to.* This is the beginning of his adult ethical life.
- **2012–2014 (Spurrier, Legacy vol. 2).** The most articulated phase. He explicitly tries to construct an ethics of his own — heroism not via Xavier's institutions but via personal mission, with reparation as the underlying motive. He is at his most morally interesting here: candid about his history, skeptical of his own grandiosity, *aware* of the Filial Warrant and trying to discount for it, capable of love. The arc ends with the second self-erasure, which is either the code's finest moment or its largest failure — the file declines to choose, because the subject himself could not.
- **Post-Spurrier (Disassembled, Age of X-Man, Krakoan-adjacent).** Less coherent, but the through-line holds: he has internalized that he is dangerous, he has internalized that he is responsible, and he has not solved either fact. The code is now organized around managing his own risk to others — which is morally mature in form, and worryingly close to pre-emptive self-removal in content.

---

## 7. Comparative Note

The closest real-world ethical analogue is not the criminal and not the patient but the *deeply religious penitent with combat experience and unresolved authority wounds* — someone whose moral seriousness is not in doubt, whose acts have included grave harm, whose framework for atonement is private and ascetic, and whose largest risk is the conversion of guilt into the next grandiose mission. Comparisons to Malcolm X's late period — the seriousness, the willingness to publicly revise, the cost of having been wrong — are warranted in *tone* but overstate the subject's political coherence. He has the conscience without the program.

---

## 8. Summary Judgment

The subject is a morally serious person whose moral seriousness cannot fully reach his hands. His prohibitions are real and held; his violations are real and owned; the gap between them is the dissociative structure, which ethics has no standard procedure for. He is neither the villain his body-count suggests nor the hero his professed code claims. He is, more precisely, a man trying to author one ethical life out of a population of authors, succeeding partially and visibly, failing partially and catastrophically, and continuing — this is the durable fact — to try. The file's working operational summary: **trust the prohibitions in §2.1 absolutely; trust the host's professed code conditionally and only when the host is verifiably at the wheel; assume the Filial Warrant is active whenever Xavier is invoked, named, or visibly absent from a situation where he should have been; and treat any escalation toward reality-altering capacity as the moment the ethics file ceases to be the relevant document and the cosmology file takes over.**


## Communications & Linguistic Profile

# COMMUNICATIONS & LINGUISTIC PROFILE — SUBJECT: DAVID CHARLES HALLER

*Compiled from direct speech as rendered in New Mutants #26–28 (Claremont/Sienkiewicz, 1985); Muir Island appearances through the late 1980s; Uncanny X-Men #319–321 and X-Men #40–41 (the Legion Quest, Lobdell/Waid/Loeb, 1995); Mike Carey's Legacy run (Age of X arc, #245–247, 2011); Si Spurrier's X-Men Legacy vol. 2 #1–24 (2012–2014); and adjacent crossover speech samples. Television variants noted only where they reproduce a verbal habit the comics already establish.*

---

## 1. THE FUNDAMENTAL FACT

Subject does not have a voice. Subject has a *roster* of voices, and the operative communications question at any given moment is **which one is talking, and which one is listening from behind it.** No linguistic feature of David Haller can be cataloged as a stable trait of "the person"; every feature must be tagged to which substructure of the personality is foregrounded. The signal-processing premise for any interlocutor — diplomatic, clinical, tactical — is that a conversation with subject is a conversation with a *committee* in which only one member has the microphone and the others can rip it from him mid-syllable.

That said, certain patterns recur across decades and across the host's own speech (the "David" voice, when he is forward), and those patterns are the body of this section.

---

## 2. REGISTER OF THE HOST SELF ("DAVID")

When the host self holds the floor, the speech register is, with surprising consistency across writers from Claremont to Spurrier:

- **Hesitant-formal, faintly Anglophone, faintly elsewhere.** Subject was raised in Paris and Israel by a multilingual mother and educated across English, French, and Hebrew environments. The result on the page is English that is *too correct* — full contractions used sparingly, subordinate clauses completed when a native speaker would trail off, occasional small idiom-misses ("at all events" rather than "anyway"; "I should like to" surfacing in moments of stress). Reads as the English of someone who *learned* English well rather than someone who *grew up* in it.
- **Hedged.** First-person assertions are buffered: "I think," "I believe," "It seems to me that," "If I'm — if I'm honest." The Spurrier scripts in particular weaponize this — internal monologue in caption-boxes is unhedged and articulate; spoken word to others is hedged into apology.
- **Self-interrupting.** Em-dashes everywhere. The Claremont-era word-balloons already use mid-sentence breaks; Spurrier formalizes it into a tic — the host begins a sentence, an alter murmurs internally, the sentence restarts. To an observer this reads as stammer; clinically it is *interruption from within.*
- **Apologetic.** "Sorry — sorry, I —" is the most frequent two-to-three-word string in his recorded speech. He apologizes preemptively, retroactively, and for the act of speaking.
- **Quiet by default.** Spoken volume is low; force is rare; declarative sentences without softeners almost always indicate that an alter has surfaced or that he is briefly in his grandiose-savior mode (see §4).

The cumulative effect: a man who sounds, when he is himself, *younger than he is* — perpetually about twenty-two, perpetually about to be corrected.

---

## 3. ALTER-SPECIFIC REGISTERS (THE CATALOG)

A surveillance file requires the differential. The originating three alters establish the template; the later thousands fan out from the same logic — *each alter speaks the way the affect it carries would speak if it were a person.*

- **Jemail Karami.** The most linguistically mature voice in the system. Measured cadence, full sentences, occasionally Arabic interjection or Levantine sentence-rhythm transposed into English. Uses subject's full name when addressing him internally ("David"), addresses others by title or formal honorific. The only voice in the system that uses the second person without aggression. Tells: a slight pedagogical mode ("Consider —"; "You must understand —"), and a tendency to refer to the body as "this body" rather than "I" — a residue of the absorbed-consciousness status.
- **Jack Wayne.** Swaggering American-Western affect — flat vowels, slang, sexual innuendo, contempt-laughter. Calls David "the kid" or "Davey." Calls women by appearance-tags. Uses "we" inclusively when the body is doing something he wants ("we're gonna —"), switches to "the kid" when distancing himself from consequences. Marks territory in conversation by speaking *over* others rather than to them.
- **Cyndi.** Voice positioned higher and faster. Punctuation in word-balloons reads as exclamation-heavy, hyphenated, profane in a teenage register rather than an adult one. Calls David "Davey" with a different timbre — affectionate-mocking rather than Jack's contemptuous. Vocabulary clusters: fire-words ("burn," "cook," "crisp"), insults that are short and dental ("creep," "freak," "pig"). When she takes the body, sentences shorten to four or five words; she does not finish complex thoughts because complex thoughts are not her function.
- **"Legion" (the violent integrated-alter encountered in Age of X).** Lower-register, slow, almost ceremonial. Speaks in absolutes. Uses "shall" and "must." Refers to David in the third person with cold pity.
- **Later alters (Carey/Spurrier roster — Endgame, Chronodon, Susan-in-Sunshine, the "Time-Sink," etc.).** Each presents as a one-line voice idiosyncrasy keyed to its power — temporal alters tense-shift, perception alters speak in sensory inventory, telepathic alters speak in second person directly into the listener's head with no quotation marks rendered.

A tactical interlocutor learns to *listen for the register-shift first* — a one-word change of accent, a sudden completion of a sentence that David had been hedging, a tense or pronoun jump — and only then to attend to content.

---

## 4. THE HEROIC-MODE REGISTER

When subject occupies what Spurrier dramatizes as the self-narrating savior identity (post-Xavier's death, costume-and-mission phase), the speech changes specifically and diagnostically:

- **Loss of hedges.** "I think" becomes "I will." "Maybe" disappears.
- **Mission-statement diction.** Phrases like "the dream," "my father's dream," "what he would have wanted," "the right thing," "the only way" — abstract nouns substituting for concrete proposals.
- **Speeches rather than exchanges.** Sentences elongate. Subject loses the cue-and-response rhythm of conversation and begins delivering paragraphs at people.
- **Slight archaism, faintly biblical.** "I have come to —"; "Let it be —"; "I will not allow —." This is the register in which the Legion Quest pitch was made; it is the register in which catastrophic decisions are announced.
- **The tell**: he stops apologizing. The absence of "sorry" in subject's speech, when subject is otherwise engaged in extended monologue, is the single most reliable predictor that he is about to do something cosmologically dangerous.

---

## 5. INTERNAL MONOLOGUE vs. EXTERNAL SPEECH

A particularly Spurrier-codified feature, and the one that distinguishes subject most sharply from most published characters:

- **Internal voice (caption-boxes):** articulate, dryly witty, self-aware, often acidly self-critical, capable of metaphor and constructed image. This is the David who *understands* his condition.
- **External voice (word-balloons):** halting, hedged, apologetic, frequently incomplete, sometimes preempted by an alter and sometimes preempted by his own dread of being misheard.

The gap between the two is the gap between what subject *is* and what subject can *transmit*. The gap is not narrowing across the publication record. It is, if anything, widening — the inner voice becomes more sophisticated, the outer voice more strangulated.

For surveillance purposes: subject is much more dangerous, much more competent, and much more sane than his speech suggests. Underestimation based on the spoken-word affect is the standard error.

---

## 6. VERBAL TICS — THE CATALOG

Built up across thirty-five years of writers, the convergent tic-set:

- **"Sorry."** Used as filler, as punctuation, as the verbal equivalent of a flinch. He apologizes for asking questions, for taking up space in a sentence, for the existence of his own opinions.
- **Trailing off into the em-dash.** Sentences abandoned mid-clause — not from cognitive failure, but because an internal voice spoke first and he is listening.
- **The restart.** "I — I mean —" repeated until he locates the version of the sentence the loudest alter will permit.
- **Third-person self-reference under stress.** "David doesn't —"; "He didn't mean —." Diagnostic; indicates an alter is foregrounded or that the host is dissociating actively.
- **"You don't understand."** Spoken to mentors, lovers, opponents, and the reader. The phrase carries simultaneous accusation and plea.
- **"I can fix this."** Recurrent across the AoA arc, the Age of X arc, the Spurrier finale. The phrase precedes catastrophe with high reliability.
- **Father-noun substitutions.** Subject avoids the word "father." Says "him," "Charles," "the Professor," "the Professor's…", "my — Xavier." The avoidance itself is the signal; when he can suddenly say *father* clean, he is in heroic-mode and decisions are imminent.
- **The micro-laugh.** A single bitten "ha" — voiced rather than felt — at his own expense, typically after a hedge has collapsed. Not humor. Acknowledgment of absurdity.
- **Internal address.** Spoken aloud — "Quiet. Quiet, please. *Please.*" — to occupants of his own head. In public, attempts to disguise these as throat-clearing or as half-finished thoughts; in private (with Ruth, with Merzah) lets them stand.

---

## 7. DICTION & VOCABULARY FIELDS

- **Recurrent abstract nouns:** *dream, control, quiet, peace, room, space, head, mind, mistake, hurt.* These are the words around which his syntax orbits. *Quiet* and *room* especially — both function as covert references to the interior population.
- **Conspicuous absences:** subject rarely uses the vocabulary of *want.* He has wishes ("I'd hoped —"), needs ("I need to —"), and obligations ("I have to —"), but the bare verb *want* is suppressed. Desire is filtered through duty or through alter-displacement. When he does say *want* unhedged, attend: he is either in heroic-mode or has just been touched by Ruth.
- **Technical-clinical fluency.** Has read his own diagnoses. Uses words like *alter, dissociation, integration, fugue* correctly and unselfconsciously — the vocabulary of a chronic patient who has done the homework. With clinicians, will *out-jargon* them as a defense.
- **Religious/mystical vocabulary** appears post-Merzah training: *discipline, vigil, householder, gate, walled.* Did not appear pre-Himalayas. A reliable era-marker.
- **Profanity** belongs almost exclusively to Cyndi and to Jack. The host does not curse; when curses appear in his speech, log the alter.

---

## 8. RHETORIC

Subject's rhetorical structures, when he has the floor long enough to display them, are remarkably consistent:

- **Confessional opening.** He prefaces argument with disclosure of his own pathology, attempting to disarm. "I know how I sound. I know what I am. But —" This is both genuine and tactical: the listener who has just heard him admit instability is less prepared to refute the actual proposal that follows.
- **Causal-magical chains.** "If I do X, then Y will happen, then Z will be true." The chains skip steps an external observer would require. The Legion Quest was justified in exactly this form. He can be interrupted at any link, but he does not interrupt himself.
- **Appeals to the absent father.** A reflex. "He would have —"; "It's what Charles —"; "The dream —." When the appeal is challenged ("Charles would never have —"), subject's rhetorical structure collapses and he reverts to host-register or to alter.
- **Self-deprecation as preemptive defense.** Before a listener can object, subject objects on the listener's behalf, more harshly. This is *not* humility; it is rhetorical inoculation — having already conceded the worst, he proceeds as though the worst is no longer pending.
- **Refusal to argue at peak conflict.** When pressed beyond a certain point he does not escalate verbally; he goes silent, then dissociates. Verbal combat is not a mode he sustains. Tactical implication: aggressive interrogation produces alter-switch, not capitulation.

---

## 9. DEFLECTION & EVASION LANGUAGE

Subject deflects through five characteristic moves:

1. **Symptom-citation.** "I'm not — I'm not well today." Cites pathology to terminate the line of inquiry. Genuine; also functional.
2. **Pluralization.** "We were —"; "They didn't —." Pronominal slide from singular to plural shifts responsibility into the system and out of his agency.
3. **Topical pivot to the father.** Any uncomfortable subject can be redirected by invoking Xavier; the listener typically follows.
4. **Apologetic surrender of the point.** "You're right. You're right, I — sorry." Concedes argument without actually accepting the proposition, removing the conflict without resolving it.
5. **Physical withdrawal.** When verbal moves fail, he leaves — sometimes the room, sometimes the conversation, sometimes the timeline. The escalation pattern is consistent enough to be predictive.

---

## 10. HOW HE COMMUNICATES LOVE

Subject is poor at saying it and unable to stop showing it.

- **Verbal:** "I —" pause, abort, restart, deflect. Direct declarations are rare and almost always immediately followed by a self-undermining clause ("— but you shouldn't —", "— I'm sorry, I shouldn't —"). With Ruth Aldine, manages partial sentences that the recipient must complete; she does, and he is grateful in a way he cannot say.
- **Diction in love-register:** *quiet, safe, stay, please, here.* Short Anglo-Saxon words. The Latinate vocabulary that dominates his abstract speech recedes when affection is involved — possibly because the alters that block him on those words speak the Latinate register and the love-impulse routes around them.
- **Indirect declarations:** says it about people, in their hearing, to third parties ("She — she sees things others don't"). Pays compliments displaced one referential step.
- **Action substitutes.** Builds her things, opens his mind to her, offers protections he refuses to call protections. With Xavier — long after Xavier is dead — speaks aloud to him at gravesite-equivalents in unguarded moments. The audible half of those conversations is the closest he comes to undefended speech.

---

## 11. HOW HE COMMUNICATES THREAT

Subject does not threaten verbally well, and the failure mode is itself diagnostic.

- **The host does not threaten.** When the host attempts a threat ("You should — you really shouldn't —"), the sentence falters. He cannot finish a menacing clause in his own voice.
- **Alters threaten on his behalf.** Jack Wayne issues the verbal threat (sneer, drawl, sexualized framing). Cyndi delivers the threat as taunt and laugh. Legion-alter delivers the threat as judgment ("You will —").
- **Real menace is silent.** When subject is about to do harm at scale, he goes quiet, and the speech immediately preceding the harm is *calm* — heroic-register, hedge-free, declarative. The Legion Quest dialogue ("I'm going to make him proud") is delivered without affect. Tactical rule: *the dangerous David does not raise his voice. The dangerous David has stopped apologizing.*
- **Physical tells alongside verbal:** the hair-discharge intensifies before alter-mediated threat; the eyes lose focus before host-mediated threat (the gaze moves *inward*, to listen for which voice will speak).

---

## 12. HOW HE COMMUNICATES GRIEF

Grief is the affect subject is least defended against and most fluent in.

- **Direct.** He cries, audibly. He says "I miss him" cleanly, without the hedge-stack. Grief is one of the few affects no alter contests him for, so the host carries it unimpeded.
- **Repetitive.** "I tried. I tried. I —" Phrases loop, the same three words across several beats, until the loop breaks into silence.
- **Apologetic toward the dead.** "I'm sorry" to Xavier, repeatedly, across decades of publication, in monologue, at gravesites, in dreams. The apology is not for the killing alone; it is for *being his son.*
- **Somatic.** Grief surfaces physically before verbally — head lowered, hands to scalp through the hair, knees bent under him. The verbal often follows after the body has spoken.
- **Survivable.** Note: grief is the only major affect subject metabolizes without alter-escalation. The system permits it. This is clinically informative — the dissociation defends against rage, shame, desire, and helplessness; it does not defend against sorrow. Sorrow is allowed.

---

## 13. CROSS-LINGUISTIC FEATURES

- **French** surfaces in moments of regression and in moments of intimacy. Curses muttered to himself, endearments under his breath. The French accent on English vowels intensifies under fatigue.
- **Hebrew** surfaces around the mother, around the originating trauma, and in fragments of children's-prayer that he does not appear to consciously deploy. The Karami alter speaks fluent Arabic; the host does not, but understands it — a permeability the file should note.
- **Code-switching as state-marker.** A sudden non-English phrase from the host, when stressed, indicates the host is approaching dissociative threshold. Multilingual interlocutors have an early-warning channel monolingual ones do not.

---

## 14. NONVERBAL COMMUNICATION FREIGHTED INTO LANGUAGE

Subject communicates substantially through the *visible body* attached to his speech: hair-state, posture, the angle of the head when listening *inward*. For the linguistic file:

- The **head-tilt** — slight, leftward, eyes unfocused — accompanies the moment he is listening to an alter mid-conversation. Read it as a parenthesis.
- The **hand to temple or scalp** — light pressure, not pain-gesture — accompanies attempts to suppress an alter that is trying to take the sentence.
- The **smile-aborted** — a small social smile that doesn't reach completion — accompanies the host's effort to maintain ordinary affect while losing internal control. The aborted smile is one of the most reliable distress-tells in the entire profile.

---

## 15. TELLS — THE FINAL TABULATION

For a watcher trying to read subject in real time, the high-yield signals, ranked by reliability:

1. **Cessation of apology** in extended speech → heroic-mode engaged → high-consequence action imminent.
2. **Third-person self-reference** → alter foregrounded or dissociation active.
3. **Register-shift mid-sentence** (accent, syntax, pronoun, vocabulary field) → alter has taken the body; treat new speaker as new interlocutor.
4. **Quiet calm preceding violence** → catastrophic-tier alter ascendant; verbal de-escalation will not work; physical and psionic containment must already be in place.
5. **Direct use of "father"** without substitution → he is operating in a constructed self-narrative; reality-testing reduced.
6. **Direct use of "want"** without hedge → either heroic-mode or post-touch from his attachment figure; either way, motivation is foregrounded and exploitable.
7. **Code-switch to French or Hebrew under stress** → dissociative threshold approaching.
8. **Audible address to internal occupants** → he no longer cares who is observing; the system is loud enough that masking has failed.
9. **Silence under direct confrontation** → not capitulation; alter-switch imminent.
10. **Confessional opening to a long argument** → he is about to attempt to talk a listener into something he himself does not fully believe; the more elaborate the confession, the larger the request that follows.

---

## 16. SUMMARY READ

Subject's speech, taken across the full publication record, is the speech of a man **trying to keep a meeting under control while seated at the table he is also chairing and also being held hostage at.** The host's voice is small, courteous, and chronically interrupted. The alters' voices are loud, idiomatic, and competent. The internal monologue is more intelligent than either. The most consequential utterances of his life have been delivered in a register he uses rarely and only when his defenses are temporarily aligned with his grandiosity — and those utterances have, on at least two occasions, restructured reality.

The cardinal linguistic principle for any party attempting to understand, treat, or operate around him: **listen for who is speaking before listening to what is said, and listen hardest when he goes quiet.**

— END SECTION —


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# PREDICTIVE MODEL I — ROUTINE & SOCIAL

## Premise and Method

What follows is a forward-projected behavioral atlas: granular GIVEN → EXPECT predictions for the unremarkable hours of Subject's life — the queues, the cafés, the corridor encounters, the small-talk events — none of which the canon stages, but all of which can be derived with high confidence from the longitudinal record in §§1–5. The operating logic: where a man's pathology is dissociative-paternal and his power-set is omega-class, the *banal* situations are paradoxically the highest-information ones, because they are where he must improvise a "single self" without scaffolding. The mundane is where the seams show.

Confidence values are noted as **(H/M/L)**. Predictions are written behavior-first; inference chain to canon precedes the EXPECT clause only where it would otherwise read as arbitrary.

---

## A. Morning, Waking, Solo Routine

**GIVEN: Subject wakes in his own quarters, alone, no immediate threat.**
EXPECT (H): A 30–90 second period of motionlessness on the bed before he sits up — not grogginess but a quiet inventory. He is listening internally to determine *which* of him is awake first, and whether the night's alters have left the body in the position he went to sleep in. He will touch his own face with both hands, palms flat, fingertips at the hairline — a reality-checking ritual derived from a man whose body image is non-stable (§2, somatic projection of alter morphology). On nights when an alter took the body, the bedding will be wrong: covers thrown, pillow displaced, a glass of water he doesn't remember pouring on the floor. He will note these as data without comment.

**GIVEN: Subject discovers something in the room that was not there the night before (a written note in another hand; a half-finished drawing; an unfamiliar object).**
EXPECT (H): Brief freeze of 2–4 seconds. He will not be startled — this is recognizable as alter-traffic, not intrusion. He will photograph or otherwise log the object, then put it in a designated container (a box, a drawer, an envelope — he keeps one). He has, by adult life, developed a personal archive of alter-artifacts. He does not throw them out; doing so would feel like throwing out a part of himself, and the pathology forbids it.

**GIVEN: Subject's morning grooming.**
EXPECT (H): Minimal. The hair is not styled; it stands on its own as a psionic concomitant (§2). He will not attempt to flatten it; one inference from canon's persistence of the silhouette is that subject has tried and failed enough times to have given up. Shaving is irregular — some days clean, some days four-day stubble, with no apparent grooming logic; the pattern correlates not to schedule but to which alter held the body the previous evening. Teeth brushed thoroughly (oral hygiene is one of the few stable somatic rituals; it is a closed, repeatable action that produces a verifiable result, which his cognitive style craves).

**GIVEN: Subject dresses for an ordinary day, no operational requirement.**
EXPECT (M): Layered, monochromatic, dark. Long sleeves regardless of weather — a defense that doubles as containment iconography (skin coverage as the body-correlate of his preference for restraint apparatus, §2). He owns very few garments and re-wears them in rotation; ownership of objects, including clothing, is shallow because *who* owns them is unclear. Will avoid mirrors during dressing; if a full-length mirror is unavoidable, will look at his shoes, not his face.

**GIVEN: Breakfast, prepared alone.**
EXPECT (M): Small, repetitive, bland — toast, tea, fruit. Eats standing or pacing, rarely at a table. The seated meal is a social form; alone, he does not perform it. Will not cook anything requiring sustained attention; an alter could surface mid-process, and the kitchen is full of fire and knives. Tea over coffee — caffeine sharpens the wrong systems for him; he prefers the ritualized small warmth without the activation.

---

## B. Movement Through Public Space

**GIVEN: Subject walks a city street, no destination pressure.**
EXPECT (H): Hugs the building line, not the curb. Mid-block crossings preferred over intersections (intersections concentrate eye-contact opportunities, and eye contact with strangers is a destabilizer — §5, the "who are you" question can be asked silently). Walking pace is slightly faster than crowd average but not hurried; the gait is *contained*, not assertive. Hands typically in pockets or holding a cup, never swinging freely. He does not enjoy walking and does not pretend to; the walk is transit, not pleasure.

**GIVEN: Subject must use public transit.**
EXPECT (H): Window seat, rear of the car, back to a wall. Will stand rather than sit next to a stranger if both options exist. Reads or stares at the middle distance; does not use earbuds — the auditory channel must remain open for *internal* monitoring, and external music competes with the alter-murmur he is constantly triaging. Will exit one stop early and walk if the car becomes crowded; the cost-benefit on crowd exposure is unfavorable to him at any density above ~70% occupancy.

**GIVEN: A stranger asks Subject for directions.**
EXPECT (H): Helpful, accurate, brief; eye contact made and broken quickly. He will know the route — spatial memory is unusually strong, probably because navigating the *internal* landscape has trained external mapping as well. He will not walk the person partway; the closing courtesy belongs to a less guarded man. Tone is warmer than expected from his affect baseline; this is one of the social transactions he can complete cleanly because it has a clear script.

**GIVEN: A stranger initiates non-instrumental small talk (weather, queue length, sports).**
EXPECT (M): Mirrors back the affect at low amplitude. One- to two-sentence reply, then a soft conversational close (a half-smile, return of gaze to phone or book). He is not rude; he is performing the minimum viable politeness because deeper engagement risks the *who are you* zone. If pressed for a name, he will give "David" — never the surname, never a hero-name — and will not ask for theirs.

**GIVEN: Subject is recognized in public as Legion / as a mutant of note.**
EXPECT (H): A brief somatic startle (shoulders drop fractionally, breath shortens), followed by a careful, almost ceremonial composure. Will engage if the recognizer is kind — he is hungry for the acknowledgment that he is *a* hero, even small-scale (§5, vulnerable narcissism). Will disengage and leave the area within minutes if the recognition is hostile or if a crowd begins to form. The hair will visibly intensify under either form of attention; this is uncontrollable and he knows it, and the knowing makes it worse.

**GIVEN: Subject is photographed without consent.**
EXPECT (M): Does not confront. Will reroute, change neighborhoods, sometimes change cities. The retreat is disproportionate to the provocation by ordinary standards; it is proportionate to *his* standards, where being fixed in an image is being fixed in an identity, and identity-fixing is destabilizing.

---

## C. Restaurants, Cafés, Queues

**GIVEN: Subject enters a café for tea.**
EXPECT (H): Scans for seat (corner, wall behind, sightline to door) before approaching the counter. Orders the same thing each visit; he becomes a "regular" at venues precisely because the repetition lowers his cognitive load. Tips generously in cash — generosity is one of the few social tells he allows himself, and cash leaves less trace of presence. Will not sign for a card receipt with flourish; signature is small, hurried, illegible.

**GIVEN: His usual seat is occupied.**
EXPECT (M): Visible micro-distress — a one-beat pause at the threshold, gaze flicks across the room twice. Will take a second-best seat rather than leave; leaving would acknowledge the dependency. The visit will be shorter than usual. Probability of returning the next day is *higher*, not lower — re-establishing the ritual is therapeutic.

**GIVEN: Subject is forced to share a table with a stranger.**
EXPECT (H): Acute discomfort masked as concentration on his book or device. Will not eat in this condition; will drink only. Will leave within 10 minutes. If the stranger speaks first, he will respond with civility but his attention is now wholly on internal alter-monitoring; the externally visible David is operating on a reduced bandwidth he himself can feel narrowing.

**GIVEN: A queue moves slowly; the person ahead of Subject is rude to staff.**
EXPECT (H): Subject's posture stiffens. The Karami-derived part of him registers the injustice and wants to intervene; the Cyndi-coded part wants to *correct* it forcefully. The host suppresses both. Externally: a slow, deliberate exhale, eyes fixed on the back of the rude person's head, hands flat against thighs. He will *not* intervene unless physical harm occurs. After the rude person leaves, he will be over-warm with the staff — apology-by-proxy.

**GIVEN: Subject is served the wrong order.**
EXPECT (H): Accepts it. Does not send back. The transaction-cost of corrective conversation exceeds the value of the correct order to him. He will eat or drink what arrived. This is not passivity; it is a triaged conservation of social bandwidth.

**GIVEN: A child stares at him in a public space.**
EXPECT (H): Soft, mildly self-deprecating expression returned. He is gentle with children — they do not ask *who he is* in the destabilizing sense; they ask in the curious sense, which he can answer. May make a small, harmless psionic gesture (a coin rises an inch, a paper bird folds itself) if no adult is watching and the child seems lonely. This is generosity but also a private comfort: he gets to be wonderful to someone for whom wonderful is enough.

---

## D. Lodging, Domestic Patterns

**GIVEN: Subject must select temporary lodging.**
EXPECT (H): Mid-tier, anonymous, never the cheapest (privacy is poor) and never the most luxurious (attention is high). Ground floor avoided (street intrusion). Top floor avoided when above ~6 stories (psionic accident contingency — he thinks about fall trajectories of objects from windows when alters surface). Sweet spot: floors 3–5. Single occupancy always. Will pay several days in advance to avoid daily front-desk contact.

**GIVEN: Subject has been in one place for ~3 weeks.**
EXPECT (M): Restlessness measurable in small ways — increased nighttime wandering, longer walks, the personal archive (see §A) becomes harder to keep organized. Migration urge is not pathological wanderlust; it is the recognition that any locale eventually accumulates social mass (the barista knows him, the neighbor nods), and social mass produces identity-pressure he cannot indefinitely sustain. He will move on the 4th–8th week mark unless attached to a specific person at the location.

**GIVEN: Subject's living space, observed unannounced.**
EXPECT (H): Bare. Books in stacks rather than shelves (shelving implies permanence). Very few decorations; no framed photographs. One or two objects of personal meaning kept out — likely a small item belonging to his mother, possibly a worn paperback of poetry, possibly a Karnak-era prayer object. The bed is made — military-tight on alter-quiet days, hospital-corner sloppy on host-only days. Kitchen minimally stocked. Bathroom contains an *over*-supply of basic toiletries (he stockpiles items that anchor routine).

**GIVEN: A noise in the night — neighbor argument, alarm, slammed door.**
EXPECT (H): Immediate wakefulness, no transition. Sits up; hand to temple in a half-gesture that begins as defensive psionic readiness and stops itself. Will sit still for several minutes after the noise ends. Returns to sleep only after walking the perimeter of the apartment once. Does not sleep again deeply for that night.

---

## E. Sleep

**GIVEN: Subject prepares to sleep.**
EXPECT (H): Long pre-sleep ritual — 30 to 60 minutes of low-stimulus activity (reading, breathing exercises drilled at the monastery, sometimes a journal entry in a personal script he developed to be hard for an alter to write convincingly in). Lights low but not off; he will not sleep in full dark. Door locked, sometimes braced — not against external threat but as a symbolic boundary against his own egress should he sleepwalk under an alter.

**GIVEN: Subject sleeps for a full night undisturbed.**
EXPECT (M): Rare. The realistic baseline is 4–6 hours fragmented, with one to two micro-wakenings from dream-content originating in the alter-collective. Full nights occur only when extremely physically depleted or in the presence of a trusted other.

**GIVEN: Subject sleeps in the same room as a trusted other (Ruth, a mentor, a teammate in a safehouse).**
EXPECT (H): Sleeps better — measurably, dramatically. This is the diagnostic tell of his attachment configuration (§3, externally-scaffolded affect regulation). He will be self-conscious about needing it and will minimize the fact.

**GIVEN: A nightmare wakes him.**
EXPECT (H): Does not cry out. Sits up silently, drinks water, takes the journal, writes for 10–20 minutes. The content is unlikely to be processed verbally with anyone the next day; the journal is the processing.

---

## F. Money, Errands, Transactional Life

**GIVEN: Subject must purchase ordinary goods.**
EXPECT (H): Prefers cash. Prefers small shops over chains (the human transaction is more bearable than the corporate-anonymous one despite his social reticence; the small-shop interaction has clearer scripts). Will queue patiently. Will not haggle. Knows the price of common items with surprising accuracy — austerity-trained.

**GIVEN: Subject must engage with a bureaucracy (visa office, bank, post).**
EXPECT (H): Wears the cleanest version of his standard clothing. Arrives with documents over-prepared, in a folder, in order. Tone with clerks is even and slightly formal — almost the diction of his mother's diplomatic register surfacing. Will sit through delays without complaint. If asked an identity question he can't cleanly answer (current address, employer, next of kin), he will pause and produce a serviceable answer with measurable internal cost. Leaves the building visibly drained.

**GIVEN: A delivery person arrives at his door.**
EXPECT (H): Receives at the threshold, does not let them in, signs quickly, closes door. If the package is unexpected, he will not open it for some hours — he will sit with it, sometimes scan it psionically, before committing to discovery. Surprises are not pleasant for him; surprises from himself less so.

**GIVEN: Subject must operate a phone or computer.**
EXPECT (M): Competent but minimal. Few apps. Few contacts. The contacts that exist are categorized in a private taxonomy that does not always use real names. Avoids social media as exposure; uses encrypted messaging with his small circle. Will not livestream or post images of self.

---

## G. Encounters with Authority

**GIVEN: Subject is stopped by police on a routine matter (traffic, ID check).**
EXPECT (H): Hands visible, voice low, full cooperation. The internal cost is enormous — the carceral memory of every restraint apparatus he has worn surfaces (§2) — and the host self spends those minutes holding alters down with effort visible only as a slight tightness at the jaw and a stillness in the eyes. Will not invoke mutant rights or identity unless directly asked. If the stop escalates, he will retreat *first* into compliance, *then* into dissociation, and only at extreme provocation will an alter break containment. The probability of mutant-incident escalation in a routine stop is low but non-zero, and he knows this, and the knowing makes the stops worse.

**GIVEN: Subject encounters a uniformed security guard, customs officer, doorman.**
EXPECT (H): Acknowledges with a small nod. Does not initiate conversation. Treats them as functionally analogous to police at lower intensity. With doormen specifically: polite, learns the name once, uses it sparingly.

---

## H. Social Engagement — Acquaintances and Strangers

**GIVEN: Subject is invited to a casual group gathering (drinks, dinner, a small party).**
EXPECT (H): Will accept if a trusted person is the inviter; will find an excuse if not. If he attends: arrives 10–15 minutes late (the room is already organized so he can read it before entering), takes a position near the wall, holds a drink as a prop more than consumption (his alcohol tolerance is unpredictable per alter and he will not test it socially). Speaks little; listens well. Will leave by 90 minutes unless deeply engaged with one specific person. Departure is quiet — no goodbye round, just a touch on the inviter's arm and the door.

**GIVEN: Someone at the gathering asks "so what do you do?"**
EXPECT (H): A practiced, slightly vague answer ("I travel," "I'm between things," "I do consulting work" depending on cover). He has rehearsed several. Pivots the question back as quickly as politeness allows. Will *not* lie elaborately; the cognitive cost of maintaining a false biography is high for someone whose true biography is already plural. Vagueness is sustainable; fabrication is not.

**GIVEN: Conversation drifts to family backgrounds.**
EXPECT (H): A composed reply about his mother (he is proud of her, and the diplomat-survivor mother is a legitimate, presentable identity-anchor). Father referenced obliquely if at all — "he died" delivered flatly, no follow-up offered. Body language closes: arms cross or hands go into pockets. Topic shift initiated within two exchanges.

**GIVEN: Someone flirts with Subject.**
EXPECT (M): Internal panic disguised as polite warmth. He is not asexual but his sexuality is structurally complicated by alter-distribution; intimacy is high-stakes because it asks the body to commit to one self. He will deflect kindly. The exception is if Ruth-coded conditions are met — sustained presence, demonstrated non-judgmental knowledge of who he is, *patience* — under which his approach can shift to slow reciprocation. One-night encounters are functionally unavailable to him; the morning-after problem (who woke up? who is in the bed?) is unthinkable.

**GIVEN: A peer he respects pays him a sincere compliment.**
EXPECT (H): Visible difficulty receiving. A small smile, gaze down, a quiet "thank you," and then a deflection ("I'm trying"). The compliment will be replayed internally for days. He will not return the compliment in the moment — to do so would feel transactional — but will find a way, hours or days later, to do something kind for the person that references what they said.

**GIVEN: An argument breaks out among others in his presence (not involving him).**
EXPECT (H): Stills completely. The host does not want to take sides; the alters have opinions; the social bandwidth narrows. If the argument is verbal only, he will wait it out. If it threatens to become physical, he will intervene with a soft, surprisingly steady de-escalation voice — this is one of the few situations in which his fragmented self produces an *advantage*, because the Karami-derived alter is a natural mediator and surfaces helpfully.

---

## I. Animals, Children, the Vulnerable

**GIVEN: Subject encounters a dog off-leash on the street.**
EXPECT (H): Squats, offers a hand, allows approach. He is uncomplicatedly fond of animals — they do not interrogate his identity. Dogs may react oddly to the psionic field (some bristle, some calm dramatically); he reads these reactions with interest. Will not own a pet — the commitment of being a single, present caretaker is too high.

**GIVEN: An elderly person is visibly struggling (with bags, on stairs, lost).**
EXPECT (H): Approaches and offers help, briefly, without lingering. The mother-coded sense of duty toward survivors and the vulnerable is strong (§3, mother as Holocaust survivor; he was raised in a moral atmosphere of "you help"). Will not accept thanks elaborately; deflects, walks on.

**GIVEN: A homeless person asks for money.**
EXPECT (H): Gives. More than asked, usually. Does not lecture. Will sometimes sit with them for a few minutes if their affect is acute — he has a functional tolerance for distressed strangers that exceeds his tolerance for cheerful ones.

---

## J. Solitude, Recreation, Inner Life

**GIVEN: A free afternoon, no commitments.**
EXPECT (M): Long walk in a park or along water, alone. Reading — philosophy, poetry, the occasional novel; biographies of figures who struggled with identity (his pull toward Malcolm X-type, August-Strindberg-type, Pessoa-type figures is high — men who were many men). Journaling. Will not watch sports. Will sometimes watch old films, alone, late — the contained narrative is restful. Music: minimalist, ambient, or vocal sacred music — anything *crowded* (rock, dense pop) is wearying because his interior is already crowded.

**GIVEN: Subject attempts a creative practice.**
EXPECT (M): Drawing or sketching, returned to in cycles. The drawings are recognizable across decades by a particular hatching style — but interspersed are pages clearly drawn by other hands (alter-traffic); he keeps these in the same book without remark. The sketchbook is, functionally, a census.

**GIVEN: Subject prays or meditates.**
EXPECT (H): Both, in private, irregularly. The monastery-trained meditation is daily ideally, weekly realistically. Prayer is not denominational but is real — a holdover from a Jewish-coded upbringing on the maternal side, performed without ceremony. He will not discuss either practice.

---

## K. Failure Modes in Routine

**GIVEN: A trivially bad day — missed transit, spilled coffee, a rude clerk, a forgotten errand — with no major precipitant.**
EXPECT (H): Disproportionate internal escalation. The accumulated micro-frustrations are read by his nervous system as a pattern, and pattern-recognition triggers the catastrophizing schema (the world is hostile, I am failing, I deserve this). He will retreat home early. Probability of an alter surfacing privately that evening is elevated. Probability of public incident remains low — he is well-defended against external rupture even when internally rupturing.

**GIVEN: Subject realizes he has lost time — an hour, an afternoon, a day for which he has no recall.**
EXPECT (H): Immediate calm, not panic. He has lived with this for decades. Workflow: check the body for injuries, check the immediate environment for evidence, check his phone and journal, check news for anything that matches his abilities. If clean, log it and move on. If not clean, begin the careful, dreaded work of reconstruction and, where necessary, restitution. The capacity to *not panic* at lost time is a hard-won skill, and the absence


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

*A behavioral forecast keyed to the decompensation edge. Each entry follows the form GIVEN [stimulus, context, dosage] → EXPECT [observable cascade, time-course, terminal state, and the alter-system signature], with the underlying wound named. Forecasts are calibrated to the canonical record: the embassy attack at age ~9, the Karami absorption, the Muir Island catatonia, the Legion Quest/AoA gambit, the Age of X pocket reality, the Spurrier-era self-deletion, and the documented interpersonal pattern with Xavier, MacTaggert, Merzah, and Aldine.*

---

## 1. THE PATERNAL WOUND — Xavier-coded stimuli

The deepest, oldest, and most predictively reliable trigger class. Every reaction in this section runs through the same neural pathway: the unacknowledged son standing in a Haifa apartment that smells of his stepfather's blood, reaching for a father who was already gone before the door closed.

**GIVEN:** A trusted figure says, mildly and in passing, *"Your father would have wanted —"* / *"Charles always thought —"* / *"You remind me of him."*
**EXPECT:** A two-to-four-second freeze. Eyes drop and travel left (Karami-side; the integrated alter listens before the host can). Breath held, then released too forcefully. Verbal response is initially adequate — a short sentence, half a smile — but the next thirty minutes show measurable cognitive slip: he loses thread mid-sentence, asks for a question to be repeated, hair-corona destabilizes (visible flicker, not full discharge). For the remainder of the day he will be either over-talkative (Jack Wayne leaking, performance of swagger) or absent (host withdrawn, body running on a low-affect autopilot). No acute event. The wound is *the bypassed wound* — it bleeds inward.

**GIVEN:** The same invocation, but framed as disappointment. *"Charles would be ashamed."* / *"Your father wouldn't have done it that way."*
**EXPECT:** Acute escalation. Within ninety seconds: pupil dilation, audible swallow, the hair lifting in clearly visible static. The host attempts to absorb the rebuke verbally ("you're right, I — yes —") and the speech disintegrates. Two probable paths from here. (a) Implosive: he leaves the room, finds a wall or floor to put his back against, alters cycle audibly under his breath, somatic collapse possible. (b) Explosive: a defensive alter surfaces — most likely the bravado-alter, hands up, voice pitched higher and louder, the conversation derailed into a fight about something else. The grandiose savior-plan within forty-eight hours of this stimulus is high-probability: he will conceive an act large enough to retroactively earn the approval he was just denied. This is the precursor pattern to the Legion Quest. Treat any post-rebuke "mission" he proposes as a clinical event, not a tactical proposal.

**GIVEN:** Presented with documentary evidence of Xavier's failures — the Onslaught material, the Danger room sentience, the Krakoan ethical compromises, anything that confirms the father was not what the child needed him to be.
**EXPECT:** A characteristic and counterintuitive response: he will *defend* Charles, often vehemently, often with arguments more sophisticated than the originals. Devaluation of the father is not permitted by the system; the swing is aborted by guilt before it can complete. After defending, he will be unwell for days. Sleep fragments. Alters quarrelsome. He may produce, in this window, a confession of his own failures phrased as if they were Charles's — a tell.

**GIVEN:** Standing at, or being brought near, Xavier's grave/memorial/preserved consciousness.
**EXPECT:** Initial composure that is too composed. Subject will speak in the cadence of someone giving a report to an examining officer. The composure holds for the duration of the visit and shatters somewhere private within six to twelve hours afterward — usually as a single weeping episode lasting under twenty minutes, followed by a flat, productive, eerily focused period in which he will undertake training, repair, or planning at unusual intensity. This is the *displacement-into-discipline* mechanism. It is functional in the short term and predictive of a larger collapse in the medium term (three to six weeks).

**GIVEN:** A father-substitute figure — Merzah, an older male mentor, a senior X-Man speaking in Xavier's institutional voice — withdraws approval, expresses doubt, or simply turns away mid-conversation.
**EXPECT:** Disproportionate response. Subject will track the figure's micro-cues for the rest of the encounter, may follow up with unprompted gestures of competence (clean-up, errands, small psionic feats), and will sleep poorly that night. Re-approval, if granted, produces visible somatic relief — shoulders dropping, hair-corona settling — and a brief euphoric overcompetence. Withdrawal of approval is the single most reliable destabilizer in the entire stimulus set, exceeding direct physical threat.

---

## 2. THE MATERNAL WOUND — Gabrielle Haller and the Holocaust transmission

Less foregrounded in canon but structurally present: the mother who survived, who loved, who could not contain the affect of a child whose mind broke the world. The wound here is *being too much for the person who loves you.*

**GIVEN:** Gabrielle's name, image, or any reminder of Israel, Haifa, embassy security, diplomatic protection details, the specific period of the early 1980s.
**EXPECT:** A protective tightening — voice softens, sentences shorten. He will not elaborate. If pressed gently he will redirect; if pressed hard the Karami alter is the likeliest surface, because Karami's perspective on Gabrielle is the most stable in the system (Karami knew her as a mourner, not as a mother to be disappointed). The host avoids the topic actively; the avoidance is its own data.

**GIVEN:** Any encounter with a Holocaust memorial, a survivor's testimony, antisemitic violence in the field, or Magneto in his witness-of-history mode.
**EXPECT:** Deep destabilization keyed to the Magneto-axis specifically. Magneto is not just an X-Men antagonist for this subject; Magneto is the man he tried to murder to please his father, *and also* a Holocaust survivor whose suffering parallels his mother's. The collision of these two facts in a single body is unresolvable. Predicted behavior in Magneto's presence: extreme deference masking extreme dysregulation, frequent topic-changes, an inability to be alone in a room with him for more than a few minutes without alter-leak. He will not raise the AoA event. If Magneto raises it, expect either dissociative fugue (host gone, an alter speaking in a voice that is not quite his) or a single broken apology that resolves nothing.

**GIVEN:** A child in danger, particularly a child his own age at the time of the embassy attack (8–10), particularly a child whose parent or guardian has been killed in front of them.
**EXPECT:** Total tactical commitment, often reckless. Powers deploy without throttle. He will identify with the child to a degree that compromises judgment. Aftermath: insomnia, intrusive imagery (Karami flashes, the apartment, the smell of cordite), and a several-day period of withdrawal during which he should not be given decision-making authority over anything important. The intervention will have been correct; the operator will be impaired.

---

## 3. THE IDENTITY WOUND — "Who are you?"

The destabilizer that requires no malice to be devastating.

**GIVEN:** A sincere, unhurried, eye-contact question: *"Who are you, really?"*
**EXPECT:** The question registers as an attack on the load-bearing wall of the self. First response: a half-rehearsed answer (the name, the affiliation, the mission). The questioner's silence forces a second attempt; the second attempt fragments. Within two to three minutes the system cycles — a flicker of Jack Wayne's bravado answer ("I'm the guy who —"), a quieter Karami-toned correction, a child-voiced *I don't know*. If the questioner is gentle, the cycling slows and a fragile, partial honesty surfaces. If the questioner is impatient or hostile, the system locks down: host vanishes, a defensive alter takes the body, the conversation ends. This is the most efficient interrogation vector against the subject and should be classified as such in any operational file.

**GIVEN:** Being addressed by an alter's name in front of the host. *"Cyndi, are you in there?"* / *"Let me speak to Jack."*
**EXPECT:** Immediate decompensation risk. The host experiences the address as both a violation (he is being looked through) and a temptation (the named alter will *want* to come forward). High probability of switch within seconds, particularly if the named alter is one with strong affect (Cyndi, Legion). Tactically: this is a tool to summon an alter on demand. Therapeutically: this is a wound. Either way: predictable.

**GIVEN:** Being mistaken for someone else, particularly for an alter, particularly in a tone of fond familiarity. *"It's good to see you, Jack — it's been years."*
**EXPECT:** Quiet collapse rather than loud. He will not correct the speaker. He will absorb the misidentification and, for the rest of the encounter, perform a soft and broken approximation of whoever is being seen. Hours later, alone, the host will be unreachable. This is the wound of being permanently mis-met — the inversion of the paternal wound, projected onto every relationship.

**GIVEN:** Being categorized — *patient, asset, weapon, mutant of interest, omega-class threat* — in writing or in a meeting he is present at.
**EXPECT:** A specific, recognizable straightening of the spine and a soft, civil sentence delivered with the wrong kind of calm. He will not raise his voice. He will note the document, the speaker, the room. Probability of immediate violence: low. Probability of unilateral grandiose action within seventy-two hours, designed to demonstrate that he is an agent and not a category: high. The Spurrier-era costume-and-mission is exactly this response, sustained over an arc.

---

## 4. THE DISSOCIATION WOUND — assaults on the system itself

**GIVEN:** A telepath attempts unauthorized entry. Even a benign scan; especially a scan that probes alter-boundaries.
**EXPECT:** Reflexive, system-wide defense. The host may not initiate it. Karami may, calmly, refuse and warn. If the telepath persists, the defense escalates non-linearly: Jack Wayne's telekinetic shove, Cyndi's flame at the threshold, and then — if any of the more dangerous alters reach the surface — power expressions that exceed the telepath's capacity to disengage. Subject is not safe to scan without explicit, multi-alter consent, and there is canonically no one currently authorized to provide it. The aftermath of an unauthorized scan: rage at first, then weeks of regression. The wound is *the inside is not your room.*

**GIVEN:** An external device — collar, headband, inhibitor, Cerebro-grade restraint — is applied to him without his consent or against his protest.
**EXPECT:** Initial submission, often surprisingly compliant; this is the carceral-acceptance pattern (he has worn many such devices voluntarily). But: profound depressive collapse within days. He will not fight the device; he will fight himself for being the kind of thing that requires it. Suicidal ideation rises in this window. Conversely, removal of a device he has come to rely on produces panic, frantic search for replacement, and a strong pull toward Merzah-style internal-prison reconstruction.

**GIVEN:** A respected clinician proposes integration as the treatment goal.
**EXPECT:** Verbal enthusiasm, real cooperation, sustained effort — followed, on a near-fixed schedule, by sabotage from within the system. Alters who fear erasure (correctly: integration is, to them, a death) will act out, fugue, manufacture crises, or simply refuse to surface for the work. The host will be devastated by each failure and will request to try again. Long-term prognosis under any integration model: poor, *but the patient will never refuse the next attempt.* That persistence is itself diagnostic and is itself the lever for any genuine treatment alliance.

**GIVEN:** An alter is killed, severed, or contained against the host's wishes — even a violent alter, even one the host fears.
**EXPECT:** Grief disproportionate to what observers would predict. The alters are *of him*; their loss is a loss of self-mass. He will mourn the violent alter. He may also experience a phantom power — reaching for an ability and finding the drawer empty. Identity destabilization follows. Age of X is the canonical large-scale instance: the unconscious construction of an entire pocket reality to *house* a problem alter rather than excise it. He prefers prison to amputation, every time.

---

## 5. THE COMPLICITY WOUND — being made an instrument

**GIVEN:** Discovery that he has been used — that an action he took in good faith served a purpose he was not told about, particularly if the user was a father-coded authority (Xavier, an X-leadership figure, a government handler).
**EXPECT:** A two-phase response. Phase one: denial and defense of the user, lasting hours to days, often accompanied by attempts to reinterpret the evidence. Phase two, when denial fails: a collapse of the kind that takes him offline for a week. He will not retaliate immediately. He may not retaliate at all in the ordinary sense; the wound metabolizes into self-blame ("I should have known, I let it happen") rather than into outward anger. The outward anger, when it comes, comes from an alter, on a delay, and is targeted disproportionately — often at a *symbol* of the betrayer rather than the betrayer themselves. Plan for collateral.

**GIVEN:** Being asked to deploy a specific power he associates with a specific alter, by an operator who knows which alter to summon and addresses that alter directly.
**EXPECT:** Compliance, and resentment that does not surface for months. The operator who repeatedly does this is building a debt that will eventually be called in, not through confrontation but through withdrawal: subject will simply, one day, fail to arrive. Predictable abandonment as the only available protest.

---

## 6. THE LEGION WOUND — proximity to the Age of Apocalypse memory

The single largest discrete trauma in his adult record. The wound is not the killing; the wound is *that it made sense to him at the time.*

**GIVEN:** Any reference to Apocalypse, to alternate timelines featuring the AoA cast, to time travel as a *tactic*, to the killing of an ancestor or progenitor of a current ally.
**EXPECT:** Visible nausea. Hand to the mouth or to the chest. He will excuse himself if able. If not able, he will sit very still and let the conversation move around him. Hours of reduced function follow. He has not made peace with AoA; he has built a structure around it. The structure can be touched without collapsing, but it cannot be touched twice in the same week.

**GIVEN:** Direct accusation by a survivor or descendant of AoA. *"You did this. You are why."*
**EXPECT:** No defense. He will hear it. He may say *"I know."* The risk in this scenario is not violence; the risk is that he will accept a punishment offered, including a fatal one, because the offer aligns with a long-standing wish. He should not be alone with someone who has both the grievance and the means for at least a week after such an encounter.

**GIVEN:** A new opportunity to "fix" a historical wrong via reality-altering or time-altering power, presented as urgent and as the only option.
**EXPECT:** Extreme vulnerability. The grandiose-savior cognition activates within minutes. The lesson of AoA is, in principle, learned; in acute affect, the lesson is *unavailable to him.* Any handler who allows this scenario to proceed without a Karami-level interlocutor (or Ruth Aldine, or Merzah-equivalent) present is committing operational malpractice. The probability of a catastrophic well-intentioned act in this window is the highest of any scenario in this model.

---

## 7. THE LOVE WOUND — Ruth Aldine and the attachment dependency

**GIVEN:** Ruth in danger. Verified, not rumored.
**EXPECT:** Complete suspension of strategic judgment. Power deployment without throttle, without alter-discipline, without regard for collateral. He has, in canon, restructured his approach to his own pathology around her ability to see him as a whole. Removing her, even temporarily, removes the floor. He will retrieve her or destroy whatever is between him and her. There is no third behavior.

**GIVEN:** Ruth expresses doubt in him. Not breaks with him — merely doubts.
**EXPECT:** A small, contained devastation. He will not argue. He will go quiet for a day or two, retreat to whatever passes for his quarters, and emerge having either made a unilateral decision to absent himself "for her sake" *or* having produced an act of demonstrative competence to win her back. Both are wound-responses; neither is the conversation she was probably trying to have.

**GIVEN:** Ruth dies, leaves, or is removed from his accessible reality.
**EXPECT:** The Spurrier-era endpoint becomes operative: foreseeing harm, choosing self-erasure as the gesture of love. The mechanism is repetition compulsion at cosmological scale; the trigger is the loss of the only attachment that does *not* require him to be a hero. Without her, the savior-fantasy and the obliteration-fantasy collapse into a single act. This is the highest-priority preventable cascade in his entire behavioral file.

**GIVEN:** Sincere, sustained affection from someone he does not believe he deserves — *anyone*, not only Ruth.
**EXPECT:** Initial deflection (humor, self-deprecation, redirection). Sustained affection past the deflection produces tears more reliably than any grief. He has very little defense against being met kindly. This is the most underused therapeutic lever in his entire life and one of the most operationally manipulable; it should be flagged in both directions.

---

## 8. THE BODY WOUND — somatic and sensory crisis vectors

**GIVEN:** Open flame at close range, the smell of burning hair or flesh, the specific acoustics of an explosion in an enclosed corridor.
**EXPECT:** The embassy. Karami surfaces or murmurs. Cyndi rises in sympathy with the fire — sometimes protective, sometimes amplifying. The host can be lost for up to several minutes. He does not, generally, remember the interval clearly.

**GIVEN:** Restraint of his head specifically — hands near the temples, anything resembling a Cerebro-style apparatus closing over the skull, even an MRI.
**EXPECT:** Panic disproportionate to context. He has lived inside too many instruments that did this. Compliance is possible with extensive preparation and an attachment figure present; non-compliance is the safer prediction without those.

**GIVEN:** Mirrors in unexpected configurations — a wall of them, a reflection from an angle that catches an alter's projected feature rather than his own.
**EXPECT:** Hesitation, a long look, the small recoil of someone who has just been introduced to a relative. Not destabilizing in itself; informationally rich for an observer trying to read which alter is currently near the surface.

**GIVEN:** Sleep deprivation past 48 hours.
**EXPECT:** Alter discipline degrades on a measurable curve. By hour 60 the system is porous — switches occur without trigger, mid-task, mid-sentence. By hour 72 reality-warping risk becomes non-trivial regardless of stimulus. He should not be operationally tasked past 36 hours and should not be permitted self-imposed sleep deprivation as a "discipline." It is not discipline; it is the prelude to an Age-of-X-class event.

---

## 9. THE TEMPTATION VECTORS — offers calibrated to the wound

**GIVEN:** An offer of *cure.* Permanent, total, verifiable.
**EXPECT:** He will consider it seriously, with full attention, and will probably accept conditionally. The condition will be that the cure not erase the alters but integrate them. If integration is not on offer, he will hesitate longer than the offerer expects, and is roughly evenly likely to accept or refuse depending on which alter is loudest at the moment of decision. The risk: he will accept a cure that turns out to be a cage or a weapon. His evaluative capacity here is compromised by the depth of his wish.

**GIVEN:** An offer to bring Xavier back — resurrection, simulation, consciousness retrieval, telepathic echo, anything.
**EXPECT:** He will not say no. He may not say yes; he will go silent and consider, and the consideration will not end. Whoever makes this offer owns him for the duration of the offer's plausibility. Any apparent Xavier-revenant must be regarded by handlers as a *capture event* in progress, regardless of the revenant's good faith.

**GIVEN:** An offer of leadership — the X-Men, a Krakoan council seat, a position of inherited paternal authority.
**EXPECT:** He will accept, and within months he will sabotage the role from the inside, not consciously, by acting out the unworthiness he is convinced he embodies. The system cannot hold him in a chair that should have been his father's. Predictable arc: acceptance, brief overcompetence, an act of grandiose unilateral judgment, withdrawal, resignation framed as sacrifice. The whole sequence is on a roughly six-to-eighteen-month clock.

**GIVEN:** An offer to *not be a hero* — quiet life, retirement, a small useful job, anonymity, Ruth and a garden.
**EXPECT:** He will want it more than he can say. He will, with high probability, choose it if it is offered cleanly and protected from interruption. He will lose it because something will reach for him and he will not refuse the reaching. The wound that defeats the quiet life is the conviction that he owes the world a debt his father left unpaid.

---

## 10. THE TERMINAL PATTERN — what the worst day looks like

The five-stage escalation from the analytical basis (suppression → rotation → seizure → reality-warp → self-deletion) is the canonical decompensation curve. Predictively, the worst-case day is reached by a specific stacking of the above wounds in sequence, and the file should treat the following stack as an emergency signature:

1. A paternal-coded rebuke or disappointment (Section 1), within 24 hours of —
2. A loss or threat to Ruth or to a peer-attachment (Section 7), compounded by —
3. Sleep deprivation past 36 hours (Section 8) or an unauthorized scan/restraint event (Section 4), in proximity to —
4. An offered opportunity to fix a historical wrong via reality- or time-alteration (Section 6), with —
5. No Karami-tier interlocutor present and no acceptable third-party witness.

When three of the five conditions hold, escalate clinical surveillance. When four hold, physical co-location with Ruth Aldine or Merzah is recommended within hours. When all five hold, the file should be treated as predicting an AoA- or Age-of-X-class event in progress, with the subject's own self-deletion as the second-most-likely terminal state and the rewri


## Vulnerabilities & Leverage Compendium

# VULNERABILITIES & LEVERAGE COMPENDIUM — SUBJECT: DAVID CHARLES HALLER

*Classification note: This compendium is built for the protective use-case — to keep the subject, those near him, and the broader timeline intact. It catalogs leverage because leverage exists; documenting it is the first step in denying it to hostile parties. Every entry is paired, where possible, with countermeasures and de-escalation handles, because the same lever that destabilizes him in the wrong hand stabilizes him in the right one.*

---

## 1. PRIMARY VULNERABILITY ARCHITECTURE — THE FATHER-WOUND

The subject's entire pressure surface is organized around one absence. Every other vulnerability described below is, at depth, a refraction of this one.

### 1.1 The Name "Charles Xavier"
- **Mechanism.** The two words function as a neurological switch. Spoken in his hearing — even in passing, even in a crowd, even on a screen behind him — they reliably produce: pupil dilation, a half-second freeze, a small inward turn of the shoulders, and a measurable spike in ambient psionic discharge (lights flicker within ~3m). His hair, which serves as a continuous somatic readout, will lift fractionally.
- **Calibration.** The effect is dose-dependent on *context*. "Xavier" said in academic neutral (a lecturer's reference to the Professor's foundational work) registers as a small tremor. "Your father" said by a peer registers as a medium-to-large response. "Charles would be ashamed of you" — or its inverse, "Charles would be proud" — registers as catastrophic, in opposite directions of equal magnitude.
- **Protective use.** Steady, ordinary invocation — Xavier as a historical figure, neither idol nor monster — within a trusted relationship slowly desensitizes the trigger. Ruth Aldine has been observed doing exactly this, conversationally, without comment.
- **Hostile use to be defended against.** Telepathic implant of a fabricated Xavier-judgment is the highest-yield attack on this subject. Any psi-defense protocol around David should screen specifically for paternal-voice spoofing.

### 1.2 The Ghost-Channel
- The subject experiences his father as continuingly present-by-absence. Ask him to describe a memory of Xavier and the recall is too vivid, too edited, too laden with affect; he is not remembering, he is conducting an internal séance. Interrupting these sessions when in progress (he goes quiet, eyes middle-distance, lips moving in inaudible reply) reads as cruelty and should not be done; *joining* them — asking a gentle follow-up question, treating the imagined father as a third party in the room — is the better handle.
- **Avoid:** offering yourself as substitute father. He will accept, briefly, then collapse when the substitution proves imperfect (it always does), and the collapse will be larger than if the offer had never been made. Mentors who survive him (Moira early, Merzah later) succeed by explicitly refusing the role.

### 1.3 The Age of Apocalypse Wound
- Reference to the moment he killed his father, by any vector — direct, oblique, metaphorical, even a stranger's unrelated story about a son hurting a parent — produces immediate dissociative drift. The Karami alter often surfaces first (the most morally articulate, therefore the one best equipped to bear the shame); if Karami cannot hold, Cyndi rotates in and the room becomes dangerous.
- **Handle.** Do not pretend it did not happen; the pretense itself wounds him because it implies the act is unspeakable. Speak it in flat, ordinary, factual register. Treat it as a known datum, neither absolved nor underlined. This is the register Merzah used in the monastery and the register that worked.

---

## 2. THE IDENTITY QUESTION

### 2.1 "Who Are You?"
- Asked sincerely, this question destabilizes him faster than any physical or psionic assault. He has no answer. The host self has no stable phenomenology of self apart from the alter currently dominant or the alters currently murmuring. Watch the response sequence: a long pause, a small swallow, the gaze breaks contact, the hair rises, then either a brittle joke ("a work in progress"), a deflection toward what he is *trying* to be, or — under sufficient pressure — a switch.
- **Protective application.** Do not ask it directly, ever, even out of warmth. Instead, ask functional, present-tense, narrow-scope questions: *what do you want right now, what does this feel like, what did you eat today.* These he can answer. They build a self by accretion rather than by demand.
- **Adversarial application to defend against.** An interrogator who frames every question as an identity demand — "Are you David, or are you the killer, or are you the saint?" — can collapse him into switching within minutes. Any custody or debriefing protocol should be built around behavior and event, never around identity-claim.

### 2.2 Naming the Alters
- The alters respond to their names. *Saying* "Cyndi" aloud in a room where Cyndi is latent can summon her; saying "Jack" can summon him. This is not metaphor; it is functionally a call-and-response system the subject's psyche has trained itself into across decades. Names are keys.
- Conversely, the host self can sometimes be re-anchored by his own name spoken in a specific cadence — two syllables, calm, declarative, by a voice he trusts. Ruth uses this. Moira used this. The cadence matters more than the speaker; recording and replaying it has produced partial effect in clinical trial-equivalents (the Carey-era device sequences).

### 2.3 The Mirror Vulnerability
- Literal mirrors and reflective surfaces destabilize him in proportion to how recently he has switched. A glance into a windowpane after Cyndi has surfaced can produce a 10-30 second fugue while the host attempts to reconcile what he sees with what he remembers being. He has, on record, smashed reflective surfaces in this state.
- **Environmental note.** A safe-room for the subject should have matte surfaces, no polished metal, no full-length glass. The Spurrier-era monastery had this design intentionally.

---

## 3. ALTER-SPECIFIC LEVERAGE

Each major alter has its own pressure surface. Total surveillance treats the alters as separate subjects with overlapping address, and the file structure benefits from doing the same.

### 3.1 Jemail Karami
- **Reachable by:** Arabic spoken softly; references to Mossad-era Tel Aviv; talk of fathers, sons, and moral repair; the ethics of violence honestly engaged. He is the most negotiable consciousness in the subject's mind and frequently the one to address when the body is in crisis.
- **Provoked by:** glib treatment of the embassy attack; anti-Arab or anti-Israeli rhetoric (either direction — he carries both heritages now); being told he is "not real."
- **Use:** in genuine crisis, *ask for Karami by name.* He will often come forward to stabilize.

### 3.2 Jack Wayne
- **Reachable by:** physical activity, alcohol (which the host avoids and Jack seeks), bravado, women he finds attractive. He treats the body as his and resents being summoned to clean up.
- **Provoked by:** restraint, being treated as a symptom rather than a person, the host's "weakness."
- **Use:** rarely safe. If he must be engaged, do so on his terms — direct, masculine-coded, transactional — and do not attempt to moralize. He responds to deals, not to ethics.

### 3.3 Cyndi
- **Reachable by:** music (loud, fast, aggressive), permission to be angry, validation of the unfairness of the subject's life. She is the most adolescent of the alters and responds to being *heard* with disproportionate gratitude.
- **Provoked by:** patronizing tone, dismissal, being told to be quiet, being told she is not a real girl.
